601 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Ervin


No. B099627.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


53 Cal. App. 4th 1323; 62 Cal. Rptr. 2d 231; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 247; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2405; 97 Daily Journal DAR 4340



March 28, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied June 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3593.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. YA024953. John P. Shook, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County, California, which convicted him of violations of Cal. Penal Code §§ 211, 212.5(b) for robbery of a person immediately after the victim used an automated teller machine and while he was in the vicinity of the machine.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of robbing a victim who had just used an automated teller machine (ATM), in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 211, 212.5(b). The court held that §212.5b was not unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the phrases "in the vicinity of an automated teller machine" and "immediately after" provided sufficiently definite notice that no reasonable person could misunderstand their meaning. Both phrases had common dictionary meanings, their usual definitions were easily understood, and they gave sufficient warning to defendant that robbing someone who just used an ATM was first degree robbery. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to support appellant's conviction because defendant's ignorance of his victim's ATM use did not negate criminal intent. The court found that § 211 defined the crime and § 212.5b merely prescribed a greater punishment if ATM use was involved. The court held that, if knowledge were required, a police officer's testimony that he saw defendant's getaway car parked near the bank provided sufficient evidence that defendant was waiting for someone to use the ATM in order to rob him.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for robbery of a person who had just used an ATM. The statute providing for increased punishment when ATM use was involved was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendant's ignorance of his victim's ATM use did not negate intent because ATM use only increased the gravity of the offense. Evidence that the getaway car was parked at the bank was sufficient to show intent to rob someone after they used the ATM.

 

602 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Thomas v. City of E. Palo Alto


No. A073656.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


53 Cal. App. 4th 1084; 62 Cal. Rptr. 2d 185; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 221; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2239; 97 Daily Journal DAR 4027



March 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 17, 1997. Opinion Modified April 22, 1997. Review Denied June 25, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3832.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County. San Mateo Superior Court No. 388738. Hon. Clarence B. Knight Hon. James L. Browning, Jr.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which ruled in favor of plaintiff taxpayers in plaintiffs' cause of action to obtain tax refunds for the imposition of a parcel tax by defendant. Plaintiffs argued the parcel tax violated Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 1.


OVERVIEW: After defendant city discovered a shortfall in revenue, they took action to impose a new parcel tax on all real property owners. Plaintiff taxpayers made administrative claims for tax refunds to defendant, which defendant declined to grant. Plaintiffs then brought a cause of action to obtain refunds for the imposition of the parcel tax. The trial court held in favor of plaintiffs. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed judgment for plaintiffs because the trial court had correctly ruled that defendant had unconstitutionally imposed and collected a property tax not apportioned according to value, as was required by Cal. Const. art. XIII, § 1. The court found that the tax was not an excise tax because it simply taxed property owners for the mere ownership of property, and was not imposed as a valid excise tax would be on any of the incidents of ownership, such as sale, transfer, rental, and special use of certain city services. The court held that those persons who had been unconstitutionally required to pay this tax could sue in a class action for the refunds they were entitled, where each plaintiff had filed a valid individual administrative claim for a tax refund from defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of plaintiff taxpayers because the parcel tax imposed by defendant city was not a proper excise tax, instead it was a property tax that was not apportioned according to value as was required by the California constitution. The court also held the trial court did not abuse its discretion in treating the action as a class action.

 

603 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Bernardi v. City Council


No. B098962.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


53 Cal. App. 4th 718; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 895; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 197



March 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1]
Rehearing denied by, Supplemental opinion at Bernardi v. City Council, 54 Cal. App. 4th 426, 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 347, 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 307 (Cal. App. 2d Dist., 1997)
Review denied by Bernardi v. City Council of Los Angeles, 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3389 (Cal., June 11, 1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. C136398 and C133468, Florence T. Pickard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed. Appellants to bear costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city council and agencies, sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which ruled in favor of respondent resident, denying appellants' motion to modify a stipulated judgment validating a business district redevelopment plan. The trial court asserted a lack of jurisdiction for such an in rem proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, city council and agencies, sought review of an order that ruled in favor of respondent resident, denying appellants' motion to modify a stipulated judgment validating a business district redevelopment plan. Appellants' motion invoked the equitable jurisdiction of the trial court, asserting that changed circumstances had rendered the fiscal cap inequitable, but the trial court properly asserted a lack of jurisdiction for such an in rem proceeding, which operated against property, not persons, and was not modifiable as an injunctive order. Appellants asserted that the part of the plan imposing the fiscal cap and debt deadline did not concern the validity of the plan, was not an integral part of the stipulated judgment, and could be modified. However, without the substantive, not merely procedural, limitations, there would never have been a stipulated judgment, so those limitations were inextricably intertwined with the plan's validating language and could not be severed. Subsequent legislation also required the imposition of precisely such restrictions on redevelopment plans. The order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order in favor of respondent resident was affirmed. The court concluded that the trial court's ruling was proper, because the stipulated judgment was binding and conclusive, and the fiscal cap and time limit were integral parts of the judgment and not modifiable. Appellants could not unilaterally change terms or collaterally attack the judgment with respondent resident.

 

604 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Warden v. State Bar


A072485


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


53 Cal. App. 4th 510; 62 Cal. Rptr. 2d 32; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 190; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1915; 97 Daily Journal DAR 3503



March 13, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 5, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3306.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Supreme Court of California Disposition Reported at: 21 Cal. 4th 628.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County. Alameda Superior Court No. 734372-4. Hon. James R. Lambden.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and matter remanded to trial court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged a summary judgment granted to respondent California Bar and two employees from the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) on appellant's complaint that the California Bar's mandatory Continuing Legal Education program, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6070 violated his right to equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 7 by exempting certain members of the bar from its requirements.


OVERVIEW: Appellant attorney was first advised and then removed from the active membership of the state bar after his noncompliance with the minimum mandatory requirements of the bar's Continuing Legal Education (CLE) program, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 6070. Appellant filed a complaint against respondent California Bar and two employees seeking compensatory and punitive damages, declaratory and injunctive relief, and a mandate alleging that the CLE program violated his equal protection rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 7 by exempting certain members of the bar from its requirements. The trial court granted summary judgment for respondents but on appeal the court reversed the judgment and remanded for a declaration that § 6070 was unconstitutional and for an injunction ordering the reinstatement of appellant to active membership. The court found no rational basis for exempting certain members from the mandatory requirement and no persuasive record of support for the exemption theory. In considering a remedy, the court declined to reform or to excise the statute concluding that was an exercise in making policy choices more appropriate for the legislative forum.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment and remanded for a declaration that the mandatory Continuing Legal Education program was unconstitutional, and for an injunction requiring respondent, California Bar and two employees to reinstate appellant attorney to active membership. The court found no rational basis for exempting certain members from the mandatory requirement and no persuasive record of support for the exemption theory.

 

605 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Thompson v. Superior Court


No. B106065.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


53 Cal. App. 4th 480; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 785; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 183; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1894; 97 Daily Journal DAR 3459



March 12, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDING; petition for writ of mandate. Super. Ct. No. BA 134067. Cesar Sarmiento, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We uphold the trial court's discovery order, deny Thompson's writ petition, and remand the matter for discovery compliance and trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applied for a writ of mandate to challenge an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) for discovery of interview notes by his investigator and one of his attorneys with defense witnesses who might testify at trial. The trial court relied on Cal. Penal Code § 1054.3 and exempted any attorney work product from the order.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, charged with possessing a gun as a convicted felon with several prior convictions, applied for a writ of mandate to challenge an order for discovery of interview notes by his investigator and one of his attorneys with defense witnesses who might testify at trial. The trial court relied on Cal. Penal Code § 1054.3 and exempted any attorney work product. The statute distinguished reports from statements and required disclosure of both. Self-recorded electronic statements were statements even though they were not heard or interpreted by anyone else. Raw written notes of witness interviews were witness statements, regardless of whether they were used to prepare a report, and were not drafts expressing the report writer's thought processes. Defense must disclose interview notes to the prosecution. The court held that compelled disclosure to the defense of raw written notes of police and prosecutors' witness interviews was also required. The impressions or opinions of the interviewer, regardless of whether the notes were used to produce a formal written report, were exempt. The discovery order was upheld, the writ was denied, and the matter was remanded to the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the trial court's discovery order, denied petitioner's request for a writ of mandate, and remanded the matter for discovery compliance and trial. The court held that raw written witness interview notes, to the extent that they recorded the witness' statement rather than an attorney's work product impressions, opinions, or conclusions about the statement, were statements and subject to discovery.

 

606 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Mosley


No. B104932.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


53 Cal. App. 4th 489; 62 Cal. Rptr. 2d 268; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 164; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1612; 97 Daily Journal DAR 3058



March 3, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 20, 1997. Review Denied May 21, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 2873.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. (Super. Ct. No. TA043784). Steven Suzukawa, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his multiple convictions from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) that found that defendant had previously been convicted of a serious felony within the meaning of Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)(i) and Cal. Penal Code § 1170.12.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his multiple convictions in which he was found to have been previously convicted of a serious felony conviction within the meaning of Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(i) and Cal. Penal Code § 1170.12. Defendant contended that he was entitled to resentencing so that the trial court could exercise its discretion pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1385(a) to strike the prior serious felony conviction in the interest of justice based on a recent California Supreme Court decision. The court affirmed the multiple convictions and denied defendant's requested resentencing. The court held that the rule allowing postjudgment attacks was not applicable to defendant's sentencing that occurred 53 days after the issuance of the supreme court's decision. The court also held that there was a complete absence of any evidence that the trial judge was unaware of the scope of his discretion and remand for resentencing was not mandated by the rule which allowed the postjudgment attack. It could have been presumed that the trial judge was aware of his power to strike the prior serious felony conviction and intelligently chose not to do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of multiple offenses and found that he had been previously convicted of a serious felony. The court held that defendant was not entitled to resentencing because it presumed that the trial judge was aware of his power to strike the prior serious felony conviction and intelligently chose not to do so.

 

607 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Wolfgram v. Wells Fargo Bank


No. C022370.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


53 Cal. App. 4th 43; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 694; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 139; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1508; 97 Daily Journal DAR 2156



February 27, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 The Reporter of Decisions is directed to publish this opinion with the exception of parts IV. and V.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 27, 1997. Review Denied May 28, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3234. Certiorari Denied October 20, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 6388.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the judgment of the Superior Court of El Dorado County. Super. Ct. No. PV940511. Jack Halpin * and Claude D. Perasso, ** Judges.


* Retired judge of the Shasta Superior Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article Vi, section 6 of the California Constitution.



** Retired Judge of the San Francisco Superior Court, assigned the the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff litigant sought review of an order from the Superior Court of El Dorado County (California), which declared him a vexatious litigant under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 391 et seq., and dismissed his action against defendant bank.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff litigant filed a lawsuit against defendant bank, alleging malicious prosecution and seeking to quiet title to certain realty. A trial court declared plaintiff a vexatious litigant and dismissed his action. Plaintiff appealed the trial court's order. The court affirmed the trial court's order, rejecting plaintiff's novel constitutional challenges to the vexatious litigant statute, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 391 et seq. Plaintiff's five previous losing lawsuits, combined with the fact that he filed another suit which was found to lack merit, supported the reasonable inference that plaintiff was using the court system inappropriately, and would continue to do so. The fact that the statute did not require that the five losing lawsuits be frivolous did not render it unconstitutional. The court concluded that the vexatious litigant statute did not impermissibly chill the right to petition and did not penalize the filing of unsuccessful, colorable lawsuits. The court concluded that the trial court's prefiling order did not constitute an unlawful prior restraint of plaintiff's right to petition, nor violate due process. Plaintiff's claims regarding writs of habeas corpus failed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a trial court's order declaring plaintiff litigant a vexatious litigant and dismissing his suit against defendant bank because plaintiff's five previous losing lawsuits, combined with the present meritless suit, supported a reasonable inference that plaintiff was using the court system inappropriately, and would continue doing so. The court rejected plaintiff's novel constitutional challenges to the vexatious litigant statute.

Lucas v. Swanson & Dowdall


G015273


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


53 Cal. App. 4th 98; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 507; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 140; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1512; 97 Daily Journal DAR 2172



February 27, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 31, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 256. Review Denied June 18, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3668.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Orange County. Super. Ct. No. 631092. Nancy Wieben Stock, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Orange County (California), which granted respondent mobilehome park owner's motion for nonsuit in appellant's action for malicious prosecution that was brought after respondent brought an action for libel and economic interference against appellant who had made published accusations regarding respondent's political activities.


OVERVIEW: Appellant resident's newsletter accused respondent mobilehome park owner of attempting to circumvent a proposed rent control ordinance and reported respondent's campaign contributions made to council members who voted against the ordinance. Respondent brought an action against appellant for libel and economic interference that was voluntarily dismissed. Appellant then brought an action against respondent for malicious prosecution. The trial court granted respondent a nonsuit, and appellant sought review. The court reversed and found no probable cause for respondent to have brought the initial action because the initial action had not been objectively tenable. The court found respondent's initial action had not been objectively tenable because appellant's accusations and comments had been clearly protected by the right to petition guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. I. In finding appellant protected by the right to petition guaranteed under amend. I, the court held that appellant was protected because respondent had failed to show that appellant's accusations and comments were made with actual malice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment granting respondent mobilehome park owner's motion for nonsuit in appellant resident's action for malicious prosecution because in evaluating the objective tenability of respondent's original action for libel and economic interference, the court found that appellant's published accusations, exercised under the First Amendment's petition clause, had been protected from liability unless made with actual malice.

 

609 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Setliff Bros. Service v. Bureau of Automotive Repair


No. C023390.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


53 Cal. App. 4th 1491; 62 Cal. Rptr. 2d 25; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 260; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2476; 97 Daily Journal DAR 4284



February 27, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published March 31, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. 95CS01968. Ronald W. Tochterman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, automotive repair and smog check facility and auto mechanics, challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which denied appellants' writ of administrative mandate challenging respondent bureau's revocations of their smog check license, automotive repair registration, and qualified mechanic certificates.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, automotive repair and smog check facility and auto mechanics, filed a petition for a writ of mandate to challenge administrative revocations of their smog check license, automotive repair registration, and qualified mechanic certificates by respondent bureau. The trial court entered judgment denying the writ, and appellants challenged the decision. The court held that the administrative action brought by respondent to revoke license, registration, and certificates for issuing fraudulent smog certificates and for unnecessary repair charges was not fundamentally unfair even though district attorney had previously brought civil action under the Unfair Practices Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 1700 et seq., based on the same facts. The court held that the administrative action and the civil action were two separate legal proceedings involving separate agencies seeking separate but necessary relief. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the civil action by the district attorney for unfair business practices, based on the same facts, did not preclude the subsequent filing of an administrative action by defendant bureau against appellants, automotive repair and smog check facility and auto mechanics.

 

610 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Laster


No. E016226.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


52 Cal. App. 4th 1450; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 680; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 134; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1448; 97 Daily Journal DAR 2051



February 26, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for partial publication with the exception of parts III.B, III.C.1, III.C.3, III.D.2, IV, V, VI, and VII.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 18, 1997. Review Denied June 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3660.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from the Superior Court of Riverside County.. Super.Ct.No. CR-57814. Edward D. Webster, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged their convictions from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), for deliberate and premeditated attempted murder arising out of a drive-by shooting, along with race and vicarious arming enhancements. Defendants claimed that the actual shooter was a passenger in the back seat, and the prosecution argued that they were both liable for attempted murder on an aiding and abetting theory.


OVERVIEW: Defendants challenged their convictions for deliberate and premeditated attempted murder arising out of a drive-by shooting. Defendants claimed that the shooter was someone in the back seat, so the prosecution argued that they were liable for attempted murder as aiders and abettors. The real question was not whether the actual offense was a consequence of the target offense, but whether the charged crime was a consequence of the aider and abettor's facilitation of the target offense. Assuming the jury found that defendants knowingly and intentionally aided and abetted the discharge of a firearm from a vehicle, it still had to determine whether attempted murder was a natural and probable consequence, which required it to consider whether it was reasonably foreseeable that the perpetrator harbored an intent to kill. A driver or owner could be held criminally liable either for affirmatively assenting to, or for failing to prevent, the discharge of a firearm from a vehicle, and an aider and abettor could be subject to life imprisonment for willful, deliberate, and premeditated murder even if he or she did not personally deliberate or premeditate. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The court found no prejudicial error. Even if defendants did not discharge the firearm, they could be held criminally liable either for affirmatively assenting to, or for failing to prevent, the discharge.

 

611 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Hepner v. Franchise Tax Bd.


No. B097029.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


52 Cal. App. 4th 1475; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 341; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 133; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1445; 97 Daily Journal DAR 2071



February 26, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 20, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BS033140. Diane Wayne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. The Board to recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax debtors challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied their petition for writ of mandate to overturn certain actions taken by respondent tax board.


OVERVIEW: Appellant tax debtors recovered a judgment against an insurer in a bad faith suit. Respondent tax board issued an order to withhold personal income tax, directing the insurer to withhold the amount of tax owed by appellants from any payments due them. Respondent denied appellants' claim that the award was exempt because it represented an award for disability payments and compensation for mental anguish. The trial court denied appellants' petition for writ of mandate. The court upheld the decision because the statutory scheme did not provide for exemptions to tax debtors when enforcement was pursued by a notice to withhold. It traced the evolution of the statute and determined that the prior statute did not contain the words "notice to withhold." Although the statute was amended to provide exemptions in cases where a warrant or notice of levy was issued, it was not amended to provide an exemption when enforcement was by way of a notice to withhold, and that the legislature was aware it was not expanding the law to permit a tax debtor to claim exemptions when enforcement was via a notice to withhold.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the trial court's denial of appellant tax debtors' petition for writ of mandate because the statutory scheme did not allow appellants to claim an exemption when respondent Franchise Tax Board of the State of California sought collection through a notice to withhold instead of through a warrant or notice of levy.

 

612 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Yamaha Corp. v. State Bd. of Equalization


B095911


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


52 Cal. App. 4th 1268; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 244; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 120; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1273; 97 Daily Journal DAR 1855



February 21, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted June 11, 1997 (S060145), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3315. (See 19 Cal. 4th 1).


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC079444. Daniel A. Curry, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of equalization challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which awarded respondent retailer a refund of use tax and interest, concluding that certain gifts of stock-in-trade and promotional literature which were made to out-of-state donees fell within the exclusion from state use tax under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 6009.1.


OVERVIEW: Appellant board of equalization challenged a judgment awarding respondent retailer a refund of use tax and interest. The trial court concluded that gifts of stock-in-trade and promotional literature made to out-of-state donees fell within the exclusion from use tax under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 6009.1. The trial court's judgment was reversed. Respondent conceded that a gift was a use, so it was subject to use tax if the gift was made in-state, whether or not a use of any other kind was made. Respondent did not show that the mutual credits provided by California and other states for sales and use taxes would not adequately protect against multiple taxation. State use tax was deemed to be due if the property was purchased without payment of sales tax and then delivered to a common carrier for transportation to a donee either inside or outside the state. Respondent's purchase of merchandise using resale certificates with the intent of giving the merchandise away was improper. Sales tax was owing on any sale of merchandise that was not purchased for resale. It was immaterial that respondent later gave some of the literature away out-of-state rather than in-state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment which awarded respondent retailer a refund of use tax and interest. It concluded that the trial court incorrectly interpreted a statute concerning an exclusion from use tax. Taxes were properly imposed on respondent retailer's gifts, and no refund was due. Costs on appeal were awarded to the respondent board of equalization.
