People v. Barrett


C016755


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


52 Cal. App. 4th 1495; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 482; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 112; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1220; 97 Daily Journal DAR 1751



February 19, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied May 21, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 2882.
Review denied by, Opinion withdrawn by order of court at People v. Barrett, 1997 Cal. LEXIS 2882 (Cal., May 20, 1997)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Barrett v. Yearwood, 1999 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 23650 (E.D. Cal., July 9, 1999)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Barrett v. Meeks, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 82935 (E.D. Cal., Nov. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Shasta County. Super. Ct. No. 898183. Jack Halpin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Shasta County (California), which convicted defendant of two counts of willful failure to file personal income tax returns with intent to evade a tax under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code §19706 and 12 counts of willful failure to file quarterly employee payroll withholding tax returns under Cal. Unemp. Ins. Code § 2117.5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of willful failure to file personal income tax returns with intent to evade a tax under Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 19706 and 12 counts of willful failure to file quarterly employee payroll withholding tax returns Cal. Unemp. Ins. Code § 2117.5. On appeal, the court found that the willful failure to file the required form could be found only if the defendant knew that he was obliged under the law of taxation to file the form. Further the court found that there was nothing in the evidence which supported an inference that defendant's failure to file a personal income tax return was not "willful" in the required sense. The court affirmed the trial court holding that there was no requirement to instruct on mistake of law as to the failure to file an income tax return because there was no evidence upon which a jury could have found a reasonable doubt under this theory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant because there was no requirement to instruct on mistake of law as to the failure to file an income tax return because there was no evidence upon which a jury could have found a reasonable doubt under this theory.

 

614 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Board of Administration v. Wilson


No. C020118.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


52 Cal. App. 4th 1109; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 207; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 115; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1204; 97 Daily Journal DAR 1731



February 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied May 28, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 3230.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. CV377815. John R. Lewis, Judge. *


* Judge of the Sacramento Municipal Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Respondents shall recover their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant governor of California sought review of a judgment by Superior Court, Sacramento County (California), which granted respondent Board of the California Public Employees' Retirement System judgment on respondent's claims that two state senate bills that were passed by the legislature to balance the budget and changed the manner in which the retirement system was funded constituted an impairment of contract.


OVERVIEW: The California legislature, by two senate bills, changed the manner in which the California Public Employees' Retirement Fund (PERS) was funded. The rationale behind the change was to balance the state budget. Respondent PERS Board of Administration filed suit against appellant governor, arguing that the funding change constituted a violation of the constitutional right to be free of impairment of contracts. The trial court found for respondent, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed, holding that the change in funding constituted an unconstitutional impairment of contract. The court stated that state employees had a vested contractual right to pension benefits, and that the right to such benefits accrued upon acceptance of employment. The pension right could not be destroyed without impairing a contractual obligation of the employing entity. The court further held that state employees had a contractual right to an actuarially sound retirement system. Appellant argued that balancing the budget was a valid reason for changing funding. The court disagreed, stating that any change in the funding of the retirement fund had to bear some relation to its successful operation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of judgment to respondent retirement system board, holding that the passage of senate bills to balance the budget impermissibly constituted an impairment of a contract. The court held that state employees had a vested contractual right to pension benefits when employment was accepted, and that such a pension right could not be destroyed without impairing the contractual obligation of the employing entity.

 

615 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Mesce


No. A071221.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


52 Cal. App. 4th 618; 60 Cal. Rptr. 2d 745; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 79; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 839; 97 Daily Journal DAR 1199



February 4, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III and IV.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied May 14, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 2576.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the County of Humboldt. (Humboldt County Super. Ct. No. 94 CR0317). Honorable J. Michael Brown.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, having found no violation of the ex post facto provisions of the United States and California Constitutions inherent in the statute and the defendant having advanced no other tenable arguments, we affirm the judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of the County of Humboldt (California), convicting him of possession of a firearm by one previously convicted of a misdemeanor assault in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12021(c). Defendant contended that the ex post facto clauses, U.S. Const. art. I, § 9, cl. 3, § 10, and Cal. Const. art. I, § 9, protected him from prosecution under the statute and required reversal of his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded no contest to a charge of misdemeanor assault in 1987. Defendant was consequently convicted of various offenses, including possession of a firearm by one previously convicted of a misdemeanor assault in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12021(c) (1993). Defendant appealed, contending that the ex post facto clauses of the federal and state Constitutions, U.S. Const. art. I, § 9, cl. 3, § 10, and Cal. Const. art. I, § 9, protected him from prosecution under the statute. The court affirmed the conviction. The court found that applying § 12021(c) to defendant did not violate constitutional ex post facto principles because defendant was convicted based on conduct occurring after the effective date of the statute. The court found that the statute did not disadvantage defendant because it did not change the punishment for the original crime. Defendant's "inability" to petition for restoration of his right to possess firearms was speculative at best and did not invalidate his conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a firearm by one previously convicted of a misdemeanor assault because application of the criminal statute did not violate the ex post facto provisions of the United States and California Constitutions. The court found that the statute was not retrospective and it did not change the punishment for the original crime.

 

616 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Falck


No. A071025.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


52 Cal. App. 4th 287; 60 Cal. Rptr. 2d 624; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 49; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 646; 97 Daily Journal DAR 986



January 27, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of the parts in brackets in the first paragraph and parts III and IV.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 24, 1997. Review Denied April 16, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1974.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court Alameda County. Super. Ct. No. H20820. Hon. John F. Kraetzer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which convicted him of stalking in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 646.9(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was diagnosed with schizophrenia and used medication to control his impulses. He became fixated with the victim. After being warned to make no further contacts, he refrained from contacting victim for 12 years. After he quit taking his medication, he made contact and was subsequently arrested and convicted of stalking. The court affirmed the conviction. It held that Cal. Penal Code § 646.9(a), was neither unconstitutionally vague nor overbroad because the term safety was commonly used and its use did not make the statute unconstitutionally vague and uncertain, and the statute's application was limited only to threats that posed a danger to society. The court held there was substantial evidence to support the conviction. It found that appellant's conduct conveyed a credible threat of his intent to cause fear in the victim because he insisted on maintaining contact although she clearly was attempting to avoid him and he had been warned away; his letters to her reflected his desire to engage in sexual acts which included elements of bondage or violence, and their being together for eternity; he sent the victim black roses; and he referred to his prowess with a rifle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of stalking. It held the statute was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad because safety is a commonly used term and the statute's application was limited only to threats that posed danger to society. It further held that appellant's conduct conveyed a credible threat and an intent to cause fear in the victim.

 

617 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Dias


No. F024370.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


52 Cal. App. 4th 46; 60 Cal. Rptr. 2d 443; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 35; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 493; 97 Daily Journal DAR 767



January 17, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part 2.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied April 16, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 2152.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Stanislaus County. Super. Ct. No. 4302. Hon. John G. Whiteside, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his convictions from the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California) for kidnapping, burglary of an inhabited dwelling, threatening a crime, and evading an officer following a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant went to the home of his ex-wife's boyfriend, pointed a fully loaded gun at them, and threatened to kill them. Defendant forced his ex-wife to leave with him in his truck. Defendant was arrested following a police chase. Defendant was charge with kidnapping, burglary of an inhabited dwelling, threatening a crime, and evading an officer. At trial, defendant maintained that he merely wanted to talk to his ex-wife and did not intend to kidnap her. A jury convicted defendant and this appeal followed. Defendant argued that the threatening counts had to be reversed because some of the threats he made were conditional and therefore, did not violate Cal. Penal Code § 422. The court disagreed and held that a threat subject to an apparent condition violated § 422. An absolutely unconditional threat is only one of several means by which that end may be accomplished. The jury was properly instructed that defendant could not have been found guilty of a violation of § 422 unless the threat was so unequivocal, unconditional, immediate, and specific as to convey to the person threatened, a gravity of purpose and an immediate prospect of execution of the threat.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for kidnapping, burglary, threatening a crime, and evading an officer because the lower court fully instructed the jury in the elements of the threatening a crime counts and made it clear that defendant could not be found guilty of a violation of the statute unless the prosecution proved an immediate prospect of execution of the threat.

 

618 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Jenron Corp. v. Department of Social Services


No. A072966.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


54 Cal. App. 4th 1429; 63 Cal. Rptr. 2d 508; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 378; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3663; 97 Daily Journal DAR 6227



January 17, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Supreme Court from Unpublished to Published May 14, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 963642. William J. Cahill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order denying appellants' petition for writ of mandate is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, adult residential care facility licensees, requested a writ of mandate to review an order of the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which affirmed the revocation of their licenses by respondent Department of Social Services.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, adult residential care facility licensees, argued that the revocation of their licenses by respondent Department of Social Services was improper because a residence housing a patient who fatally stabbed another patient was not an unlicensed facility, or was exempt from licensing. The court held that appellants accepted a patient who required care and supervision, and thus the residence was an unlicensed facility. The court refused to address the issue of whether the exemption statute was constitutional because appellants' conduct constituted conduct inimical to the health of residents receiving services, another ground for revocation. The court affirmed because appellants knew or should have known the patient required supervision, because they were aware of the patient's history of schizophrenia and of a previous assault, and thus the facility was not exempt from licensing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of licenses held by appellants, adult residential care facility licensees, because their facility was not exempt from licensing by respondent Department of Social Services, because appellants knew or should of known that their patient needed care and supervision.

 

619 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Ohio v. Barron


No. F023873.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


52 Cal. App. 4th 62; 60 Cal. Rptr. 2d 342; 1997 Cal. App. LEXIS 34; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 495; 97 Daily Journal DAR 759



January 15, 1997, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II and III.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County. Super. Ct. No. 487756-9. Hon. Nancy A. Cisneros, Judge. *


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Fresno County (California), which required him to pay support arrearages pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 11350, subd. (a)(2), contending that the statutory requirement that he reimburse the state for amounts in excess of what was actually paid violated his due process and equal protection rights under Cal. Const. art. I, § 7 subd. (a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant father was a noncustodial parent whose child received Aid to Families with Dependent Children (AFDC) support. The state sought reimbursement from appellant for support expended, plus additional sums that would total the amount appellant would have been required to pay in child support. Appellant contended that the state action seeking more than the state had expended was an equal protection and due process violation under Cal. Const. art. I, § 7 subd. (a), because it treated noncustodial parents differently, i.e., if the child had not received AFDC support, the state would not be able to seek any reimbursement, and could not seek reimbursement for sums prior to an order to show cause. On appeal, the court examined the state and federal statutory schemes, under AFDC, and held that because the support of needy children was a legitimate state purpose, the Uniform Reciprocal Enforcement of Support Act (URESA), Cal. Fam. Code § 4800 et seq., was narrowly tailored and worked in conjunction with the controlling federal statute, the statute bore a rational relationship to the legitimate purpose, and was not unconstitutional as applied, and affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment requiring appellant father to pay child support arrearages, holding that because the statute was narrowly tailored, rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose, and was in compliance with federal reimbursement mandates, the trial court's judgment did not violate appellant's equal protection or due process rights.

 

620 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Sacramento County Deputy Sheriffs' Assn. v. County of Sacramento


No. C019777.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


51 Cal. App. 4th 1468; 59 Cal. Rptr. 2d 834; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1216; 12 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 723; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 48; 96 Daily Journal DAR 53



December 31, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 26, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1779.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. CV536194. Hon. Joe S. Gray, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Defendants shall recover their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriffs' association sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which entered summary judgment in favor of respondent county. Appellant brought a civil action against respondent for the warrantless video surveillance of a county jail office. Appellant contended that the videotaping was excessively intrusive and invaded their expectation of privacy.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined that appellant sheriffs' association had no reasonable expectation of privacy. Appellant contended summary judgment was improperly granted to respondent county because the videotaping assertedly violated protections against unlawful search and seizure, violated statutory prohibitions against invasion of privacy, and constituted a tortious intrusion into their seclusion. The court affirmed the judgment. Balancing the institutional security interests against appellant's interests in this case, the court did not believe that appellant had a reasonable expectation of privacy against being videotaped in the release office of the jail. The videotaping was not excessively intrusive because there was no audio recording and the sole intent was to record an act, not a confidential communication. The court also found that there was no offensive conduct supporting appellant's tortious privacy claim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which entered summary judgment in favor of respondent county. The court did not believe appellant sheriffs' association had a reasonable expectation of privacy against being videotaped in the release office of the jail and the videotaping was not excessively intrusive.

 

621 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Peck


No. E016630.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


52 Cal. App. 4th 351; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 1; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1222; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 654; 97 Daily Journal DAR 1003



December 30, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published January 27, 1997. Review Denied March 26, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1795.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Riverside County. Super. Ct. No. CR57118. Hon. Robert G. Spitzer, Judge. *


* Judge of the Municipal Court for the Western Riverside County Judicial District, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant church member challenged the order of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California) which rejected his free expression of religion defense under Religious Freedom Restoration Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb et seq., and challenged the judgment of conviction and sentence imposed for transportation of marijuana and possession for sale of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant church member was convicted of transportation of marijuana and possession for sale of marijuana and imposed probation. Defendant sought review, asserting that his drug use was the free exercise of his religion, which considered marijuana a sacrament. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that the criminal laws under which defendant was convicted did not substantially burden his free exercise of religion under the Religious Freedom Restoration Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000bb et seq., and the laws did not have to be supported by a compelling state interest. There was no interference with a tenet or belief that was central to religious doctrine. Defendant was prosecuted for transporting a large quantity of marijuana and possessing it for sale, activities related only peripherally to his religious practice. Compelling state interests supported the probation condition that he not associate with drug users.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction for transportation of marijuana and possession for sale of marijuana was affirmed because there was no denial of defendant's right to free expression of religion or to free association. The challenged law did not directly interfere with the use of marijuana for religious purposes and compelling state interests supported the terms of his probation.

 

622 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Rodriguez v. Dep't of Real Estate


No. A074922.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


51 Cal. App. 4th 1289; 59 Cal. Rptr. 2d 652; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1207; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9480; 96 Daily Journal DAR 15537



December 26, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 24, 1997. Review Denied April 16, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 2046.


PRIOR HISTORY: Contra Costa County Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. C95-01543. Hon. Ignazio Ruvolo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant realtor challenged the order of the Contra Costa County Superior Court (California) which denied the petition for a writ of administrative mandate against respondent California Department of Real Estate to prevent automatic revocation of his license pursuant to Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 10475 after respondent department paid the defrauded respondent real party in interest from respondent department's client recovery account.


OVERVIEW: Real party in interest lender provided loans for the purchase of real estate to appellant realtor's clients. Those clients were insolvent, and defaulted on the loans. Because appellant failed to record the deeds of trust against the properties sold, real party in interest was unable to recover from the clients the amounts loaned. Respondent California Department of Real Estate paid real party in interest from its real estate recovery account, and automatically suspended appellant's broker's license under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 10475. The superior court denied appellant's petition challenging the revocation. The court affirmed the judgment, concluding that appellant's U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 7(a) due process rights were not violated by the revocation of his license without a formal hearing. Applying a four-factor analysis, the court concluded that notice and an opportunity to provide written argument satisfied due process requirements. Further, the court concluded that the suspension was not a quasi-judicial act requiring a formal hearing under § 10475.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of the petition for a writ of administrative mandate because appellant realtor's due process rights were not violated by respondent California Department of Real Estate's suspension of his license as an automatic consequence of granting defrauded respondent real party in interest's claim for payment from the client recovery account.

 

623 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Nazem


No. A068823.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


51 Cal. App. 4th 1225; 59 Cal. Rptr. 2d 794; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1201; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9389; 96 Daily Journal DAR 15625



December 23, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of City and County of San Francisco. Super. Ct. No. 157166. Hon. Anne Bouliane, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from Superior Court of City and County of San Francisco (California) which convicted him of possession of MDMA, or Ecstasy, and sentenced him to three years of probation and six months in prison, contending that prosecution was barred by the double jeopardy clause of U.S. Const. Amend. V.


OVERVIEW: When defendant consented to a search of his home, police found MDMA, or Ecstasy, marijuana, a loaded handgun, brass knuckles, paraphernalia related to MDMA sales, and cash. After defendant was convicted of possession of MDMA and sentenced to three years of probation and six months in prison, defendant appealed, contending that his prosecution was barred by the double jeopardy clause of U.S. Const. Amend. V, following the completed forfeiture of money and property in a related civil action. The court disagreed and affirmed. A presumption existed that in rem civil forfeiture proceedings did not result in punishment for purposes of the double jeopardy clause. That presumption could be rebutted by the clearest proof that an in rem civil forfeiture was so punitive either in purpose or effect as to be equivalent to a criminal proceeding. In this case, forfeiture served nonpunitive purpose of discouraging property owners from using or allowing use of property in illegal activity and, although forfeiture was linked in some instances to commission of criminal offenses, that fact alone did not constitute the clearest proof necessary to demonstrate that a proceeding was criminal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence because forfeiture served nonpunitive purpose of discouraging property owners from using or allowing use of property in illegal activity and, although forfeiture was linked in some instances to commission of criminal offenses, that fact alone did not constitute the clearest proof necessary to demonstrate that a proceeding was criminal.

 

624 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Perez


No. C021585.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


51 Cal. App. 4th 1168; 59 Cal. Rptr. 2d 596; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1192; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9345; 96 Daily Journal DAR 15351



December 19, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied March 19, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1501.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of County of Siskiyou. Super. Ct. No. 51761. Hon. Guy M. Young, Judge, Assigned.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed. The superior court is directed to vacate its sentencing order directing service of custody in the home detention program monitored by Hayden Consulting. Since we are advised that defendant has completed the probation condition of a period of custody, remand for resentencing is unnecessary. (See People v. Superior Court (Peterson) (1992) 12 Cal. App. 4th 16, 27 [14 Cal. Rptr. 2d 685].)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hunter appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Siskiyou County (California), for possession of methamphetamine under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11377, and unlawful possession of waterfowl under Cal. Fish & Game Code § 2002. Defendant contended his motion to suppress should have been granted because he was unlawfully detained at a fish and game checkpoint; the prosecution challenged the sentence as unauthorized.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction and sentence for possession of methamphetamine under Cal. Health & Safety Code § 11377, and unlawful possession of waterfowl under Cal. Fish & Game Code § 2002. The court affirmed and held that a fish and game checkpoint did not result in an unreasonable search or seizure under U.S. Const. amend. IV, but defendant's home detention sentence exceeded the trial court's jurisdiction, so the sentencing order was vacated. The convictions were affirmed because the court held that the checkpoint was only slightly intrusive in that it was designed with specific, legitimate guidelines in mind; its location and operational procedures were determined at the supervisory level, vehicles were stopped according to a neutral formula; and signs advised of the checkpoints. The court held that hunters had a reduced expectation of privacy in their gear and their take from hunting, so it was reasonable to detain hunters briefly, near hunting areas during hunting season, to inspect their licenses, tags, equipment, and any wildlife taken. The search was not pretextual and defendant consented to a search that led to the drugs.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for unlawful possession of methamphetamine and waterfowl was affirmed but the order of home detention exceed the trial court's jurisdiction. The strong public interest in regulation of natural resources outweighed the slight intrusion caused by the stop at a properly administered checkpoint, defendant's detention was justified, and the vehicle search was legitimate.

 

625 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Welch


No. H014843


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


51 Cal. App. 4th 1128; 60 Cal. Rptr. 2d 116; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1194; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9350; 96 Daily Journal DAR 15290



December 19, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied March 19, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, section 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1546.


PRIOR HISTORY: Santa Clara County Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. 181006. Hon. Taketsugu Takei, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Santa Clara County Superior Court (California), which convicted him of rape under Cal. Penal Code § 261(a)(2), and penetration with a foreign object under Cal. Penal Code § 289(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with rape under Cal. Penal Code § 261(a)(2), and penetration with a foreign object under Cal. Penal Code § 289(a), after his wife's minor daughter accused him of these charges. Defendant submitted to a polygraph test, and admitted that he had consensual sex with the minor but stated that he did not rape her. Defendant passed the polygraph test and turned the evidence over to the prosecution to aid plea negotiations. The trial court admitted his admission of consensual sex, but denied admission of the test result, and defendant was convicted as charged. The court affirmed, finding that, as the evidence did not establish that defendant believed at the time he made the admission that his statement would necessarily be turned over to the prosecution for plea negotiations, the trial court could conclude that defendant's admission was not made in the course of plea negotiations. The court found that defendant did not establish a due process violation where defendant made no offer of proof of the reliability of polygraph test results. With the absence of an offer of proof, due process challenges to the statutory exclusion of polygraph evidence were rejected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of rape and penetration with a foreign object because an admission during a polygraph test was admissible where the admission was not made during the course of plea negotiations, and defendant's due process rights were not violated by excluding evidence of the polygraph test result, where defendant made no offer of proof as to the reliability of the polygraph test.

 

626 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Longval v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


No. D024789.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


51 Cal. App. 4th 792; 59 Cal. Rptr. 2d 463; 61 Cal. Comp. Cases 1396; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1175; 96 Daily Journal DAR 15047; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9124



December 16, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1364.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for a writ of review from a decision of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board. WCAB SD0 200983 & SD0 193104.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of November 12, 1996, Previously Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1050.



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the WCAB are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner representative filed a writ of review from a decision of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (California), which denied petitioner's request for attorneys' fees in association with his representation of a claimant because petitioner was not licensed to practice law.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner representative was not licensed to practice law in California. Petitioner represented a claimant seeking workers' compensation benefits. Prior California statutes allowed unlicensed persons to represent workers before the Workers' Compensation Board of Appeals (WCAB), and to receive compensation. The workers' compensation judge denied petitioner's request for attorneys' fees, and the WCAB affirmed. On judicial review, petitioner argued that he was deprived his fundamental right to engage in his occupation. However, the court found that the relevant statutes had been amended, and that the clear aim of the amendments to Cal. Labor Code §§ 4903 (a) and 5710(b)(4) was to control fraudulent claim practices by increasing professional and criminal penalties and actively investigating and prosecuting fraud, and that any deprivation was a valid exercise of police power. The court rejected petitioner's argument that the amendments denied him equal protection of the laws because there was nothing in the record to support those assertions, and petitioner did not have standing to challenge the statutes on behalf of applicants. The decisions of the WCAB were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Decision of the Workers' Compensation Board of Appeals (WCBA) that denied petitioner representative's request for attorneys' fees in association with his representation of an applicant before the WCBA was affirmed because petitioner was not licensed to practice law. Furthermore, statutes that were amended to allow only licensed attorneys' to receive fees did not deny petitioner his rights of equal protection or due process.

 

627 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Native Am. Heritage Com v. Bd. of Trs.


No. B093693.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


51 Cal. App. 4th 675; 59 Cal. Rptr. 2d 402; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1157; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 9021; 96 Daily Journal DAR 14925



December 12, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 31, 1996. Review Denied April 2, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1863.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC 087212. Hon. Abby Soven, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We reverse the judgment and remand the matter for trial. Plaintiffs are entitled to their costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, California Native American Heritage Commission and individual Native Americans, challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found that the statute that authorized appellants actions was facially unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent university, a state agency, decided to develop a 22-acre site on its campus. Appellants, the California Native American Heritage Commission, also a state agency, and several individual Native Americans, filed a lawsuit seeking an injunction to prevent damage to a Native American religious or ceremonial site located on public property pursuant to Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 5097.94 (g). The trial court granted appellant's motion for summary judgment, finding that the statutes authorizing respondents' actions were facially unconstitutional. On review, the court found that appellants lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the statute that authorized respondents' actions. Furthermore, the court found that the rights forwarded by respondent were personal rights designed to protect individuals from governmental violations of their constitutional rights; they were not designed to be used as leverage by one state agency in a dispute with another agency about the appropriate use of state-owned land. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for trial.


OUTCOME: Trial court's decision that found statutes that empowered appellants Native American Heritage Commission unconstitutional was reversed because respondent university had no standing to challenge the constitutional validity of another state agency's statute.

 

628 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Brillantes v. Superior Court


No. B100434.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


51 Cal. App. 4th 323; 58 Cal. Rptr. 2d 770; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1114; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8661; 96 Daily Journal DAR 14264



November 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied March 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1320.


PRIOR HISTORY: Petition for Writ of Mandate. Super. Ct. No. BH-00750. Hon. Charles Horan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of mandate is denied, and the alternate writ is discharged. The stay imposed by this court shall remain in effect until issuance of the remittitur. The real party in interest is to recover costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner doctor filed an application for writ of mandate which sought to challenge an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied petitioner an in camera hearing and file review of patients medical records pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1524(c) and denied petitioner's motion for a sealing order in a Medi-Cal fraud action filed against petitioner.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner doctor was suspected of Medi-Cal fraud and a search warrant was procured to search petitioner's residence and medical offices. Petitioner filed an objection to the search and seizure and a motion for a sealing order. The trial court issued a protective order and sealed the patients' files for 30-days. Petitioner filed an application for writ of mandate and a request to extend the 30-day stay. Petitioner argued that even though he was suspected of criminal activity, he was entitled to an in camera review pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1524(c). The court denied petitioner's application and held that petitioner did not have a statutory right to either a special master or a hearing because he was suspected of criminal activity. Further, the court held that the Medi-Cal patients had only a limited privacy interest in their records, and that there was no violation of this interest. The search warrant procedure used adequately protected whatever privacy interest the patients had in their medical information and therefore, the court held that the patient files specifically related to the fraud investigation must be unsealed and provided to the investigators.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner doctor's application for writ of mandate. The court held that petitioner did not have a right to an in camera hearing and file review because he was suspected of Medi-Cal fraud. The court also held that the privacy interest the Medi-Cal patients had in their files was not absolute and the state demonstrated a compelling interest in the medical records related to the fraud investigation.

 

629 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Imuta v. Nakano


No. B070113


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


51 Cal. App. 4th 243; 59 Cal. Rptr. 2d 78; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1129; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8669; 96 Daily Journal DAR 14337



November 27, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing of December 24, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1206. Review Denied April 16, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. C630297, Consolidated with No. C643515. Hon. Philip M. Saeta, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant religious leaders sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondents', reverend and church, monetary and declaratory relief in an action that alleged various torts including breach of fiduciary duty, intentional interference with contract relations, intentional interference with prospective business advantage, and intentional infliction of emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: Respondents', reverend and church, filed a complaint that alleged various torts against appellant religion leaders. The trial court awarded judgment in favor of respondents. On appeal, appellants' argued that the trial court lacked constitutional jurisdiction to decide the dispute because is was ecclesiastical in nature, that appellants' statements and actions were privileged under U.S. Const. amend. I, and that awarded punitive damages were excessive. The court held that the trial court had the power to decide the case because it did not decide any religious questions and all ecclesiastical inquiries had been determined by a Japanese court under a final and binding judgment. Appellants' U.S. Const. amend. I contentions were waived because appellants did not ask the court to apply the Sullivan test, New York Times v. Sullivan, 376 U.S. 254, 11 L. Ed. 2d 686, 84 S. Ct. 710 (1964), or object to the fact that the Sullivan test was not used. The court reversed and remanded the judgment insofar as it awarded punitive damages because new case law was retroactively applied that required an inquiry of appellants' financial condition.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, insofar as it awarded compensatory and declaratory relief in favor of respondents', reverend and church. The trial court reversed and remanded an award of punitive damages because a change in the law required evidence of appellant religious leaders' financial status before such an award could be granted.

 

630 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Scott v. State Bd. of Equalization


No. C021645.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


50 Cal. App. 4th 1597; 58 Cal. Rptr. 2d 376; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1090; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8537; 96 Daily Journal DAR 14065



November 22, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. CV542769. Hon. Richard K. Park, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county tax assessor sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), in favor of respondent State Board of Equalization declaring Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 63.1(e)(4) to be constitutional. Section 63.1(e)(4) retroactively extended the time period during which the parent-child exclusion from property reassessment must be claimed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant county tax assessor sought review of a declaratory judgment finding Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 63.1(e)(4) constitutional. Under Cal. Const. art. XIII A, § 2(h), real property could be transferred from parents to children without triggering a reassessment of the value of the property (the parent-child exclusion). Section 63.1(e)(4) retroactively extended the time period during which the parent-child exclusion could be claimed. On appeal, the reviewing court rejected appellant's argument that § 63.1(e)(4) violated Cal. Const. art XIII, § 6, which provided that the failure in any year to claim a classification which reduced a property tax amounted to a waiver for that year. The court found that the waiver provision in art. XIII, § 6 applied to classifications filed annually. It did not apply to the parent-child exclusion, which is only claimed once. The court also found that § 63.1(e)(4) did not amount to an unconstitutional gift of public funds given its valid public purpose. The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, finding that the provision that retroactively extended the time period for filing the parent-child exclusion from reassessment was constitutional. It did not violate the California Constitution's annual waiver provision because it was a one-time exclusion. Nor did it violate the constitution's prohibition against making a gift of public funds.

 

631 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Nunn


No. D023930.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


50 Cal. App. 4th 1357; 58 Cal. Rptr. 2d 294; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1071; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8427; 96 Daily Journal DAR 13841



November 18, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of Discussion part B.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied March 12, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1361.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. SCD106831. Hon. Richard M. Murphy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his convictions of multiple attempted murders and assaults with a deadly weapon, enhanced by firearms findings, from an order the Superior Court of San Diego County (California). Appellant asserted that the trial court improperly excluded defense psychological testimony.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought reversal of his conviction of multiple attempted murders and assaults with a deadly weapon, enhanced by firearms findings. Appellant asserted that the trial court erred in excluding defense psychological testimony regarding appellant's tendency to be impulsive. The court affirmed the convictions and held that appellant's expert witness was properly prohibited by the trial court from testifying to appellant's state of mind at the time of the incident, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 29. However, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code §§ 28, 29, appellant's expert was allowed to testify about appellant's psychological history and appellant's impulsive tendencies generally, which the trial court admitted into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions because the trial court properly excluded testimony of appellant's expert witness regarding appellant's state of mind at the time of appellant's criminal conduct.

 

632 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Hubbart v. Superior Court


No. H015007


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


50 Cal. App. 4th 1155; 58 Cal. Rptr. 2d 268; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1054; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8264; 96 Daily Journal DAR 13729



November 14, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted February 26, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 1008.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Supreme Court of California disposition reported at: 19 Cal. 4th 1138.


PRIOR HISTORY: Sup. Ct. No. 140294. Hon. Robert M. Foley, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Petition for writ of prohibition denied. Temporary stay, dated May 3, 1996, dissolved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara Count (California), which denied defendant's demurrer to the state's petition for commitment as sexually violent offender pursuant to the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq. Defendant filed a petition for writ of prohibition and requested a stay.


OVERVIEW: The state filed a petition to commit defendant as a sexually violent predator pursuant to the Sexually Violent Predators Act (SVP), Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq. The trial court denied defendant's demurrer to the petition. On appeal, the court denied defendant's writ of prohibition and lifted the stay on proceedings. Defendant contended that the SVP violated constitutional prohibitions against ex post facto and double jeopardy. The court held that the statute was not penal in nature, but was a civil procedure for committing and treating persons representing a danger to society because of mental disorders. The court held that the law did not operate to increase punishment for the underlying crime, because the commitment was not based on a proven history of prior violent sexual acts. Defendant complained that the statute violated equal protection and due process. The court held that equal protection standards were met by requiring a finding of current mental disorder and present danger. The court held that the statute was specifically tailored to assure that only those most likely to engage in violent sexually predatory behavior could be committed.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for writ of prohibition and lifted the stay on further proceedings. The court held that the Sexually Violent Predators Act (SVP) did not violate ex post facto and double jeopardy protections. The court held that SVP was not unconstitutional on its face, and did not violate constitutional guarantees of equal protection and due process of law.

 

633 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Appel


No. B097113.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


51 Cal. App. 4th 495; 59 Cal. Rptr. 2d 216; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1135; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8828; 96 Daily Journal DAR 14604



November 7, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published December 5, 1996. Review Denied February 19, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 861.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County of Ventura. Super. Ct. No. CR36644. Hon. James P. Cloninger, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment granting probation is affirmed. The stay on jail time previously ordered by trial court is vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of Ventura County (California), which sentenced him to probation after a jury convicted him of knowingly discharging pollutants into the waters of the United States in violation of Cal. Water Code § 13387(a)(4).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who constructed a levee in the bottom of a river running through his property without first obtaining a stream bed alteration agreement, was convicted under Cal. Water Code § 13387(a)(4). The court held that defendant's conviction under the statute did not violate ex post facto principles because the statute was enacted prior to the acts with which he was charged. Defendant's due process rights were not violated because the jurisdictional determination language in the statute was not vague, defendant had no right to challenge the determination prior to trial, and defendant failed to show that he was prejudiced by the prosecution's delay in bringing the charges after evidence of his activities was destroyed because defendant was aware of the investigation beforehand. The state was not precluded from prosecuting defendant because 33 U.S.C.S. §§ 1319(c)(2), 1251(b), portions of the Federal Water Pollution Control Act, provided for criminal penalties and did not preempt California law. Defendant could not have used the converted cropland exemption under 33 U.S.C.S. § 1344(f)(1)(A) as a defense because his activities did not qualify as part of an ongoing farming operation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment granting probation because defendant's prosecution under the water code did not contravene ex post facto principles and his rights to due process had not been violated.

 

634 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Superior Court (Myers)


No. B103647.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


50 Cal. App. 4th 826; 58 Cal. Rptr. 2d 32; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1025; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8075; 96 Daily Journal DAR 13367



November 4, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding; petition for writ of mandate. Super. Ct. Nos. ZM001828, A928026. Hon. Harold E. Shabo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue directing respondeat superior court to vacate its order of June 12, 1996, which granted real party in interest Myers's motion to dismiss the People's petition for extended commitment, and to make a new and different order denying Myers's motion and reinstating proceedings on the People's petition for involuntary treatment pursuant to section 2970. It is further ordered that the temporary stay issued herein on August 12, 1996, shall remain in effect until respondent complies with our direction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought a writ of mandate and a stay of the order entered by respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which order dismissed the involuntary treatment petition of the state on behalf of the real party in interest, a released convict who was an alleged mentally disordered offender under the Mentally Disordered Offender Law, Cal. Penal Code § 2970.


OVERVIEW: Real party in interest, a released convict who was an alleged mentally disordered offender, filed a motion to dismiss petitioner state's request under the Mentally Disordered Offender Law (MDO), Cal. Penal Code § 2960-§2981, to provide involuntary treatment for him, and the motion was granted by respondent trial court. Petitioner then sought a writ of mandate and a stay of the dismissal order. The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate and directed the trial court to vacate its order because the court concluded that the MDO's extended treatment provisions for parolees had no penal consequences because it was for treatment and protection of the public and was not punitive. The court held that because the MDO expressly required a civil hearing before involuntary treatment and was not punitive, it did not violate U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 nor Cal. Const. art I, § 9's prohibition against ex post facto laws. Finally, the court found that because the proceedings were civil, petitioner had a right to appeal. Therefore, having determined that there was no plain, speedy, and adequate remedy, the court granted the writ of mandate.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that a preemptory writ of mandate issue directing respondent superior court to vacate the order granting real party in interest's motion to dismiss petitioner state's petition for extended commitment. The court further ordered that an order denying real party in interest's motion and reinstating proceedings on petitioner's petition be entered because the Mentally Disordered Law was not an ex post facto law.

City County of San Francisco v. Bullock


No. A068409


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


50 Cal. App. 4th 1738; 58 Cal. Rptr. 2d 482; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1107; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8554; 96 Daily Journal DAR 14158



November 1, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified November 25, 1996. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published November 25, 1996 on Denial of Rehearing, Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1108. Review Denied February 19, 1997 and Reported of Decisions is directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, section 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 813.


PRIOR HISTORY: San Francisco County Superior Court. Super Ct. No. 898704, consolidated with 802676, 809721, 825159, 825717, 847989, 848087, 851156 & 856680. Hon. Donald S. Mitchell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant hotel owner challenged the remand decision of the San Francisco County Superior Court (California), granting summary judgment in favor of appellee city in appellant's action alleging that the Residential Hotel Unit Conversion and Demolition Ordinance amounted to an unconstitutional taking.


OVERVIEW: Appellant hotel owner claimed that the Residential Hotel Unit Conversion and Demolition Ordinance, which affected the conversion of his residential hotel into a tourist hotel, amounted to an unconstitutional taking under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Appellant challenged the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee city, and the court examined whether appellant presented sufficient evidence of infringement of his civil rights to warrant going to a jury trial. The court held that appellant had not presented sufficient evidence to warrant a jury trial and affirmed the trial court's order, holding that the trial court correctly excluded privileged information. Appellant hotel owner moved for reconsideration after the expiration of the time provided, failed to produce sufficient evidence, and failed to establish that appellee acted out of retaliation. The court held that the trial court acted within its discretion in consolidating appellant's pleadings into his cross-complaint.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee city, holding that the trial court correctly excluded privileged information and that appellant hotel owner moved for reconsideration after the expiration of the time provided, failed to produce sufficient evidence, and failed to establish that appellee acted out of retaliation.

 

636 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Western/California, Ltd. v. Dry Creek Joint Elementary School Dist.


No. C020197.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


50 Cal. App. 4th 1461; 58 Cal. Rptr. 2d 220; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1076; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8413; 96 Daily Journal DAR 13883



October 31, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published November 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. CV376367. Hon. John R. Lewis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. The district shall recover its costs on appeal and cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school district challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which found that the imposition of a fee against plaintiff developers violated the monetary limit of former Cal. Gov't. Code § 65996, and thus ordered all such fees refunded. The judgment also directed defendant county to cease requiring payment of these fees as a condition to issuing building permits and certificates of occupancy.


OVERVIEW: In 1986, the legislature authorized school districts to assess fees on development projects to fund school facilities. In lieu of proceeding thereunder, plaintiff developers signed a funding agreement with the county and defendant school district. The agreement, denoting a specific area within the district, provided for issuance of bonds by the county and assessment of taxes to pay therefor. Subsequently, Cal. Gov't. Code § 65995.3 was passed, authorizing school districts to charge developers an additional dollar per square foot on residential building. Plaintiffs challenged defendant's resolution of the charge, claiming it was prohibited by the funding agreement, and that the total assessed exceeded the limit set by Cal. Gov't. Code § 65996. The trial court entered judgment in favor of plaintiffs, and directed issuance of a peremptory writ of mandate commanding defendant to refund the fees paid by plaintiffs. The court reversed and found that the assessment was specifically authorized. and that the statutory limit excluded amounts paid under the funding agreement. Defendant had satisfied the statutory requirement of making a determination of the need and reasonableness of the fee.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that overturned a fee imposed on plaintiff developers by defendant school district because the fee was authorized by statute. A separate fee which plaintiff paid was specifically excluded from the monetary limit that could be imposed.

 

637 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Smith


No. D022102.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


50 Cal. App. 4th 1194; 58 Cal. Rptr. 2d 9; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1056; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8262



October 21, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published November 14, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. SCD102829. Hon. William D. Mudd, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the case remanded to the trial court for further proceedings in accordance with the views expressed in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the people, sought review of a judgment by the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which, at sentencing, struck defendant's two serious/violent felony prior convictions and imposed a determinate sentence pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1385.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to all charges in the information and admitted the alleged prior felony convictions. At sentencing, the trial court struck defendant's two serious/violent felony prior convictions in order to avoid the harsh penalties of the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(i), and imposed a determinate term. Appellant, the people, sought review of the trial court's judgment. On appeal, the court reversed and held that although the trial court had the power under Cal. Penal Code § 1385 to strike serious/violent felony priors in the furtherance of justice, the trial court abused its discretion by failing to state in the minutes its reason for striking the priors as required by § 1385. In addition, the court found that the trial court had further abused its discretion because the trial court struck the defendant's priors on an invalid reason -- its disagreement with the law. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings in accordance with the court's opinion.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment striking two of defendant's prior serious/violent felony convictions and remanded. The court held that the trial court abused its discretion when it struck the prior convictions because it failed to state its reasons in the minutes and because judicial disagreement with the law was not a permissible ground on which the trial court could have made the decision to strike prior felony convictions.

 

638 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Cornelius v. L.A. County Etc. Auth.


No. B094962.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


49 Cal. App. 4th 1761; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 618; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 978; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7712; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12690



October 17, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing November 18, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BC101913. Hon. Dzintra Janavs, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment (entered August 11, 1995) and the post-judgment award of attorney fees (entered October 11, 1995) are reversed and the trial court is directed to enter judgment in favor of defendants on the basis that plaintiff has no standing to pursue his action. The parties to bear their own costs on appeal. The writ of supersedeas issued on December 14, 1995, is to remain in effect until the remittitur has issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant transportation authority sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted summary judgment and attorney fees in favor of plaintiff engineer, found that the Disadvantaged Business Enterprise Program (DBE) was unconstitutional, and enjoined any future activity by defendant under the DBE.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff engineer worked for a company that joined a bid submitted by another construction company to defendant transportation authority. Defendant denied the bid to the construction company because it had not achieved the requisite Disadvantaged Business Enterprise Program (DBEP) commitment. The trial court held that the DBEP was unconstitutional and enjoined defendant from any further activity under the program. The court reversed and held that plaintiff lacked the requisite standing because he had not suffered any actual or imminent injury and that, pursuant to U.S. Const. art. III, the assertion of third party rights could not have conferred standing on him. The court found that plaintiff was not a licensed contractor and failed to show that he was able to bid on contracts but was prevented from doing so by the discriminatory policy under the DBEP. The court also held that plaintiff lacked standing as a taxpayer under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 526a because he was not a resident of Los Angeles County and had not paid real property taxes in that county. The court found that the payment of sales, gasoline, and state income taxes was insufficient to confer standing under § 526a.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment and attorney fees in favor of plaintiff engineer and directed the lower court to enter judgment in favor of defendant transportation authority. The court held that plaintiff, who was not qualified to make the bids that the Disadvantaged Business Enterprise Program allegedly precluded, lacked standing because he failed to show that he had suffered any actual or imminent injury.

 

639 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Williams


No. H013331.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


49 Cal. App. 4th 1632; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 448; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 972; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7629; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12495



October 11, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III. A., III. B., III. D., III. E., III. F., III. H., III. I. and IV.


PRIOR HISTORY: Monterey County Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. S. Ct. 940625. Hon. John M. Phillips.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed. However, the matter is remanded for the court to reconfigure defendant's sentence in accordance with this opinion and the plea agreement.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and sentence of the Monterey County Superior Court (California) entered after he pleaded guilty to three counts of residential burglary and one count of receiving stolen property on the ground that the trial court improperly applied Cal. Penal Code § 667, the three strikes law, in sentencing defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to three counts of residential burglary and one count of receiving stolen property. The trial court found him guilty of a fourth count of residential burglary and also found true prior conviction allegations. The trial court held that defendant's plea established his prior burglary conviction. Defendant claimed that the trial court improperly applied Cal. Penal Code § 667, the three strikes law, because his prior offenses predated the enactment of the law. The court affirmed the judgment on defendant's convictions, but concluded that that the credit limitation in Cal. Penal Code § 667(c)(5) did not apply to terms imposed for offenses committed before enactment of the three strikes law. The prosecution also appealed the judgment, claiming that the court erred in staying a five-year enhancement for a prior serious felony conviction. The court agreed with the prosecution. The court remanded the matter to the trial court to reconfigure defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and remanded the matter for the trial court to reconfigure defendant's sentence in accordance with the opinion and the plea agreement, because the credit limitations in the three strikes law did not apply to terms imposed for offenses committed before the three strikes legislation became effective.
