Garcetti v. Superior Court


No. B103020


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


49 Cal. App. 4th 1533; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 420; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 962; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7588; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12442



October 10, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted February 5, 1997 (S057336), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 634.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Review Dismissed February 16, 2000 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 2d Dist., Div. 2 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 2000 Cal. LEXIS 994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding; petition for writ of mandate. Super. Ct. Nos. ZM001798, ZM001801, ZM001814, ZM001847, ZM001854, ZM001867, ZM001869, ZM001884, ZM001886, ZM001904, ZM001920, ZM001930, ZM001945, ZM001946, ZM001965. Harold E. Shabo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prosecutor filed a petition for a writ of mandate seeking a reexamination of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained ex post facto demurrers of defendants, here, real parties in interest, to the civil commitment petitions filed pursuant to the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq., and ordered defendants' release.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner prosecutor filed civil commitment petitions pursuant to the Sexually Violent Predators Act (SVPA), Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq., against defendants, here, real parties in interest. Defendants filed ex post facto demurrers to the petitions and the trial court sustained the demurrers and ordered defendants release, concluding that the ex post facto clause, Cal. Const. art. I, § 9, rendered the SVPA unenforceable as to all sex offenders whose crimes preceded enactment of the SVPA. Petitioner filed a petition for a writ of mandamus and the court granted the petition. The court found that the trial court, in ruling that the SVPA was unconstitutional, concluded that the authorized commitments constituted additional punishments in violation of the ex post facto clause. The court ruled that such findings could not be made with out factual information and could not, therefore, be answered as a matter of law on demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and ordered the trial court to vacate the order sustaining the ex post facto demurrers to the petitions and instead to overrule those demurrers, to vacate the order for release of the defendants, here, the real parties in interest, and remanded the matter for further proceedings because the constitutionality of the statute under which petitioner prosecutor filed the civil commitment petitions could not be answered on demurer.

 

641 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Pitts v. County of Kern


No. F021678


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


49 Cal. App. 4th 1430; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 471; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 969; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7545; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12321



October 8, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted January 22, 1997 (S057270), Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 267. (See 17 Cal. 4th 340).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Super. Ct. Nos. 215245, 218820. Hon. Stephen P. Gildner, Rebecca A. Wiseman and John I. Kelly, Judges. * 


*  Judge Gildner ruled on pretrial motions, Judge Wiseman ruled on the motion for summary judgment, and Judge Kelly presided at trial.



DISPOSITION: The judgment in favor of County of Kern reversed. In all other respects the judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, accused child molesters, appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which granted summary judgment to defendants, district attorney, employees of the district attorney, and the county, in plaintiffs' claim for civil rights violations pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1988.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, accused child molesters, filed an action against defendants, the district attorney, employees of the district attorney, and the county, for alleged violations of their civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 after their convictions were overturned. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment, finding that defendants had absolute immunity from liability for their alleged misconduct and plaintiffs appealed. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to defendant district attorney because he was entitled to absolute immunity from liability for his alleged deficiencies in training and supervising his employees. Defendants, employees of the district attorney, were entitled to summary judgment on the basis of immunity because their alleged violative conduct fell within the scope of their authority as employees of the district attorney. The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to the county because triable issues of material fact remained as to whether the district attorney was a policy maker for the county and whether his alleged conduct constituted an official policy or custom subjecting the county to liability under §1983.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment to defendant county because issues of material fact remained as to whether defendant district attorney's alleged conduct toward plaintiffs, accused child molesters, constituted an official policy for which immunity would attach. The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of defendants, district attorney and employees of the district attorney, because they were entitled to absolute immunity.

 

642 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Adoption of Haley A.


No. A070920


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


49 Cal. App. 4th 1351; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 361; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 959; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7464; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12289



October 7, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted January 22, 1997 Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 264.
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Review Dismissed May 12, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Cal. LEXIS 2990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Contra Costa Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. 9400055. Hon. Patricia Sepulveda, Judge.

Original Opinion of September 5, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 846.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant birth mother sought review of a judgment of the Contra Costa Superior Court (California), which terminated her parental rights to her child on the grounds of abandonment within the meaning of Cal. Fam. Code § 7822, denied her petition for writ of habeas corpus, and appointed respondents, adoptive parents, temporary guardians of the child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant birth mother gave birth to a child and released the child to respondents, adoptive parents. Appellant never signed an agreement consenting to the child's adoption. Six months later appellant refused to sign the relinquishment papers and requested that the child be returned to her. Respondents filed a petition pursuant to Cal. Fam. Code § 7822 alleging that appellant had abandoned the child on the date of her birth. The trial court concluded that appellant had abandoned the child within the meaning of § 7822 and declared that the best interests of the child would be served by termination of appellant's parental rights. Appellant sought review of the decision. On appeal, the court reversed, concluding that subdivision (d), an amendment to § 7822, which did not specify a period of time within which a birth mother was required to conclusively decide about an adoption, did not change the common law rule that if a birth mother refused to consent to an adoption within six months of the child's placement with the adoptive family, the child was required to have been returned to the birth mother immediately without any consideration of the best interests of the child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the termination of appellant birth mother's parental rights to her child because the common law rule required respondents, adoptive parents, to return of the child to the birth mother without any consideration of the child's best interest where the birth mother refused to consent to the adoption within six months. The court remanded the matter for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

643 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Alcala Co. v. Superior Court


No. D026044.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


49 Cal. App. 4th 1308; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 349; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 936; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7478; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12236



October 7, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Proceedings in mandate after the court granted good faith settlement motion and ruled the settling defendants could stay in the suit as direct defendants. Super. Ct. No. 670058. Hon. Robert E. May, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for writ of mandate is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, general contractor and subcontractors, sought review by writ of mandate of the decision of respondent, the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which granted a good faith settlement motion under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 877.6 in an action by a homeowners' association to recover damages due to construction defects and ruled that the homeowners' association could proceed against settling defendants in the direct action.


OVERVIEW: A homeowners' association (association) filed an action for damages arising out of construction defects. One of two general contractors and the developers (settling defendants) entered into a sliding scale or "Mary Carter" settlement agreement with the association. The trial court granted a good faith motion and ordered the association to proceed against the settling defendants as well as petitioners, general contractor and subcontractors, in the direct action. Petitioners sought review by writ of mandate of the trial court's action, claiming it was an abuse of discretion. The court denied the writ petition and held that petitioners' interests would have been adequately protected by disclosure to the jury of the settlement agreement terms as mandated by Cal. Civ. Proc. § 877.5 (a), (b). The court found that allowing the settling defendants to remain in the direct action permitted the introduction of all relevant evidence and, thus, petitioners could have made motions to limit evidence. The court determined that, contrary to petitioners' contention, there was a justiciable controversy because the jury had to determine the extent of the damages and the existence of any liability.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for the writ of mandate and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it granted a good faith settlement motion and allowed the settling defendants to continue as defendants in the direct action. The court found that adequate disclosure of the settlement agreement terms and the parties' true interests to the jury protected the interests of petitioners, general contractor and subcontractors.

People v. Ridge


No. F024697


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


49 Cal. App. 4th 1275; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 255; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 939; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7436; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12177



October 4, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied January 22, 1997 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Super. Ct. No. SCO62140A. Hon. Roger D. Randall, James M. Stuart and Richard Oberholzer, Judges. * 


* Judge Randall presided at the suppression motion; Judge Stuart presided at appellant's change of plea hearing; Judge Oberholzer sentenced appellant.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the cause remanded to the superior court with directions to grant the motion to suppress and motion to quash.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Kern County (California), which denied his motions to suppress evidence and quash a search warrant in connection with his conviction for receiving a stolen pickup truck, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 496(a).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of receiving a stolen pickup truck in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 496(a). The truck was discovered in a search of defendant's premises after a policeman received permission to conduct the search from state parole authorities. During the course of the search, defendant told the policeman he was no longer on parole, and the search was discontinued. The next day the policeman learned that one of the vehicles he had seen on defendant's premises was reported stolen. The policeman included all the facts in an affidavit in support of a search warrant which was issued and resulted in recovery of the vehicle. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that the parole supervisor was operating as a member of the "law enforcement team," and because the record did not permit a determination that the parole supervisor's conduct was "objectively reasonable," the prosecution had failed to prove that the violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV did not merit the sanction of exclusion. The second search, made with a warrant, was also invalid because it was based on information received from the prior unlawful search.


OUTCOME: The order denying defendant's motions to suppress and quash a search warrant was reversed and the case remanded, because the state parole officer who mistakenly authorized the search was part of the law enforcement team, and the record did not show that his conduct in approving the search was objectively reasonable.

 

645 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Evans


No. E018197.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


49 Cal. App. 4th 1263; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 314; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 940; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7414; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12145



October 3, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Proceeding by way of petition for writ of review or habeas corpus. Super. Ct. No. 271936. Hon. Robert G. Spitzer, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we conclude that the provisions of section 12021, subdivision (c)(3) must be extended to all those who committed qualifying misdemeanors at a time when the offenses were not listed in section 12021, subdivision (c), and thus did not subject them to a firearms prohibition. The judgment of the appellate department is reversed, and the matter is remanded to the municipal court with directions to consider Evans's petition on its merits as brought under subdivision (c)(3).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a convicted misdemeanant, sought review of a decision of the Appellate Department of the Superior Court (California), reversing a trial court's order granting him the right to request relief from the provisions of Cal. Penal Code § 12021(c)(1), which prohibited any person convicted of specified misdemeanors from possessing a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a convicted misdemeanant, filed for relief from the provisions of Cal. Penal Code § 12021(c)(1), which prohibited persons convicted of specified misdemeanors from possessing a firearm. At the time of petitioner's conviction, his offense was not one of the listed misdemeanors in § 12021(c)(1) but it was added by amendment later. Misdemeanants subject to the prohibition fell into three classes: peace officers convicted of certain offenses, any misdemeanant who was convicted before January 1, 1991, and misdemeanants who were convicted after January 1, 1991. Persons in the first two categories could have sought relief from the firearms prohibition pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 12021(c)(3) but those in the third category, such as petitioner, could not. On appeal, the court reversed and held that the statute violated the equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 7(a) because the classifications were not rationally related to a legitimate public purpose. The court extended the relief avenue provided by the statute to all those who committed qualifying misdemeanors at a time when their offenses were not listed in Cal. Penal Code § 12021(c).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order reversing the decision allowing petitioner, a convicted misdemeanant, to seek relief from a statute prohibiting him from possessing a firearm because the classifications set forth in the statute violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment in that they were not rationally related to any legitimate government purpose.

People v. Cepeda


No. B091112.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


49 Cal. App. 4th 1235; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 246; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 937; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7388; 96 Daily Journal DAR 12093



October 2, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. NA021832. Hon. James B. Pierce, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed, but the matter is remanded for the trial court to state its reasons in the minute order for the dismissal of prior convictions in conformity with Penal Code section 667, subdivision (f)(2) and Penal Code section 1385.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which entered a judgment of conviction following his negotiated plea of no contest to possessing a controlled substance, with his admissions that he had one strike, per Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(i), and two prior felony convictions for which he had served separate prison terms, per Cal. Penal Code, § 667.5(b).


OVERVIEW: In exchange for defendant's plea of no contest, allegations of two prior residential burglary strikes and two prior prison term enhancements were to be stricken. Defendant entered a plea and was sentenced to the second strike sentence he was promised. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and refused to set aside the plea agreement because defendant received the benefit of the bargain he negotiated, an eight-year sentence as a second strike offender rather than an indeterminate life term as a third strike offender, and the plea bargain accomplished everything defendant could have hoped for had the trial court exercised its own discretion. The court found that defendant's sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment, and was not grossly disproportionate to the current offense, given his individual circumstances and criminal history. The court remanded for the sole purpose of permitting the trial court to indicate in writing in the minute order whether defendant's two prior residential burglary strikes were dismissed for insufficient evidence or in furtherance of justice, and, if the latter, to comply with the requirements of Cal. Penal Code § 1385.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's sentencing of defendant in accordance with the terms of a negotiated plea agreement because defendant was sentenced as a second strike rather than third strike offender, received the exact sentence he had negotiated, and the sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment. The court remanded so the trial court could state its reasons in the minute order for the dismissal of two prior convictions.

People v. Superior Court (Cain)


Nos. A074501, A074644, A075283


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


49 Cal. App. 4th 1164; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 296; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 931; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7341; 96 Daily Journal DAR 120331



October 1, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified October 16, 1996. Review Granted February 5, 1997 (S057272).
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.
Review Dismissed February 16, 2000 and cause remanded to the Ct. App., 1st Dist., Div. 5 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 2000 Cal. LEXIS 993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco. Super. Ct. Nos. 105531, 123931, 148257/120513 & 15808, 110306, 121966, & 106061, Nos. 98595, 108809 & 131587. Alex Saldamando and Lucy Kelly McCabe, Judges.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought writ review of the orders of respondent, the Superior Court of the County of San Francisco (California), which dismissed petitions for civil commitment under the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq., of 10 prisoners, real parties in interest, who had been convicted of sexually violent felonies and were about to complete their criminal sentences.


OVERVIEW: The state petitioned to have 10 prisoners civilly committed as sexually violent predators under the Sexually Violent Predators Act (Act), Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 6600 et seq. The prisoners, real parties in interest, moved to dismiss the petitions on the basis that the Act was an ex post facto law as it allowed for physical confinement beyond the length of their criminal sentences. Respondent trial court dismissed the petitions, ruling that the Act was unconstitutional because it did not require amenability to treatment as a precondition to commitment, rendering the confinement punitive rather than curative. The state petitioned for a writ of mandate challenging respondent's dismissal. The court granted the peremptory writ, holding that the Act was not an ex post facto law. The court held that the Act was not retroactive because it did not increase the sentence for the prisoners' original sex offenses. The Act was not penal because it imposed a mental health commitment for a present diagnosed mental illness, which was that the predator would likely commit future sexually violent offenses. The court ruled that amenability was irrelevant to the predator determination.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's request for a writ of mandate and directed respondent trial court to set aside its orders dismissing the commitment petitions against 10 prisoners, real parties in interest, and to proceed pursuant to the Sexually Violent Predators Act (Act), because the Act was not an ex post facto law as it did not retroactively increase the prisoners' criminal sentences and was curative, not penal, in nature.

 

648 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Cunningham


No. C021056.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


49 Cal. App. 4th 1044; 57 Cal. Rptr. 2d 179; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 922; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7317; 96 Daily Journal DAR 11997



September 30, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II through V of the Discussion.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. 95F01889. Hon. Gerald S. Bakarich, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which convicted him of petty theft with a prior in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 666 and sentenced him under the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code §§ 667, 1170.12.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with petty theft with a prior under Cal. Penal Code § 666. The complaint also alleged a prior strike under the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code §§ 667, 1170.12. Defendant filed a motion to strike the prior offense allegation pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1385, which was denied by the trial court. Defendant then pled guilty to the petty-theft-with-a-prior charge and submitted the truth or falsity of the prior conviction to the trial court. It was stipulated that if the prior conviction was found true, defendant would be sentenced pursuant to the three strikes law. The trial court found the prior strike allegation to be true and sentenced defendant under the three strikes law. On appeal, the court affirmed because defendant expressly agreed to the imposition of a sentence under the three strikes law. Defendant's express agreement precluded a remand for the purpose of obtaining a lesser term by virtue of the striking of the prior offense because the trial court was bound to enforce the plea bargain and the appropriate sentence within the limits of the bargain.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's sentencing under the three strikes law because defendant expressly agreed to a plea bargain and was sentenced according to the plea bargain. The negotiated plea precluded a remand to strike the prior offense because the trial court was bound to enforce the plea bargain.

 

649 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Thomsen v. City of Escondido


No. D025853.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


49 Cal. App. 4th 884; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 902; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 912; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7257; 96 Daily Journal DAR 11851



September 26, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from an order of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. N70263. Hon. Lisa Guy-Schall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order granting the preliminary injunction is affirmed, with such further proceedings to take place as are required to enter a final judgment consistent with the principles set forth in this opinion. Thomsen is awarded costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which preliminarily enjoined appellant from enforcing Escondido, Cal., Mun. Code § 29-101 et seq., that regulated rents charged for space in mobilehome parks, in respondent mobilehome park owner's action for declaratory relief and an injunction.


OVERVIEW: Respondent mobilehome park owner filed an action against appellant city for declaratory relief and an injunction to restrain appellant from enforcing an ordinance that regulated mobilehome park owners entering into rental space agreements with prospective purchasers of mobilehomes. The trial court entered a preliminary injunction against appellant. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that Proposition K, Escondido, Cal., Mun. Code § 29-101 et seq., had not prohibited mobilehome park owners from charging prospective purchasers rents exceeding those permitted for current tenants. Proposition K, which regulated rents charged for space in mobilehome parks, was adopted by the voters of Escondido by a ballot initiative measure. The court found that Proposition K was intended to deal with rent increases for current tenants, not prospective tenants, and that Proposition K had not either expressly or impliedly provided for the continued regulation of rents at the current tenant's level upon sale or transfer of the mobilehome. The trial court properly enjoined appellant from enforcing Proposition K against respondent in situations involving prospective purchasers of mobile homes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's preliminary injunction in favor of respondent mobilehome park owner against appellant city, in respondent's action seeking to enjoin appellant from enforcing an ordinance that regulated rents charged for space in mobilehome parks. The court held that the ordinance did not limit respondent's right to negotiate mutually agreeable rent spaces with prospective purchasers of mobilehomes.

 

650 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Askey


No. B097733.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


49 Cal. App. 4th 381; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 782; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 869; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6951; 96 Daily Journal DAR 11326



September 16, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. KA026560. Hon. Alfonso M. Bazan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is modified to impose the stayed five-year term on the prior serious felony conviction under section 667, subdivision (a)(1), and, as so modified, affirmed. The trial court is directed to prepare a new abstract of judgment incorporating the modification, and to forward a copy of the new abstract to the Department of Corrections.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment entered by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found that defendant had suffered three prior serious felony convictions within the meaning of the Three Strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667, and sentenced defendant to a term of 25 years to life in state prison, after his conviction of attempted first degree burglary under Cal. Penal Code § 664.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted first degree burglary under Cal. Penal Code § 664. During the sentencing phase, the trial court considered defendant's 13 prior felony convictions stemming from a previous case as separate incidents and imposed a term of life to 25 years. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the Three Strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667, did not require that defendant's prior convictions be brought and tried separately. The court ruled that the Three Strikes law was not unconstitutional because the manner in which prior convictions were determined was not ambiguous, and defendant had adequate notice of the punishment to be imposed in his case. The sentence imposed by the trial court was not unconstitutionally disproportionate because it was not imposed solely for defendant's current offense, but was based on his status as a repeat offender. The court modified the judgment to impose the five-year enhancement pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667(a)(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for attempted first degree burglary, and modified the judgment to impose a five-year enhancement under the Three Strikes law, because defendant's sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment, and the Three Strikes law was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

651 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Snook


No. D021913


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


49 Cal. App. 4th 289; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 630; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 863; 96 Daily Journal DAR 11196; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6881



September 12, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review or Rehearing granted, Depublished: People v. Snook, 1996 Cal. LEXIS 7158 (Cal. 1996).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. SCD101291. Hon. Linda S. Quinn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), which convicted him for driving under the influence per Cal. Vehicle Code § 23152(a), driving while having .08 percent or more blood alcohol per Cal. Veh. Code § 23152(b), and driving with a suspended license per Cal. Veh. Code § 14601.1. The charges were enhanced from misdemeanors to felonies pursuant to Cal. Veh. § 14601.1.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in April 1994 with violations of Cal. Veh. Code §§ 23152(a), (b), and § 14601.1, for drunk driving and driving with a suspended driver's license, which occurred in April 1992. Defendant also admitted to Cal. Veh. Code § 23175, a penalty enhancement statute, of having been convicted on October 1992, January 1994, and February 1994 of drunk driving incidents. The court affirmed the trial court's convictions in part and reversed in part. The court concluded that the legislature intended § 23175 to adopt the rule that penalties for subsequent offenses can be increased based on earlier offenses even if the subsequent offenses occurred before conviction on the earlier offenses. Based on this conclusion, the court reversed and held § 23175 unconstitutional as an ex post facto law as applied in this case because this case involved the increase of penalty due to events occurring subsequent to the crime.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and sentences for drunk driving in part, holding that the enhancement statute did not permit subsequent offenses and convictions to be used to increase the penalty for the first offense, and remanded the matter to the trial court for resentencing.

 

652 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Davidson v. County of San Diego


No. D021478.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


49 Cal. App. 4th 639; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 617; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 890; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7107; 96 Daily Journal DAR 11592



September 10, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published September 19, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. 667421. Hon. J. Michael Bollman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the matter is remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the issue of whether the County's major use permit and 650-foot setback requirements were sufficiently necessary to the public welfare to justify impairment of Davidson's vested rights. Davidson to bear costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants County of San Diego, Board of Supervisors of San Diego County (California) and director of the county's department of planning and land use sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County in favor of respondent permit applicant, directing the county to process respondent's application for a permit to build a crematorium under regulations effective when he applied.


OVERVIEW: Appellant county sought review of a superior court judgment in favor of respondent permit applicant, directing the county to process respondent's application for a building permit for a crematorium under the regulations effective when the application was made. The court of appeal concluded the trial court erred because respondent's vested rights could be impaired by subsequent police power enactments where reasonably necessary to protect the health and safety of the public. The determination of whether respondent had vested rights was to be made as of the time he applied for the building permit. The clear language of the San Diego County Zoning Ordinance § 1019a showed it was intended to confer the vested right to have a building permit application reviewed and considered in light of the regulations existing on the date of application. A governmental entity could not, through contract or legislation, abdicate its police power.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded to the trial court for a new trial on the issue of whether appellant county's major use permit and 650-foot setback requirements were sufficiently necessary to the public welfare to justify impairment of respondent's vested rights in applying for a building permit for a crematorium.

 

653 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Adoption of Haley A.


No. A070920


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


48 Cal. App. 4th 1858; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 505; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 846; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6727; 96 Daily Journal DAR 11663



September 5, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Granted October 7, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 952. Rehearing Opinion October 7, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 959. Rewiew Granted January 22, 1997 (S057197).


PRIOR HISTORY: Contra Costa Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. 9400055. Hon. Patricia Sepulveda, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment for respondent adoptive parents from the Contra Costa Superior Court (California), challenging the trial court's termination of her parental rights based on a finding of abandonment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a judgment terminating appellant mother's parental rights to the minor child, concluding that, although appellant refused to consent to the adoption, she did so one day after expiration of six months from release of the child to respondent adoptive parents. On review, appellant contended that the trial court erred in finding that she abandoned her child. Specifically, appellant contended that because she refused to consent to the adoption within six months of the child's placement with respondent adoptive parents and requested the child be returned to her, she could not be found to have abandoned the child within the meaning of Cal. Fam. Code § 7822. The court agreed with appellant's argument and reversed the decision. The trial court's finding that appellant intended to abandon her child was not supported by substantial evidence. To the contrary, the court found that appellant asserted her refusal to consent to the adoption before expiration of period provided in § 7822, and followed this refusal to consent with reasonable action to recover custody of the child.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment for respondent adoptive parents and remanded based on its holding that appellant mother asserted her refusal to consent to adoption within the statutory limitations period and followed her refusal with reasonable action to recover custody of her child.

 

654 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



County of L.A. v. Ralph V.


No. B088907.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


48 Cal. App. 4th 1840; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 558; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 839; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6659; 96 Daily Journal DAR 10849



September 4, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. Nos. BD116385. & BD118312. Hon. F. Filmore Jaffe, Temporary Judge. (Pursuant to Cal. Const., art. VI, § 21.)



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed. The cases are remanded for further proceedings as required by this decision. The parties shall bear their own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of the judgments of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which required appellants, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §903, to reimburse respondent county for the cost of the child support provided to their minor son while he was confined as a ward of the juvenile court.


OVERVIEW: Following the release of appellant parents' minor son from juvenile custody, the trial court, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code §903, granted respondent county recovery of the cost of child support provided to appellants' minor son during his confinement. Thereafter, appellants sought review, contending that such recovery was invalid because the trial court did not require respondent to itemize and prove the particular components of the support. On review, the court affirmed the judgments. The court found that respondent had complied with the constitutional limitations on governmental assessment of support from parents of juvenile court wards. The court noted that such assessments were constitutional in that parents could be required to reimburse the cost of support provided to children as distinguished from the costs of incarceration and that respondent no longer needed to affirmatively demonstrate the components of the charges or to itemize them. However, the court remanded for further proceedings for the trial court to order respondent to render an accounting of the costs of support to ensure compliance with the law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments in favor of respondent county's recovery of the cost of the child support provided to appellant parents' minor child because such recovery was constitutional, and because respondent was no longer required to demonstrate the components of the charges or to itemize the charges. However, the court remanded for further proceedings for the trial court to order respondent to give an accounting of the costs of support.

People v. Halgren


No. D023600.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


52 Cal. App. 4th 1223; 61 Cal. Rptr. 2d 176; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 1224; 97 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1236; 97 Daily Journal DAR 1825



September 3, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Supreme Court from Unpublished to Published February 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. SCD107843. Robert C. Coates, Judge. * 


* Judge of the San Diego Superior Court, assigned by the Chief Justice pursuant to article VI, section 6 of the California Constitution.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment convicting him of felony stalking, Cal. Penal Code § 646.9. The Superior Court of San Diego County (California) had sentenced defendant to five years' probation with credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed a judgment convicting him of felony stalking in violation Cal. Penal Code § 646.9. The court of appeal affirmed. Cal. Penal Code § 646.9 was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant, who threatened and repeatedly harassed a woman he did not know. Defendant's statements to the victim were not equivocal and vague and were not protected under U.S. Const. amend. I. Rather, the statements constituted a credible threat and that term was not unconstitutionally vague: the statute provided sufficient notice of the conduct prohibited. Section 646.9 was not overbroad and was sufficiently narrowly tailored to survive constitutional scrutiny.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of felony stalking. The felony stalking statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant. Defendant's statements constituted a credible threat and that term was not unconstitutionally vague: the statute provided sufficient notice of the conduct prohibited.

 

656 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tavernetti


No. C020794


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


48 Cal. App. 4th 1621; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 423; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 826; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6529; 96 Daily Journal DAR 10659



August 29, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied December 11, 1996 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Colusa County. Super. Ct. No. CR31025. Hon. S. William Abel, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of conviction from the Superior Court of Colusa County (California). Defendant also challenged the trial court's decision to enhance his sentence by three consecutive five-year terms for each serious felony conviction, and a one-year term for each of four prison term enhancements under the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(a).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that defendant incurred three serious felony convictions pursuant to the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code §§ 667(d) and (e). He was sentenced to a consecutive 19-year term consisting of a five-year term for each of the three serious felony convictions and a one-year term for each of the four-prison term enhancements. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in imposing five-year enhancements for the three serious felony convictions because the prosecutor failed to plead and prove them under Cal. Penal Code § 667(a). The court found that defendant received notice of each fact required for imposition of an enhanced term under § 667(a). Further, the requisite factual allegations to establish a serious felony conviction under § 667(a) were both pleaded and proven. However, the court concluded that defendant correctly contended that his three serious felony convictions were not brought and tried separately under § 667(a). Therefore, only one five-year term could be imposed. Accordingly, the judgment was modified to strike two of the five-year terms imposed under § 667(a). As modified, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The enhanced sentence imposed by the trial court was erroneous. Accordingly, the court struck two of the five-year terms and two of the one-year terms imposed under the three strikes law, and modified the term imposed on the remaining enhancement from one year to three years. As modified, the judgment was affirmed.

Community Memorial Hospital v. County of Ventura


No. B095022.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


50 Cal. App. 4th 199; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 732; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 888; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7021; 96 Daily Journal DAR 11427



August 20, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* This opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part III.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified September 18, 1996. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published September 18, 1996.
In the Advance Report of the case reported at 49 Cal. App. 4th 527, there was a publishers error, part IV of the opinion was inadvertently omitted. The Opinion was reprinted at the above citation (50 Cal. App. 4th 199) to include part IV.
Review Denied November 13, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 6394.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County of Ventura. Super. Ct. No. 146407. Hons. Frederick Jones, Judge and Richard w. Abbe, Judge * 


*  Retired Justice of the Court of Appeal assigned by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Costs are awarded to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, private hospital and taxpayers, sought review of an order of the Superior Court County of Ventura (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendant county in plaintiffs' lawsuit to enjoin unlawful and unfair competition by public hospitals for paying patients, and violations of Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17000 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, private hospital and taxpayers, sought review of an order granting summary judgment in favor of defendant county. The court held that nothing in the language of Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1008 prohibited the trial court from reconsidering a motion overruling a demurrer. Regarding the merits of the case, pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code. § 14000.2, defendant was authorized by the legislature to treat paying patients at public hospitals. And, although defendant's policy of treating paying patients had the effect of creating competition with plaintiff private hospital, that policy did not exceed defendant's police power. Furthermore, that practice did not constitute a gift of public funds because the expenditure of money to promote health was an expenditure for a public purpose. Finally, the court held that defendant was not a person subject to suit under the Unfair Practices Act, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §17000 et seq., or the unfair competition statute, Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code §17200 et seq. for acts relating to the operation of its public hospital. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment because defendant county's policy of accepting paying patients at its public hospital was authorized by the legislature, did not exceed defendant's police powers, and did not constitute a gift of public funds. The court also held that defendant was not a person subject to suit under the Unfair Practices Act or the unfair competition statute for acts relating to the operation of its public hospital.

 

658 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Conservatorship of O'Connor


No. A066822.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


48 Cal. App. 4th 1076; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 386; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 782; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6194; 96 Daily Journal DAR 10219; 96 Daily Journal DAR 10529



August 19, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of San Francisco County. Super. Ct. Nos. 238499, Super. Ct. No. 948278. Hon. Leighton Hatch, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed, and the trial court directed to enter a new judgment consistent with the foregoing. Costs on appeal are awarded to appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administrator challenged an order of the Superior Court of San Francisco County (California), which absolved respondent surety company of liability for damage to a conservatorship estate caused by an attorney appointed as the conservator for the estate.


OVERVIEW: Appellant administrator challenged a judgment favoring respondent surety company, which absolved respondent of liability for damage to a conservatorship estate by an attorney appointed to act as successor conservator for the estate. After the attorney was found to have embezzled from the estate property, appellant filed a claim for a surety bond issued by respondent. Respondent denied the bond on grounds that the appointment by the probate court of the attorney was invalid. Ultimately, the dispute was heard by the trial court which declared void the order appointing the attorney as conservator for the estate and rescinded the bond issued by respondent guaranteeing the attorney's performance. On appeal the court reversed, holding that the order appointing the attorney as successor conservator was not void and that respondent was precluded from challenging its validity. The procedural irregularities which occurred in the course of the appointment did not deprive the probate court of subject matter jurisdiction over the estate. Respondent manifested its consent to the procedure by which the attorney was appointed conservator and therefore was estopped from challenging the appointment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order which declared void the order of the probate court appointing an attorney as conservator for the estate. The court held that the appointment was not void and that respondent surety company was not entitled to recission of the bond guaranteeing the attorney's performance in favor of appellant administrator, where it had manifested its consent to the appointment and was precluded from challenging it.

Gilliam v. Moreno Valley Unified Sch. Dist.


No. E014979.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


48 Cal. App. 4th 518; 55 Cal. Rptr. 2d 695; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 772; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6076; 96 Daily Journal DAR 9893



August 13, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied October 30, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 6279.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court of Riverside County. Super. Ct. No. 249990. Hon. Richard G. Van Frank, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. The District shall recover its costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-principal sought review of a decision of the Superior Court, Riverside County (California), which denied his petition for writ of mandate seeking reinstatement as principal of a school administered by respondent school district.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was hired as principal by respondent school district. This was his first employment by respondent, thus, he was a probationary employee. On March 11, 1994, respondent sent appellant a letter notifying him that it had determined not to reelect him; his employment was to terminate at the end of the academic year. In a separate letter, appellant was notified of a new assignment as a Principal on Assignment. Appellant immediately reported that he was sick and would be unable to return to work until July 3, 1994. The employment year ended June 30, 1994. Appellant filed a petition for writ of mandate alleging that he did not receive proper notice of his nonreelection or of his transferred assignment as required by Cal. Educ. Code § 44951. The trial court found the statute to be inapplicable and denied his petition. The court affirmed, finding that respondent properly noticed appellant's non-reelection pursuant to Cal. Educ. Code § 44929.21 because appellant was a probationary employee. The court found that Cal. Educ. Code § 44951 did not apply and that respondent's notice of non-reelection was timely and provided appellant with the appropriate notice of his non-reelection.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed on the basis that respondent school district's notice of non-reelection was timely and provided appellant ex-principal with the appropriate notice of his non-reelection. The applicable statute section relating to appellant's non-reelection required notice by March 15. Respondent properly noticed appellant's non-reelection on March 11, 1994, and therefore, his non-reelection notice was timely.

 

660 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Antoine


No. D023183.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


48 Cal. App. 4th 489; 56 Cal. Rptr. 2d 530; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 770; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6050; 96 Daily Journal DAR 9841



August 12, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. 1 


1 Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of Discussion parts B., C. and D.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. SCD106400. Hon. Linda B. Quinn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction from the Superior Court, San Diego County (California) of carjacking, assault with a deadly weapon, robbery, unlawful vehicle taking, and possession of a firearm by a felon.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of carjacking, assault with a deadly weapon, robbery, unlawful vehicle taking, and possession of a firearm by a felon. In affirming the convictions, the court held that the crime of carjacking did not create a potential for the punishment of protected conduct. The reason for a special carjacking statute, with a penalty greater than that for second-degree robbery, was that carjacking was a particularly serious crime that victimized persons in vulnerable settings. Cal. Penal Code § 215 gave notice that it did not supplant Cal. Penal Code § 211, and depending on the facts and the discretion of the prosecutor, a carjacking could result in charges of both carjacking and robbery. Section 215 was not void for vagueness because it defined the number of offenses committed when the vehicle was taken from both a possessor and a passenger. There was specifically no denial of equal protection because every similarly situated defendant charged with those offenses could face the same charging, convicting, and sentencing options.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions, holding there was no impediment to convictions of carjacking and robbery that arose from the same act because neither was a necessarily lesser-included offense of the other. The court ruled that there was no denial of equal protection because every similarly situated defendant charged with those offenses could face the same charging, convicting, and sentencing options.

 

661 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tritchler


No. D021748


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


48 Cal. App. 4th 367; 55 Cal. Rptr. 2d 650; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 776; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6015; 96 Daily Journal DAR 9788



August 9, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied November 20, 1996 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from judgments of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. SF83242. Hons. Jesus Rodriguez and Philip D. Sharp, Judges.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed, sentences vacated and case remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Co-defendants challenged their convictions in connection with the possession of destructive devices in the Superior Court of San Diego County (California), alleging the trial court should have suppressed their statements to the police and that their sentences constituted cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: Co-defendants were convicted in the trial court on numerous charges in connection with an incident in which they possessed, transported, and then threw an explosive device at a third party, who was not injured. Defendants sought review, alleging first that their statements to the police should have been suppressed because they did not fall within the "public safety" exception to the Miranda rule. The court affirmed conviction, holding that the evidence of the explosion, the unknown nature of the devices found hidden under the car seats, and the necessity of further handling of the devices justified questioning defendants without first informing them of their Miranda rights. Defendants also argued their two-year prison term constituted cruel and unusual punishment in violation of the state and federal constitutions. The court agreed and reversed the sentence. It noted that defendants testified they did not know the rockets were potentially destructive because they were small in size and they believed they were fireworks. Furthermore, defendants could have been prosecuted under a different statute that would have resulted in misdemeanor charges and probation.


OUTCOME: Co-defendants' convictions on charges related to the explosive devices were affirmed because the police were justified in questioning defendants before complying with the Miranda rule; defendants' sentences were reversed and remanded because the mandatory two-year prison term constituted cruel and unusual punishment.

 

662 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Honig


No. C015357.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


48 Cal. App. 4th 289; 55 Cal. Rptr. 2d 555; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 755; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5920; 96 Daily Journal DAR 9647



August 7, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. CR111247. Hon. James L. Long, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The condition of probation that defendant pay restitution is set aside and the cause remanded to the trial court with directions to exercise its discretion in determining whether to impose restitution as a condition of probation and, if so, to determine whether the state has suffered a loss and then redetermine the amount of any restitution. In all other respects the judgment of conviction and the order of probation are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant elected state official appealed from a judgment of conviction and an order of probation entered by the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California) pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1237(a), after a jury found appellant guilty of four counts of making official contracts in which he had a financial interest in violation of Cal. Gov't Code §§ 1090, 1097.


OVERVIEW: Appellant elected state official participated in the forming of state contracts in which he had a financial interest through the Department of Education, which financially benefited a non-profit organization employing his spouse. Appellant was clearly financially interested in his spouse's employment and remuneration by the organization, and was convicted of violating Cal. Gov't Code §§ 1090, 1097, upon which the trial court ordered probation. Appellant challenged the conviction and order, contending that the trial court erred in its jury instructions, that the contracts were grants beyond the scope of the charged crimes, and that the Attorney General lacked authority to prosecute this action. The court affirmed the judgment and order, but remanded the cause directing the trial court to use its discretion in determining whether to impose restitution. The trial court fully and fairly instructed the jury on all elements of the charged offenses. There was ample evidence to support the transactions as contracts, not grants. The Attorney General was within his discretion to prosecute the action because he felt that state law would otherwise not be adequately enforced in any county.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and probation order, remanding the cause to the trial court to exercise its discretion in determining whether to impose restitution. The trial court fully and fairly instructed the jury on all elements of the charged offenses, including the requirement that appellant must have known he had a financial interest in the contracts, and did not give a contradictory instruction on the required mental elements.

City of San Diego v. Rider


No. D025921.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


47 Cal. App. 4th 1473; 55 Cal. Rptr. 2d 422; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 738; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5710; 96 Daily Journal DAR 9301



July 30, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of San Diego County. Super. Ct. No. 697147. Hon. Judith McConnell, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Parties to bear their own costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, city and financing authority, in a case concerning whether a lease-back financing arrangement to fund improvements to a stadium was valid under Cal. Const. art. XVI, § 18.


OVERVIEW: Appellant electors challenged the superior court judgment, which validated a lease-back financing arrangement to fund improvements to a stadium. The financing arrangement was being effected without a two-thirds vote of the qualified electorate as provided in the Cal. Const. art. XVI, § 18. The arrangement included a ground lease, bond issuance, and a facility lease. Respondents filed an action in superior court seeking validation of the leases, bonds, and related ordinances and resolutions. The superior court held that respondents established that the lease fell within the well-established contingent-payment exception to the constitutional limitation on indebtedness of a city. The superior court also found that respondents were not constrained in the issuance of bonds by the provisions of the city charter. On appeal the court concluded that the provision allowing respondent agency to relet the stadium would not convert respondent city's obligation to pay rent into a prohibited debt under article XVI, section 18, when it was not previously a prohibited debt because respondent city continues to receive consideration. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court judgment that held that respondents, city and financing agency, established that the lease fell within the well-established contingent-payment exception to the constitutional limitation on indebtedness of a city, holding that the reletting of the stadium did not turn respondent city's obligation to pay rent into a constitutionally prohibited debt.

 

664 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Donohue v. Santa Paula West Mobile Home Park


No. B099368.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


47 Cal. App. 4th 1168; 55 Cal. Rptr. 2d 282; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 720; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5615; 96 Daily Journal DAR 9132



July 29, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court County of Ventura. Super. Ct. No. 146761. Hon. Joe D. Hadden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Section 66427.5 does not apply under the circumstances presented here. The initiative is constitutional on its face. Accordingly, the judgment is reversed. Costs to appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant residents of a mobilehome park sought review of the decision rendered by the Superior Court of Ventura County (California) which entered judgment in favor of respondents in a case concerning rent regulation.


OVERVIEW: This case involved a failed attempt by appellant residents of a mobilehome park to convert the park to resident ownership and respondent owners' subsequent attempt to increase rents to the level allowed under Cal. Gov't Code § 66427.5. The trial court found that § 66427.5 applied whenever a subdivider filed a tentative map to convert a rental park to resident ownership, even if the conversion did not occur. Thus, the trial court found that § 66427.5 regulated rents at the park and preempted contrary provisions in an initiative. Accordingly, it entered judgment in favor of respondents, city, the park, and the park's owners and managers. The court rejected respondents' argument that appellants' claims were barred under Cal. Gov't Code § 66499.3 because they failed to challenge the tentative map within 90 days after its approval. The court also stated that respondents only raised a facial challenge to the initiative. They did not claim that the initiative had been applied in a manner that denied respondents a fair return on their investment. As a result, the record contained no evidence concerning respondent city's willingness to grant respondent park a rent increase.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling of the trial court where it was proven that an initiative to regulate the rent increase of mobilehome lots was valid on its face. The initiative did not violate any statutory rules, and there was no evidence that the exclusion of land acquisition costs would deprive respondent owners of a fair return.

 

665 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dingman


No. H013433


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


47 Cal. App. 4th 1068; 55 Cal. Rptr. 2d 211; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 710; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5541; 96 Daily Journal DAR 8983



July 25, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted October 2, 1996 (S056079), Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 7356.
Reprinted without change in the January 2000 Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Court.
Review Dismissed September 27, 2000 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 6th Dist. (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 2000 Cal. LEXIS 7505.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Santa Clara County. Super. Ct. No. 172660. Joseph F. Biafore, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which convicted defendant of possession of an unregistered assault rifle, in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 12280(b), and sentenced him to three years' formal probation, with conditions of community service work and various fines.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of violating Cal. Penal Code § 12280(b), possession of an unregistered assault rifle, and sentenced him to three years' formal probation. Defendant claimed that his weapon was not prohibited because, when correctly interpreted, Cal. Penal Code § 12276(a)(11) referred to an assault weapon manufactured with a detachable magazine. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that defendant's weapon was prohibited because the plain meaning of § 12276(a)(11) indicated that it was applicable to an assault weapon with a detachable magazine, whether manufactured as part of the weapon or otherwise attachable. The court followed the plain meaning of the Assault Weapons Control Act, Cal. Penal Code § 12275 et seq., because the legislative purpose of restricting firearms with a high rate of fire and capacity for firepower was clear, and assault weapons were the evil the legislature had attempted to control. Because an ordinary person of reasonable intelligence, or anyone familiar with gun parlance, would have known that defendant's weapon was prohibited under Cal. Penal Code § 12276(a)(11), the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of possession of an unregistered assault rifle, holding that the weapon defendant possessed was statutorily prohibited, as indicated by the plain meaning of the Assault Weapons Control Act (AWCA). The AWCA was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

666 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Willon


No. H015032.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


47 Cal. App. 4th 1080; 55 Cal. Rptr. 2d 245; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 718; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5564; 96 Daily Journal DAR 9041; 24 Media L. Rep. 2121



July 25, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Santa Clara County Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. 186000. Hon. Thomas C. Hastings, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a reporter and news director of a local television station, challenged a judgment of the Santa Clara County Superior Court (California), holding petitioners in contempt for refusing to disclose their source. Petitioners requested a writ of habeas corpus or certiorari on the ground that they were immunized them from contempt under the shield law, Cal. Const. art. I, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners, a reporter and news director of a local television station, sought relief from contempt after they refused to disclose their source that provided information about a pending criminal prosecution in violation of a protective gag order. The action stemmed from a trial involving an accused killer charged with a child's murder. Respondent court issued a protective order prohibiting the release to the public of evidence that had not been ruled admissible and any comments about gathered evidence. Petitioners broadcast a report regarding accused's videotaped confession and details regarding the investigation. Petitioners argued that the shield law, Cal. Const. art. I, § 2, immunized them from contempt. Respondent court maintained that the contempt order was necessary to deter future violations and to protect accused's right to a fair trial. The appellate court granted petitioners' request for a writ of habeas corpus or certiorari and annulled the contempt judgment, because the shield law protected petitioners from contempt absent a specific showing that nondisclosure of the source created a substantial probability of injury to accused criminal's right to a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was annulled. Petitioners, a reporter and news director of a local television station, were entitled to a writ of habeas corpus or certiorari, because the shield law immunized them from contempt based on their news media status. It was unlikely that the failure to identify petitioners' source would facilitate additional leaks to jeopardize the fairness of the accused's trial.

 

667 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cortez


B093691


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


47 Cal. App. 4th 828; 54 Cal. Rptr. 2d 841; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 713; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 5394; 96 Daily Journal DAR 8749



July 19, 1996, FILED


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified July 23, 1996. Review Granted October 16, 1996 (S055733), Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 5794. (See 18 Cal. 4th 1223)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. BA067687. Jacqueline A. Connor, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of conspiracy to commit murder and imposed an enhanced sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to 25 years to life for conspiracy to commit murder, with an additional year for an arming enhancement. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed. The court held that the trial court properly declined to direct the jury to determine the degree of murder that defendant conspired to commit, because such a determination could have had only one legally correct outcome -- first degree murder. The definition of murder included in the attempted murder instruction was sufficient to communicate the necessity of finding specific intent to kill and it was unnecessary to instruct on the mental states of premeditation and deliberation or to distinguish the implied and express malice charges. The court found that the trial court had no sua sponte duty to link its instructions on withdrawal and the burden of proof. The court held that withdrawal was not a viable defense because defendant had already completed the overt act of conspiracy when he agreed to kill a gang member, got into a stolen car with a loaded handgun, and attempted to enlist other gang members in the plan.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for conspiracy to commit first degree murder because the trial court properly declined to instruct the jury to determine the degree of murder where defendant could not be guilty of conspiracy to commit unpremeditated or second degree murder.
