People v. Washington


No. A070166


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


44 Cal. App. 4th 162; 51 Cal. Rptr. 2d 618; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 304; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2366; 96 Daily Journal DAR 3939



April 4, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied July 11, 1996 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 3980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Francisco County. Super. Ct. No. 134124. Hon. Honorable Alex Saldamando, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of San Francisco County (California), that continued his involuntary mental health treatment under Cal. Penal Code § 2960 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant contended that extension of his involuntary mental health treatment under Cal. Penal Code § 2960 et seq., the amended Mentally Disordered Offender (MDO) statutes, violated the ex post facto clauses of the federal and state constitutions. The court agreed with appellant's contention and reversed the judgment of involuntary commitment. The court held that the MDO statutes could not be constitutionally applied to appellant because appellant committed his crime after the original statutes were found unconstitutional, but before the amendments to the statutes were effective. The court found that because the MDO statutes were penal in nature, application of the amended statutes retroactively violated constitutional ex post facto clauses. The court ruled that the existence of the statutory scheme did not constitute fair warning to appellant of the consequences of his criminal conduct because the statutes had been declared unconstitutional at the time appellant committed his crimes and were therefore unenforceable.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court. The court held that application of amended Mentally Disordered Offender (MDO) statutes to appellant violated federal and state ex post facto constitutional provisions because at the time appellant committed his crime, the statutes had not yet been amended, but had been declared unconstitutional and were therefore void.

 

699 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Weaver


No. A069988.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


44 Cal. App. 4th 154; 51 Cal. Rptr. 2d 602; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 301; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2304; 96 Daily Journal DAR 3833



April 3, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of part II.B.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. 950208-9, John C. Minney and Douglas E. Swager, Judges.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California), which convicted him of second degree murder under Cal. Penal Code §187.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of second degree murder. Appellant challenged his conviction, contending that Cal. Penal Code §1538.5(j), which granted the prosecution the right to a de novo hearing of a suppression motion, was unconstitutional in that it violated appellant's right to due process because appellant was not permitted the same right under Cal. Penal Code §1538.5(i). The court rejected appellant's contention, finding that appellant's due process rights were not violated because the statute granted the same procedural rights at the de novo hearing to both appellant and the prosecution. The court noted that the procedure permitting the prosecution the right to a de novo hearing did not give the prosecution any greater advantage than that which was granted appellant because appellant was not required to give the prosecution notice of the motion to suppress at the preliminary hearing. Accordingly, the court affirmed appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's second degree murder conviction. The court held that appellant's right to due process was not violated by the procedural right to a de novo hearing granted the prosecution because appellant was afforded a preliminary hearing on the motion to suppress, and appellant was not prevented from fully litigating his suppression claim at the de novo hearing.

People v. Dominguez


No. B093134


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


44 Cal. App. 4th 389; 51 Cal. Rptr. 2d 588; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 319; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2543; 96 Daily Journal DAR 4160



April 1, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified April 10, 1996. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published April 10, 1996.
Review Denied June 26, 1996 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 3728.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County. Super. Ct. No. KA025192. Hon. Robert C. Gustaveson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Modified, and as modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted him of second-degree commercial burglary and petty theft with a prior conviction and imposed his sentence under Cal. Penal Code § 667.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant of second-degree commercial burglary and petty theft with a prior conviction. The court affirmed those convictions after modifying them to stay the petty theft conviction. The court held that adjudicating appellant's prior robbery and kidnapping convictions in a single proceeding did not make those offenses one qualifying prior conviction under Cal. Penal Code § 667, reasoning that § 667 did not require basing otherwise qualifying prior convictions on charges that were brought and tried separately. The court also found that the concurrent sentence that appellant received for his petty theft conviction had to be stayed, because absent § 667, § 654 would have barred multiple punishment on his current convictions. The court additionally concluded that § 667's mandate to the executive branch to allege all prior convictions did not violate the constitutional separation of powers doctrine because the legislature could reasonably restrict a coordinate branch's constitutional functions provided that the exercise of those functions was not defeated or materially impaired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for second-degree commercial burglary and petty theft with a prior conviction after ordering his petty theft sentence stayed because the applicable law barred multiple punishments for his current convictions. The court found that jointly trying appellant's prior convictions did not merge them under the three strikes law, which did not require separate trials of qualifying prior convictions.

People v. Mills


No. F022282


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


48 Cal. App. 4th 143; 51 Cal. Rptr. 2d 168; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 272; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 2059; 96 Daily Journal DAR 3440



March 26, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Granted June 12, 1996 (S053149), Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 3264.
Transferred December 17, 1997 to Ct. App., 5th Dist., with directions to vacate its decision and reconsider in light of People v. Superior Court (Romero) (1996) 13 Cal. 4th 497, Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8525.
Opinion filed March 12, 1998 not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Super. Ct. No. 58289. Hon. Roger D. Randall, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Superior Court of Kern County (California) that denied appellant's motion to dismiss a prior "strike" conviction under the three strikes law.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of one count of burglary and two counts of receiving stolen property. Appellant filed a motion to dismiss a prior "strike" under the three strikes law. The court denied the motion and appellant sought review. Appellant contended that the court should have granted his motion because the three strikes law had not eliminated the court's discretionary power under Cal. Penal Code § 1385(a) to dismiss the priors on its own motion. The state argued that the three strikes law prohibited the trial court from dismissing a prior "strike" conviction on its own motion, and that the court could only dismiss on the prosecutor's motion in the interests of justice, or for insufficiency of the evidence. The court affirmed denial of appellant's motion. Upon review of the statutory language found in the three strikes law, the court concluded that the trial court properly held that it did not have discretion to dismiss any of the prior "strike" convictions. The legislative enactment of the three strikes law was intended to eliminate the court's discretion to dismiss a strike. Appellant was properly sentenced to a third strike term.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied appellant's motion to dismiss a prior "strike" conviction because under the three strikes law, the trial court did not have the discretion to dismiss a prior conviction pleaded and proved as a strike on its own motion.

People v. Stofle


No. A067877.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


45 Cal. App. 4th 417; 52 Cal. Rptr. 2d 829; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 427; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 3371; 96 Daily Journal DAR 5425

NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* The above referenced opinion is certified for publication with the exception of the following parts: Uncharged-acts evidence; Pre-enactment "strikes"; Separation of powers; Vagueness of punishment; Concurrent terms as double punishment; Five-year enhancement; Dual use of prior as double punishment; and Urgency measure validity.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified April 25, 1996. The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Partially Published May 10, 1996 on Denial of Rehearing, Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 428.


PRIOR HISTORY: Super. Ct. No. CR-3693. Hon. Winslow Christian, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is modified (1) to stay execution of the term of 25 years to life imposed on count IV, such stay to become permanent when service of sentence under count III is completed ( In re Adams (1975) 14 Cal. 3d 629, 637 [122 Cal. Rptr. 73, 536 P.2d 473]), and (2) to impose an additional 5 years for the found-true enhancement allegation of prior serious felony conviction (§ 667, subd. (a)(1)). As so modified, the judgment is affirmed. Because the addition of the mandatory five-year enhancement term may alter the [***2] superior court's determination of the propriety of the total length of sentence (cf. People v. Burns (1984) 158 Cal. App. 3d 1178, 1181-1184 [205 Cal. Rptr. 356]), the cause is remanded to that court for the purpose of entertaining any application which Stofle may make, within thirty days of the finality of this opinion, for the superior court to exercise any discretion it may have to strike a prior "strike" on the motion of counsel or on its own motion in the furtherance of justice under section 1385 (People v. Superior Court (Romero) (S045097), argued and submitted Apr. 2, 1996


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sex offender challenged an order of the Superior Court (California) denying his parole request. Appellant challenged application of a California credit limitation statute as potentially vague and discriminatory.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sex offender was convicted of two counts of lewd and lascivious conduct with a minor, after one of the child's parents discovered appellant and the child with the child's undergarments down. The appellant and the victim's family were staying at a cabin for a family gathering when the incident occurred. The incident was the third such offense that appellant had been convicted of. Appellant was sentenced to two concurrent terms of 25 years to life. Appellant later sought parole, and challenged a California statute limiting in-prison credits to one-fifth of the total term as vague, arbitrary and discriminatory. Appellee challenged appellant's standing to raise an objection to the statute on hypothetical grounds, and argued that the credits limitation did not apply to a third strike defendant sentenced to an indeterminate sentence. On appeal, the court affirmed as to interpretation of the California statute. The court noted that the credit limitation did not apply to appellant because he received an indeterminate sentence of 25 years to life. The court therefore applied the general rule that release on parole is barred until a specified minimum term has elapsed.


OUTCOME: The court partially affirmed a trial court parole denial to appellant sex offender; a California credits limitation statute challenged as vague did not apply to appellant because he received an indeterminate sentence of 25 years to life.

Professional Engineers v. Department of Transportation


No. C018317


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


48 Cal. App. 4th 1; 51 Cal. Rptr. 2d 465; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 244; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1819; 96 Daily Journal DAR 3092



March 15, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted June 19, 1996 (S042591)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County. Super. Ct. No. CV336697. Hon. Eugene T. Gualco, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Transportation sought review of a permanent injunction from the judgment of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), prohibiting it in specified circumstances from contracting with private entities to perform state work. Appellees labor union initiated the underlying action to enjoin certain contracting practices alleged to have violated the organic civil service mandate and statutory authority.


OVERVIEW: This appeal involved a challenge to Cal. Stat. 433 (1993) extending the authority of appellant Department of Transportation to contract with private entities for the performance on state highway projects of design, inspection, and related work which had traditionally been performed by civil service employees. The superior court issued a permanent injunction against appellant prohibiting it in specified circumstances from contracting with private entities to perform state work. The superior court concluded that the statute was unconstitutional as in violation of the civil service article of Cal. Const., art. VII, § 1. The court reversed the judgment holding that the statute was not violative of the constitutional civil service mandate. Article VII did not prohibit all government contracting with the private sector, only that which implicated the policies immanent in the constitutional provision. Those policies were twofold: to encourage efficiency and economy in state government and to eliminate the spoils system of political patronage by ensuring that demonstrated fitness -- rather than political considerations -- spurred all appointments to public service.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the superior court prohibiting appellant Department of Transportation from contracting with private entities to perform state work. The court ruled against appellees labor union holding that the statute giving appellant authority to contract with private entities was not violative of the constitutional civil service mandate.

 

704 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. White Eagle


No. F022283


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


43 Cal. App. 4th 1053; 51 Cal. Rptr. 2d 68; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 253; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1933; 96 Daily Journal DAR 3264



March 15, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Granted April 18, 1996. (See 48 Cal. App. 4th 1511)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kern County. Super. Ct. No. 58236A. Hon. Richard J. Oberholzer, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the sentence imposed by the Superior Court of Kern County, California, for his conviction for theft with a prior conviction for robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to theft with a prior conviction for robbery. Cal. Penal Code § 666. The aggravated term of three years for theft was doubled pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667(e)(1). The prior prison term enhancement pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667(b) was stayed pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 654. On appeal, the court noted that appellant was not subject to multiple enhancements, because neither § 667(e) nor § 666 were enhancements. Applying the "three strikes" sentencing provisions to the § 666 term of imprisonment was consistent with legislative goals, and it was provided for by statute. The prohibition against double punishment for a single act or omission did not apply because the prior conviction was not an act or omission; it simply established appellant's status as a repeat offender. Double jeopardy was not an issue because appellant was not being punished for the earlier robbery. No factual or legal basis existed for the court to strike or stay the enhancement, thus the trial court's order was an unauthorized sentence. The trial court was directed to vacate the order staying imposition of the § 667.5(b) enhancement, and to prepare a new abstract of judgment.


OUTCOME: The court directed the trial court to vacate its order staying imposition of the enhancement, and to prepare a new abstract of judgment. Applying the "three strikes" provisions to the term of imprisonment was consistent with legislative goals, double jeopardy was not an issue, and the prohibition against double punishment for single acts did not apply because the prior sentence only served to establish appellant's status as a repeat offender.

 

705 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Cooper


No. F022384.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


43 Cal. App. 4th 815; 51 Cal. Rptr. 2d 106; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 247; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1845; 96 Daily Journal DAR 3055



March 15, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rule 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts 1, 2, 3, and 4 of the Discussion.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kings County, No. 1303, Peter M. Schultz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Kings County (California) sentencing him to 25 years to life as a third-strike offender under Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)(i) for his conviction as an ex-felon in possession of a handgun.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of being an ex-felon in possession of a handgun, which he pointed at supermarket employees who detained him for shoplifting a can of frosting. Appellant was sentenced to 25 years to life under the three-strikes legislation, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)(i). On appeal, he challenged the constitutionality and application of the three-strikes legislation. The court affirmed the judgment, holding that the legislation did not provide for cruel and unusual punishment and did not deprive him of equal protection. A 25-year sentence for a recidivist offender like appellant, convicted of a nonviolent, non-serious felony but with at least two prior convictions for violent or serious felonies was not grossly disproportionate to the crime. Appellant's intractable recidivism, coupled with his offense, justified the term. Appellant failed to meet the threshold prerequisite to an equal protection claim of unequal treatment to similarly-situated persons.


OUTCOME: Appellant's sentence of 25 years to life as a third-strike offender for his conviction of being an ex-felon in possession of a handgun was affirmed because the application of the three-strikes legislation was not unconstitutional.

Gilbert v. Nat'l Enquirer


No. B095913.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


43 Cal. App. 4th 1135; 51 Cal. Rptr. 2d 91; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 258; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1984; 96 Daily Journal DAR 3336; 24 Media L. Rep. 2377



March 7, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published March 22, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC131079, Robert H. O'Brien, Judge.



DISPOSITION: On the appeal, we reverse the order issuing the preliminary injunction and award costs to defendants. On the cross-appeal, we affirm the order denying the motion to seal the record in this case and award costs to defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant magazine and former husband sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) which granted a preliminary injunction restraining appellant former husband from disclosing allegedly defamatory statements about cross-appellant former wife/actress to appellant magazine. Cross-appellant sought review of the trial court's denial of her motion to seal the record.


OVERVIEW: Cross-appellant former wife/actress filed an action for defamation and invasion of privacy against appellant magazine and former husband after appellant magazine published an article about her. Cross-appellant added a cause of action for injunctive relief against appellant former husband and obtained a temporary restraining order which restricted him from revealing personal information about her to appellant magazine, after he threatened to reveal personal information unless cross-appellant dismissed the action against him. The trial court granted the preliminary injunction, but refused to enter a protective order sealing record. Appellants sought review of the entry of the injunction and cross-appellant sought review of the denial of her motion to seal the record. The court reversed the order granting the injunction and held that it was an invalid prior restraint of free speech and that cross-appellant's right to privacy did not outweigh appellants' rights to publish opinions about her. The court affirmed the denial of the motion to seal and held that cross-appellant failed to show that her case fell under a specific exception to make a court record nonpublic.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of a preliminary injunction against appellant newspaper and former husband and held that it was a prior restraint of free speech. The court affirmed the denial of cross-appellant former wife/actress's motion to seal the record.

 

707 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Walsh v. Superior Court


No. B094286


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


42 Cal. App. 4th 1822; 50 Cal. Rptr. 2d 751; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 176; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1564; 96 Daily Journal DAR 2540



March 5, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Real Party in Interest's Review Denied May 29, 1996 and the Reporter of Decisions directed not to publish this opn. in the Official Reports (Cal. Const., art. VI, § 14; rule 976, Cal. Rules of Ct.).


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding; application for a writ of prohibition. Super. Ct. No. PA 017549. Hon. Ronald S. Coen, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant petitioned for a writ of prohibition restraining respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), from commencing trial on an information charging defendant with assault on a peace officer in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245(c).


OVERVIEW: At a first preliminary hearing at which defendant was held to answer to an information charging assault on a peace officer in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 245(c), defendant's counsel indicated that he doubted defendant's competence. Based on the report of a court-appointed psychiatrist, respondent trial court found defendant incompetent, and committed him to the Department of Mental Health for placement in a state hospital. Later, respondent found that defendant's competence had been restored, and criminal proceedings were resumed. Defendant moved, under Cal. Penal Code § 995, for a second preliminary hearing. Respondent denied the motion for lack of proof that defendant was incompetent at the time of the first hearing. The court of appeal granted defendant's petition for a writ of prohibition prohibiting respondent from conducting any proceedings other than granting defendant's motion under § 995. Under Cal. Penal Code § 1368.1(a), the information had to be set aside because the defendant was found mentally incompetent shortly after the preliminary hearing, and due process required that he be given a second preliminary hearing when his competence was restored.


OUTCOME: The writ of prohibition was issued. The preliminary hearing that preceded defendant's arraignment in respondent trial court was held shortly before defendant was found to be incompetent. Due process required that the information be set aside and a second preliminary hearing be held.

 

708 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


Santa Monica Beach, Ltd. v. Superior Court


No. B097056


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


47 Cal. App. 4th 120; 50 Cal. Rptr. 2d 726; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 161; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1300; 96 Daily Journal DAR 2155



February 27, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 249. Review Granted May 29, 1996 (S052824), Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 3039.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 42 Cal. App. 4th 1228.)]
Reprinted without change in the Review Granted Opinions Pamphlet to permit tracking pending review and disposition by the Supreme Ct.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original proceeding; application for writ of mandate. Super. Ct. No. SS005266. Hon. Alan B. Haber, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner sought a writ of mandate against respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), after respondent sustained a municipality's demurrer in petitioner's complaint for inverse condemnation and petition for a writ of administrative mandate.


OVERVIEW: A municipality adopted a rent control charter amendment and created an administrative rent control board to regulate rentals. Petitioner filed a petition asking for permission to increase its rents. The board's hearing examiner found that petitioner was not entitled to a rent increase. After changes in rent regulations, petitioner filed a second petition. Although the hearing officer found that petitioner was entitled to rent increases, petitioner appealed the hearing officer's determinations. The board affirmed the hearing officer's decision. Petitioner then filed a complaint for inverse condemnation and petition for a writ of administrative mandate. Respondent trial court accepted the board's position and sustained its demurrer. Petitioner filed for a writ of mandate. The court granted the writ and determined that there had been a regulatory taking of petitioner's property. Therefore, an inverse condemnation action was proper, and the demurrer was improperly sustained. Petitioner was entitled to an opportunity to establish that the municipality's rent control law went too far and to establish a compensable regulatory taking.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of mandate was granted. Respondent trial court improperly sustained a municipality's demurrer to petitioner property owner's complaint for inverse condemnation and petition for a writ of administrative mandate, because petitioner was entitled to establish that there was a compensable regulatory taking.

 

709 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Ameri-Medical Corp. v. Workers' Comp. Appeals Bd.


No. B084720, No. B081772.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


42 Cal. App. 4th 1260; 50 Cal. Rptr. 2d 366; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 168; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1292; 96 Daily Journal DAR 2181; 61 Cal. Comp. Cases 149



February 27, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified March 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Proceeding to review decisions of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board. W.C.A.B. Nos. LBO 218124; ANA 236540.



DISPOSITION: Orders annulled and matters remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner medical clinic sought review of decisions of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (California), which ordered petitioner to comply with discovery requests in cases in which petitioner, as lien claimant, sought payment for a medical evaluation and report.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a medical clinic, challenged the orders of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board (board) that ordered it to comply with discovery requests made by respondents. Petitioner argued that Cal. Lab. Code § 4628, subd. (d), as applied was an unconstitutional fee regulation statute that deprived it of the ability to make any profit, and that the discovery requests constituted an impermissible invasion of the right to privacy in financial information. The court annulled the orders below. It held that the purpose of Cal. Lab. Code § 4628 must govern the interpretation of subdivision (d). It found that subdivision (d) merely furthered the anti-ghostwriting purpose by listing permissible charges that were reimbursable as fees and costs for the preparation of the report. Thus, the statute was not unconstitutional. The court further held that respondents, when asserting a violation of the statute as an objection to payment of a bill, had a legitimate interest in identifying impermissible charges in the billings, but did not have a right to unfettered access to petitioner's business records. Respondents could only seek discovery of relevant and unprivileged information.


OUTCOME: The orders of the Workers' Compensation Appeals Board that ordered petitioner to comply with discovery requests made by respondents were annulled because respondents could only seek discovery of relevant and unprivileged information in determining the amount of medical costs due petitioner.

 

710 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Reese


No. A068871


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


47 Cal. App. 4th 92; 50 Cal. Rptr. 2d 162; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 147; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1223; 96 Daily Journal DAR 2022



February 21, 1996, Filed


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing March 21, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 255. Review Granted June 12, 1996 (S052695), Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 3262..
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 42 Cal. App. 4th 1113.)]
Transferred December 17, 1997 to Ct. App., 1st Dist., Div. 5 with directions to vacate its decision and reconsider in light of People v. Fuhrman (1996) 16 Cal. 4th 930, 941-947, reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 8524. Opinion filed April 2, 1998 not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Contra Costa Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. 9407149. Hon. Richard P. Arnason, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Contra Costa Superior Court (California), which sentenced him to 25 years to life as a "third strike" defendant under California's three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(i), for first degree burglary, under Cal. Penal Code § 459.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a career criminal, was convicted of first degree burglary, under Cal. Penal Code § 459, for stealing a videocassette recorder and screwdrivers from an unoccupied residence. Because defendant had two prior serious felony convictions, he was sentenced under the three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667 to 25 years to life. Defendant challenged his sentence as constituting cruel and unusual punishment. Although it did not file an appeal, the state argued that the trial court erred by failing to impose two five-year enhancements for defendant's two prior serious felony convictions and a one-year enhancement for a prior prison term under Cal. Penal Code § 667.5(b). The court found that because the enhancements were mandatory, the trial court erred in not imposing them and that the state was allowed to challenge the unauthorized sentence. The court also found that the sentence did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment because the crime being analyzed for proportionality to the sentence was not burglary alone, but burglary by a recidivist. The court remanded for resentencing, stating that the trial court could dismiss a strike allegation if it was so inclined.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the portion of the trial court's judgment that sentenced defendant to 25-years-to-life, finding that it did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment, but that the trial court erred in failing to impose mandatory sentence enhancements. The court remanded to the trial court for resentencing in order to afford the trial court an opportunity to dismiss a strike allegation if so inclined.

 

711 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Tanya B.


No. B089992.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


43 Cal. App. 4th 1; 50 Cal. Rptr. 2d 576; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 199; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1591; 96 Daily Journal DAR 2619



February 20, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published March 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. YJ07789, Roosevelt F. Dorn, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under Cal. Veh. Code § 13202.5, appellant juvenile challenged an order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which suspended appellant's license for nearly four years after she admitted violating Cal. Veh. Code § 23152(a) by driving under the influence of a drug.


OVERVIEW: Appellant admitted to driving under the influence of a drug in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23152. At the disposition hearing, the trial court ordered appellant, then 17 years old, to be released on probation with a number of conditions, including that she was not to drive until the age of 21. No objection was made at the time, but defense counsel later filed a motion for modification, arguing that the order violated Cal. Veh. Code § 13202.5, a law which requires that a court suspend a juvenile's license for one year after a violation such as appellant's. The juvenile court denied appellant's motion. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that appellant had not waived her appeal, but that it was within the broad discretion of the juvenile court to impose a term of suspension longer than that required by the law. The court found that the suspension was directly related to appellant's violation of driving under the influence of a drug, that the offense occurred only four days after appellant's probation for an earlier drug offense ended, and that the juvenile court had legal jurisdiction over appellant until she turned 21, the time the suspension was to end.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the juvenile court's order which suspended appellant juvenile's license for four years. The court found that the juvenile court had the discretion to extend the driver's license suspension period provided for by statute because the suspension was directly related to appellant's offense of driving under the influence of a drug and because the juvenile court had jurisdiction over appellant until she turned 21 years old.

 

712 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Doyle


No. A068529


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


47 Cal. App. 4th 74; 50 Cal. Rptr. 2d 28; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 123; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1064; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1744



February 15, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted April 26, 1996 (S052277), Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 2416.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 42 Cal. App. 4th 837.)]
Review Dismissed May 13, 1998 and cause remanded to Ct. App., 1st Dist., Div. 5 (rule 29.4(c), Cal. Rules of Ct.), Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 2969.


PRIOR HISTORY: Alameda County Superior Court. Super. Ct. No. C121433. Hon. Joanne Parrilli, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Alameda County Superior Court (California), which convicted him of the offense of robbery and sentenced him under the California three strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(1), on the grounds that the jury instruction was improper, the three strikes law was unconstitutionally vague and violated the separation powers doctrine, and the trial court did not properly exercise its discretion.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and one other man robbed a 71 year old woman by grabbing her tote bag and yanking it from her arm. She suffered a broken elbow and other injuries. Both men were convicted of robbery. Appellant had a prior serious felony conviction and a prior prison term. He was sentenced to the middle term with enhancements for the priors and the victims' age. On appeal, the court struck the enhancement based on the victim's age, awarded presentence credit and affirmed. It held that the jury instruction given, based on dicta from a supreme court case, satisfied federal due process concerns, that the three strike law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(1), did not impermissibly change the duties of judges and prosecutors, that any error in the exercise of judicial discretion was harmless, and that the three strike law was not unconstitutionally vague as applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for robbery but struck the enhancement based upon victim's age and as modified affirmed the sentence. The court held that the jury instruction properly dealt with federal due process concerns, the three strikes law was not unconstitutional as applied, and any error in the ruling of the court was harmless under the circumstances.

 

713 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. McGowan


No. C017839.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


42 Cal. App. 4th 740; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 866; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 119; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 1012; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1647



February 13, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - ORDERED NOT PUBLISHED


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Mono County, No. 10771, N. Edward Denton, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Mono County (California), which convicted defendant on three counts of driving or taking a vehicle with the intent to permanently or temporarily deprive the owner of title to or possession of the vehicle and four counts of vehicle burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contested the use of the Cal. Penal Code § 666.5, a recidivist enhancement statute, in his sentencing because the state did not prove he had been convicted previously of vehicle theft or that his current convictions were for vehicle theft. The court found that § 666.5 applied only to motor vehicle theft under Cal. Veh. Code § 10851 because the Omnibus Motor Vehicle Theft Act of 1989, which created § 666.5, made several references to § 10851 but only referred specifically to motor vehicle theft under § 10851 in § 666.5. However, the court found that when defendant admitted to a 1975 conviction under § 10851 he admitted to every element of the offense charged even if he did not specifically admit to vehicle theft under § 10851. Furthermore, the court found that although the trial court erred in applying § 666.5 because the jury only found defendant guilty of a violation of § 10851in his current convictions rather than specifically vehicle theft, the error was harmless. The court affirmed the sentence and conviction of defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction and the trial court's application of the vehicle theft recidivism enhancement statute because defendant admitted to a previous conviction for vehicle theft and the error in applying the statute absent a specific finding of vehicle theft was harmless.

 

714 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Murphy v. Padilla


No. H013695.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


42 Cal. App. 4th 707; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 722; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 112; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 974; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1577



February 9, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Santa Clara County, No. 719891, William Harris, Judge. * 


* Retired judge of the Santa Clara Superior Court sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: For reasons set forth above, we conclude that the alleged oral settlement agreement is not enforceable under section 664.6. The judgment is reversed. Costs are awarded to appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant easement owner sought review a decision of the Superior Court of Santa Clara County (California), which enforced an alleged oral settlement pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 664.6 in an action concerning an easement over respondent landowners property. Appellant alleged that the agreement was not enforceable and could not be used as evidence to prove the agreement.


OVERVIEW: Respondent landowners discovered that appellant easement owner had a forty foot easement over their property, after they bought it. They filed a complaint against appellant and others alleging various contract claims, fraud and an equitable claim for abandonment. The lower court referred the case to mediation under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 638, without a proper stipulation or order. A retired judge was appointed and the parties thought they had an agreement, but appellant backed out. Respondents brought a motion to enforce the agreement and the lower court granted it. On appeal, the court reversed. It held that the retired judge under the reference in the case was not a general referee under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 638(1) and that the oral agreement could not satisfy the "before the court" requirement of Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 664.6. It also held that the alleged agreement could not be enforced by motion as a contract under agency principles because appellant's attorney was not invested by virtue of his employment with the authority to make such a contract.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision to enforce the mediation agreement because the alleged oral settlement agreement was not enforceable under the mediation statute. The court held also held that the agreement was not enforceable as a contract.

 

715 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Forbes


No. F022177.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


42 Cal. App. 4th 599; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 836; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 108; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 931; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1426



February 7, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of the Statement of Facts and sections I, II, IV and V.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Stanislaus County, No. 269871, David G. Vander Wall, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his convictions of two charges of sexual misconduct with a child from the Superior Court of Stanislaus County (California). It was alleged at trial that appellant was a stranger to victim under Cal. Penal Code §1203.066(a)(3). Appellant contended the trial court erred by failing to give appellant's requested instruction of a definition of the word stranger.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of the commission of a lewd or lascivious act on a child and penetration with a foreign object of the genital opening of a child. It was alleged appellant was a stranger to the victim within the meaning of Cal. Penal Code § 1203.066(a)(3). Appellant sought review of the convictions and contended that the trial court erred by failing to give his requested instruction setting forth a definition of the word stranger in conjunction with the § 1203.066 allegation. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the word stranger in § 1203.066 had no technical meaning peculiar to the law and therefore the trial court did not err in refusing to give a jury instruction that purported to define the word. The court found that the trial court was not required to instruct on the meaning of a commonly understood term.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant of lewd or lascivious act on a child and penetration with a foreign object of the genital opening of a child, and held that the word stranger under California law had no technical meaning peculiar to the law and therefore that the trial court did not err in refusing to give a jury instruction which purported to define the word.

 

716 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Linney v. Turpen


No. A066290.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


42 Cal. App. 4th 763; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 813; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 109; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1403; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 917



February 7, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III B, III C and III D.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, No. 368179, Walter H. Harrington, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which denied his writ of mandate to compel respondent employer to set aside a six-month suspension. Appellant was suspended after a hearing under San Francisco Cal. Charter § 8.341.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee was suspended for violating rules of conduct set forth in the airport police manual. A hearing was conducted pursuant to San Francisco Cal. Charter § 8.341. The trial court denied appellant's petition for writ of mandate to set aside the suspension. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial of the writ of mandate and held that appellant had failed to clearly establish prejudice or bias in the manner of selecting the hearing officer. Appellant contended that the method of selecting the hearing officer deprived him of due process. The court found that the procedure for selection of hearing officers could not reasonably be characterized as granting the city an unrestricted selection. The court determined that appellant could have challenged the competence of the hearing officer before the hearing, and that his failure to do so precluded him form raising the issue on appeal. The court concluded that appellant failed to establish disqualification under the objective standard set out in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 170.1(a)(6)(C). Due process required only a reasonably impartial, noninvolved reviewer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which denied appellant employee's writ of mandate to compel respondent employer to set aside a six-month suspension. The court held that appellant failed to clearly establish prejudice or bias in the manner of selecting the hearing officer.

 

717 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Church of Scientology v. Wollersheim


Nos. B084686, B086063.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


42 Cal. App. 4th 628; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 620; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 87; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 773; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1162



February 1, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC074815, Edward Y. Kakita, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of dismissal and judgment awarding attorney fees are affirmed. Wollersheim is awarded costs and attorney fees on appeal. The matter is remanded to the trial court to determine the amount thereof.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner church sought the review of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted respondent church member's motion to strike the complaint and dismissed the suit pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 425.16.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner church filed a petition to set aside the judgment that respondent church member had been awarded against it in a prior suit. Petitioner alleged that the judge in the former suit was biased against it. The lower court granted respondent's motion to strike the complaint and dismissed the suit pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 425.16. The court affirmed the order of the lower court, holding that petitioner's suit was a strategic lawsuit against public participation under § 425.16, in that the suit sought to harass respondent for his having asserted his rights against petitioner in the prior suit. The court further held that petitioner had failed to meet its burden of proving that it could have prevailed in the suit against respondent because there was no admissible evidence alleged in petitioner's complaint to substantiate its claims of judicial bias in the prior suit. The court also affirmed the lower court's award of attorney fees to respondent and awarded respondent attorney fees on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the lower court, which granted respondent church member's motion to strike the complaint and dismissed petitioner church's suit against him, and the court affirmed the lower court's award of attorney fees to respondent; petitioner did not present a prima facie case that it would have prevailed in its petition against respondent.

 

718 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Brown


No. E014125.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


42 Cal. App. 4th 461; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 652; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 91; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 804; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1226



February 1, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III, IV, V, VI, VII, VIII, IX, and X.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied April 25, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 2401.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR 46378, W. Charles Morgan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which convicted appellant, under Cal. Penal Code § 288(b), of 20 counts of forcible lewd and lascivious acts against appellant's stepdaughter.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's step-daughter was molested, and appellant was convicted of 20 counts of forcible lewd and lascivious acts under Cal. Penal Code § 288(b). Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed. The court found appellant had not needed to testify in order to preserve a challenge to the use of a voluntary extrajudicial statement for impeachment, the statement having been obtained in the absence of a knowing and voluntary waiver of the right to counsel guaranteed by U.S. Const. amend. VI. However, the court overruled the challenge and found the voluntary statement had been admissible for impeachment because the exclusion of the statement from the prosecution's case-in-chief had sufficiently vindicated appellant's amend. VI rights. The court also found that limiting appellant's preemptory challenges to 10 had not deprived appellant of equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Cal. Const. art. I, § 7. The court held appellant had not been entitled to 20 preemptory challenges under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 231(a) because § 231(a), which applied to offenses with life sentences, had not been applicable to appellant's aggregate sentence for the multiple counts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment convicting appellant of 20 counts of forcible lewd and lascivious acts because appellant's voluntary statements, obtained in the absence of a knowing waiver of the right to counsel guaranteed by the Sixth Amendment, had been admissible for impeachment purposes and because appellant had not been entitled to additional preemptory challenges even thought the 20 counts, in aggregate, had created a de facto life term.

 

719 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. McClelland


No. B089024.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


42 Cal. App. 4th 144; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 587; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 76; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 718; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1100



January 31, 1996, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. *


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts II.B. and II.C.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As modified February 16, 1996. Review Denied April 17, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 2160.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. PA017707, Judith Meisels Ashmann, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. The clerk of the superior court is directed to correct the adstract of judgment by striking the language in paragraph 4 and substituting therefor language reflecting that the court found to be true the allegation of a prior conviction under Penal Code section 667, subdivision (e)(i).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted appellant of stalking under Cal. Penal Code § 646.9 (b).


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for stalking based on behavior that was prohibited by a restraining order under Cal. Penal Code § 646.9(e) because there was sufficient evidence to support the conviction. The court concluded that there was sufficient evidence to show that appellant rammed his car into the front gate of complainant's home, telephoned her and stated that there would be a fire bomb, called her and her children vile names, and threw an explosive device at her home. The court found that appellant was aware of the behavior the restraining order prohibited and that the stalking statute was constitutional. The court affirmed appellant's conviction because there was evidence to show that he had harassed the complainant and made a credible threat with the intent to place complainant in reasonable fear of her safety as required under the stalking statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for stalking because he had violated the restraining order, harassed complainant and had made a credible threat to place her in reasonable fear for her safety.

 

720 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Garcia v. Superior Court


No. B092707.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


42 Cal. App. 4th 177; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 580; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 77; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 703; 96 Daily Journal DAR 1110



January 31, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC098524, Arthur Baldonado, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ, having served its purpose, is discharged. The petition for a writ of mandate is denied. The temporary stay of further proceedings in the trial court shall remain in effect until issuance of the remittitur.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner survivor sought a writ of mandate to compel respondent Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) to set aside its order striking a complaint from petitioner's pleading dealing with decedent's loss of the enjoyment of life and other hedonic damages in an action brought under the Civil Rights Act, 42 U.S.C.S. §1983.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner survivor filed suit in her capacity as representative of decedent's estate against police and paramedics alleging violations of the decedent's federal civil rights resulting from excessive force used following his arrest, including a carotid chokehold. Petitioner brought the action pursuant to the federal Civil Rights Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Respondent trial court struck a paragraph from the complaint dealing with hedonic damages and petitioner filed a petition for a writ of mandate to compel respondent to set aside its order. The court issued an alternative writ of mandate, temporarily stayed further trial proceedings, and after full briefing and oral arguments, the court concluded the trial court's order striking the hedonic damages was correct. Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 377.34 allowed the representative of decedent to sue on decedent's cause of action before death and for punitive damages. The court opined these damage provisions sufficed to fulfill the compensatory and deterrent purposes of the federal Civil Rights Act in a case where the civil violation caused the death. As such, state law was not inconsistent with the law of the federal government.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that the trial court's order striking the claim for loss of enjoyment of life and other hedonic damages was correct in the federal civil rights suit brought by petitioner as survivor of decedent. The petition for a writ of mandate was denied. The court found that punitive and other damages under state law were sufficient to fulfill the compensatory and deterrent purposes of the federal civil rights act.

 

721 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Howard Jarvis Taxpayers' Assn. v. Board of Supervisors


No. B081566.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


41 Cal. App. 4th 1363; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 157; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 45; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 462; 96 Daily Journal DAR 723



January 22, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC054196, David A. Workman, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Defendants are awarded costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer groups appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sustained a demurrer to an amended complaint that alleged that defendant county violated Cal. Gov't Code § 7507 and Los Angeles County, Cal., Code § 5.27.100, by including flexible benefits in calculation of retirement benefits to county employees. The appeal did not challenge dismissal of the complaint against two other defendants.


OVERVIEW: Defendant county adopted flexible benefit plans for its employees. An independent public agency, whose dismissal from the action was not appealed by plaintiff taxpayer groups, adopted a policy of including defendant's benefit plan contributions in "compensation" to calculate retirement benefit payments of defendant's employees. Plaintiffs sued, claiming that defendant altered its employees' retirement benefit plan without a public hearing and an actuarial report in violation of Cal. Gov't Code § 7507. Plaintiffs also claimed that inclusion of flexible benefits in retirement benefit calculations violated Los Angeles County, Cal., Code § 5.27.100 because defendant's chief administrative officer (CAO) did not obtain approval of that decision from defendant's board of supervisors. The court affirmed a dismissal of the complaint. The record demonstrated that the decision to include flexible benefits was not made by defendant, but was made by an independent public agency that was not subject to Cal. Gov't Code § 7507. Los Angeles County, Cal., Code § 5.27.100 did not grant the CAO authority to set policy regarding inclusion of flexible benefit payments in calculating retirement benefits.


OUTCOME: The judgment that sustained a demurrer to plaintiff taxpayer groups' complaint was affirmed. Defendant county did not take the action that was challenged by the complaint. Those actions were taken by independent public agencies, which were created by statute.

 

722 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Kilborn


No. B094396.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


41 Cal. App. 4th 1325; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 152; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 41; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 428; 96 Daily Journal DAR 662



January 19, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. KA026539, Charles W. McCoy, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), where defendant was sentenced under the Three Strikes Law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a guilty plea to a felony and was sentenced under the Three Strikes Law. Defendant challenged his sentence asserting that it violated due process as well as the equal protection clause. The appeals court affirmed defendant's sentence under the Three Strikes Law. According to the court, a sentencing law that was utterly irrational was unconstitutional, and did not afford a basis for punishment. The court held that in the case of a substantive due process claim, deprivation of a right was supportable only if the conduct from which the deprivation flowed was prescribed by reasonable legislation that was reasonably applied. The court concluded that the Three Strikes Law bore a rational relation to the legislature's goal. The court stated that there was no doubt that the legislative purpose to punish recidivist criminals more severely than others was a proper goal. Next, the court stated that the equal protection clause was not violated because defendant was treated similarly to others similarly situated with respect to the legitimate purpose of the law. The court held that the legislature could enact laws signaling out certain recidivist for greater punishment.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed defendant's sentence under the Three Strikes Law because the law bore a rational relation to the legislature's goal of punishing recidivist criminals more severely than others.

 

723 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Bridget R.


No. B093520, No. B093694.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


41 Cal. App. 4th 1483; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 507; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 37; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 394; 96 Daily Journal DAR 619



January 18, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. BN1980 and BC114849, John L. Henning, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order to show cause is discharged. The petition for writ of mandate is granted. The order vacating the termination of the parental rights of Richard A. and Cindy R. over the minors Lucy and Bridget R. is reversed. The matter is remanded, and the trial court is ordered to conduct further proceedings consistent with the views expressed in this opinion. Costs on appeal are awarded to the R's and Vista Del Mar.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adoptive parents and adoption agency sought review from a judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which issued an order pursuant to the Indian Child Welfare Act, that invalidated a voluntary relinquishment of parental rights respecting twin infants. The judgment ordered the twins removed from appellants and returned to the extended family of respondent biological parent.


OVERVIEW: Twin children were born of Indian decent by respondent biological parent and were adopted by appellant adoptive parents through appellant adoption agency. Appellants sought review from an order, which invalidated a voluntary relinquishment of parental rights by respondent and ordered the twins removed from appellant adoptive family and returned to the extended family of the respondent biological parent. On appeal, the court examined the scope of the Indian Child Welfare Act (the Act) and determined that it could not be constitutionally applied in the absence of evidence demonstrating that respondent biological parent had a significant social, cultural, or political relationship with the Tribe. On the record, the court found little or no support for the existence of such a relationship. The court observed that it was error for the lower court to apply the Act without first determining whether its application was proper. The court gave guidance in that the burden of proof was on the respondent biological parent who sought to set aside the relinquishment of parental rights. The order that vacated the termination of the parental rights was reversed and the matter was remanded.


OUTCOME: The order that vacated the termination of the parental rights of appellant adoptive parents was reversed and the matter was remanded for a determination of the applicability of the Indian Child Welfare Act. The court found little or no support for the existence of a relationship between respondent biological parent and the Indian Tribe.

 

724 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



California State Electronics Assn. v. Zeos Internat. Ltd.


No. B086059.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


41 Cal. App. 4th 1270; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 127; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 34; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 379; 96 Daily Journal DAR 599; 28 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 1207



January 17, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC066120, Stephen M. Lachs, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state electronics association sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent, an out-of state seller and distributor of computers. The summary judgment was on the grounds that the Song-Beverly Consumer Warranty Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 1790 et seq., violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3., and 15 U.S.C.S. § 2301 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state electronics association brought an action under Cal. Bus. & Prof. Code § 17200 et seq. to enjoin sales by respondent, an out of state seller and distributor of computers, alleging a violation of the Song-Beverly Consumer Warranty Act (Act), Cal. Civ. Code § 1790 et seq. The Act required local repair facilities for warranty work. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of respondent on the grounds that the Act was applicable to respondent's sales and that it violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. Appellant sought review and the court affirmed. Without ruling on the constitutional challenge to the Act, the court held that the Act's requirement of local repair facilities was not applicable to respondent because its sales were made over the phone from out of state and the nature of its contracts did not specifically require delivery in the state. Therefore title passed to an in state buyer outside the state.


OUTCOME: Without addressing the constitutional issue raised under the Commerce Clause, the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of respondent, an out of state seller and distributor of computers. The court held that the Song-Beverly Consumer Warranty Act's requirement of local repair facilities was not applicable to respondent because its sales were shipment contracts made over the phone where title passed to the buyer outside the state.

 

725 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Bury


No. B086381.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SIX


41 Cal. App. 4th 1194; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 107; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 32; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 360; 96 Daily Journal DAR 551



January 16, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 11, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 2111.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Ventura County, No. CR33642, Charles W. Campbell, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his Superior Court of Ventura County (California) conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23152(a).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol in violation of Cal. Veh. Code § 23152(a). The court of appeals affirmed. Contrary to appellant's assertion, admission of the results of a preliminary alcohol screening (PAS) test administered to appellant at the scene of his arrest was proper to show appellant's intoxication. Evidence demonstrated that appellant voluntarily took the PAS test and then refused to take a chemical test under the implied consent law, Cal. Veh. Code § 23157(a)(1). PAS tests had been deemed scientifically reliable. Additionally, the legislative intent behind the enactment of the statute was to assist the prosecution of driving under the influence cases and not to exclude the admissibility of PAS evidence. Such evidence was relevant, not only to establish cause to arrest, but as tending to prove the essential element of the offense itself--the accused's intoxication.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for driving under the influence of alcohol was affirmed because the results of a preliminary alcohol screening test administered to him at the scene of his arrest was properly admissible at trial to show appellant's intoxication.

Pacific Mutual Life Ins. Co. v. State Bd. of Equalization


No. B076158.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


41 Cal. App. 4th 1153; 49 Cal. Rptr. 2d 99; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 30; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 333; 96 Daily Journal DAR 479



January 12, 1996, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC037751, Victor E. Chavez, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed insofar as it (1) confirms the validity of Revenue and Taxation Code section 12202.1, (2) confirms the validity of the 1989 premiums tax rate, and (3) confirms the invalidity of the 1990 premiums tax rate. The judgment is reversed insofar as it (1) orders a refund to plaintiffs of taxes paid in 1990 beyond those based on a rate of 2.35 percent and (2) awards attorney fees to plaintiffs. The cause is remanded for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed herein. Costs on appeal to the Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff life insurance companies and defendant California State Board of Equalization appealed a judgment from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California) which upheld the constitutionality of Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 12202.1, approved the insurance premiums tax rate for 1989, but held that the tax rate for 1990 was invalid. The trial court ordered defendant to refund plaintiffs for overpayment in 1990 and to pay their attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff life insurance companies brought suit challenging the validity of Cal. Rev. & Tax. Code § 12202.1 which authorized defendant California State Board of Equalization to impose new insurance premium tax rates for 1989 and 1990. The trial court held that § 12202.1 did not violate the state constitution. The trial court also determined the revised tax rate imposed on plaintiffs for 1989 was properly calculated but the rate imposed for 1990 did not comply with § 12202.1. The trial court ordered defendant to refund plaintiffs' overpayment for 1990. Defendant was also ordered to pay plaintiffs' attorney fees. Both parties appealed. The court agreed that § 12202.1 was a valid delegation of power, and affirmed the validity of the 1989 rate and the invalidity of the 1990 rate. However, the court reversed insofar as the trial court's judgment required a refund to plaintiffs rather than a remand to defendant for recalculation of the 1990 premiums tax rate. Because plaintiffs brought the suit for their own strong personal economic interests, the court held, the award of attorney fees under the private attorney general statute, Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1021.5, was not justified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment insofar as it upheld the validity of statute authorizing defendant state board of equalization to impose new insurance premium tax rates and confirmed the validity of the 1989 premiums tax rate and the invalidity of the 1990 rate. The judgment was reversed insofar as it ordered a refund to plaintiffs of taxes paid in 1990 and awarded attorney fees. The court remanded to defendant for recalculation of the 1990 rate.

People v. Christian


No. A067247.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


41 Cal. App. 4th 986; 48 Cal. Rptr. 2d 867; 1996 Cal. App. LEXIS 5; 96 Cal. Daily Op. Service 249; 96 Daily Journal DAR 331



January 9, 1996, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied April 11, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 2102.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Contra Costa County, No. 940743-8, Patricia K. Sepulveda, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgments are affirmed as to both appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Contra Costa County (California), which convicted them for the robbery of a fast food restaurant.


OVERVIEW: Appellants were charged with the robbery of a fast food restaurant. The trial court permitted a public defender's office and an alternate defender office to represent both appellants at trial. Appellants were subsequently convicted of the charged crime. One appellant contended that because both offices were under the supervision of one public defender, they were not separate entities for conflict of interest purposes. Appellant contended that he was denied the right to conflict-free and independent counsel. On appeal, the court found that the offices were separate. The court found that the alternate defender's office litigated its own cases, had its own clerical staff and investigators, and that the offices were physically separated. The offices maintained minimal contact with each other. The court concluded that the offices provided representation to indigent defendants that was free from inherent conflicts of interest. The court stated that there was simply no evidence that either attorney represented conflicting interests in his defense of the case. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment that convicted appellants of robbery was affirmed because no conflict of interest existed between two public defender's offices that represented both appellants.
