Family Planning Specialists Medical Group, Inc. v. Powers


No. A066362.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


39 Cal. App. 4th 1561; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 667; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1098; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8673; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14961



November 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 6, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1272.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. 724759-8, James R. Lambden, Judge.



DISPOSITION: For all the foregoing reasons, the judgment of the trial court is affirmed. Costs to respondents.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant anti-abortion activist sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Alameda County (California), which denied his motion for attorney fees under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1021.5, after respondent obstetricians/gynecologists voluntarily dismissed their complaint for injunctive and monetary relief for libel based on leaflets promulgated by appellant.


OVERVIEW: Respondent obstetricians/gynecologists brought suit against appellant anti-abortion activist, seeking injunctive and monetary relief for appellant's allegedly libelous leaflets. Respondents obtained a temporary restraining order, which had to be enforced with a contempt finding and appellant's imprisonment, but when the trial court refused to issue a temporary injunction against appellant, respondents voluntarily dismissed their complaint. Appellant then sought attorney fees pursuant to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1021.5. The trial court denied his motion. The reviewing court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying attorney fees, because appellant failed to show that defense of the libel action resulted in the enforcement of his or anyone else's free speech rights; he only enforced his own free speech rights. The court also held that he did not confer a significant benefit on the general public or a large class of persons; his "success" benefited only himself.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court denying attorney fees to appellant anti-abortion activist. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in such denial. The court held that appellant failed to show that defense of the libel action resulted in the enforcement of his or anyone else's free speech rights, or that he conferred a sginificant benefit on the general public or a large class of persons.

 

754 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



County of Los Angeles v. McMahon


No. B083583.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


39 Cal. App. 4th 1432; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 550; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1083; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8639; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14926



November 8, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BC015907, Kathryn Doi Todd, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and the matter remanded. The trial court is directed to order the Department to hear the County's outstanding appeals within 60 days of the filing of this opinion. The Department is awarded costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which found in favor of respondent Director of Department of Social Services on appellant's claims that respondent's regulation limiting reimbursement for emergency shelter costs was invalid, and found that appellant had failed to exhaust administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: After an audit, respondent Director of Department of Social Services of the Health and Welfare Agency denied appellant county reimbursement for operating funds for the county's center providing emergency care for children threatened with harm or abuse. Appellant sought a writ of mandate as well as declaratory and injunctive relief, alleging that the regulation limiting such reimbursement was invalid. The trial court held that the regulation was valid and that appellant had not exhausted its administrative remedies. The reviewing court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the regulation was valid because the funds at issue originate with the state and federal governments and were intended to fund temporary emergency care only, not care of unlimited duration. The regulation did not conflict with Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 10101 or 1991 Cal. Stat. ch. 91, § 15, providing that the state's share for child welfare programs shall be 25 or 30% respectively. The court also held that issues of reimbursement could not be decided as they were questions of fact as well as law, and appellant had not exhausted its administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the regulation was valid because the funds at issue originate with the state and federal governments and are intended to fund temporary emergency care only, not care of unlimited duration. Appellant's constitutional challenge failed, because it failed to pursue required procedures to challenge the regulation as mandating a new program or higher level of service.

 

755 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Douglas


No. E014602.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


39 Cal. App. 4th 1385; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 534; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1089; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8648; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14869



November 7, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III, IV, V, VI.A, VI.B, VI.C and VI.E.2.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied January 30, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 741.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Riverside County, No. CR-52772, Norman M. Turner, Judge * 


* Retired judge of the Municipal Court for the Western Riverside Judicial District sitting under assignment by the Chairperson of the Judicial Council.



DISPOSITION: The judgment as to prison terms is modified by staying the three-year kidnapping enhancements to counts 3 and 4, said stay to become permanent upon defendant's service of the remainder of his sentence. The judgment as to direct victim restitution is reversed and remanded with directions to the trial court to determine the appropriate amount of direct victim restitution. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Riverside County (California), which convicted and sentenced him for the offenses of kidnapping for robbery, robbery, forcible oral copulation, and rape, and enhanced the sentences based on kidnapping for purposes of forcible oral copulation and rape.


OVERVIEW: Appellant defendant demanded and took money and valuables from complainant. He then made complainant drive to a place where he forced her to commit oral copulation, and was raping her when apprehended by the police. Defendant was charged with kidnapping to commit robbery, robbery, forcible oral copulation, and forcible rape. Based on a jury verdict, the trial court convicted and sentenced defendant, enhanced the sentence on each of the sexual offenses for kidnapping, and imposed a restitution fine and direct restitution in an amount to be determined by the probation officer. Defendant sought review. The court modified in part, reversed and remanded in part, and affirmed in part. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 654 prohibited multiple punishments of defendant for the single kidnapping offense. The court found that the trial court was required to determine the amount of direct victim restitution. The court held that defendant had waived any error in the imposition of the restitution fine by failing to object, but that the imposition of the fine was proper because it could be based on the wages defendant would earn in prison.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing appellant defendant for kidnapping for robbery, robbery, forcible oral copulation, and rape, by staying kidnapping enhancements to the sentences for the sexual offenses, because defendant could only be punished once for the kidnapping. The court reversed and remanded the judgment on direct victim restitution, and otherwise affirmed the judgment.

 

756 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Suman v. Superior Court


No. B094591.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


39 Cal. App. 4th 1309; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 507; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1076; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8549; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14734



November 2, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. NWC51549, John H. Major, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ is discharged. Let a peremptory writ issue directing the trial court to reinstate its order of June 6, 1995, and to conduct further proceedings not inconsistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner automobile owner sought a writ of mandate to prevent respondent, Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), from revoking its previous order to eliminate, in retrial of lemon law action against automobile manufacturer, all references to the first jury's determination on the issue of civil penalties.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner automobile owner brought action against automobile manufacturer under the Song-Beverly Consumer Warranty Act, Cal. Civ. Code § 1790 et seq. The court remanded to the trial court for further trial on the sole issue of civil penalties because the trial court gave erroneous jury instructions. Petitioner filed for a writ of mandate to prevent the trial court from revoking its previous order to eliminate all references to the first jury's determination on the issue of civil penalties in the retrial. The court held that the jury in the partial retrial could not be informed of the former jury's decision with regard to civil penalties under Cal. Civ. Code § 1794(c), which required a finding of willful failure to comply, because the special verdict form used by the first jury did not indicate the reason it declined to award civil penalties and petitioner was seeking penalties in partial retrial under Cal. Civ. Code § 1794(e), which did not require a finding of willfulness. The court held that the civil penalty provisions in Cal. Civ. Code § 1794(e) were not impermissibly vague as to the standards to be used by a jury considering whether to impose such sanctions.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ directing the trial court to reinstate its order eliminating all references to the first jury's determination on the issue of civil penalties in the partial retrial of petitioner automobile owner's lemon law action against automobile manufacturer.

 

757 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Brooks v. Binderup


No. C020328.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


39 Cal. App. 4th 1287; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 501; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1070; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8511; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14661



November 1, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Yuba County, No. 55667, Raymond Roberts, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed. Plaintiffs shall receive costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the director and the deputy director of a county planning and building department, sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Yuba County (California), granting defendant grand jury members' motion for judgment on the pleadings in an action for defamation in grand jury reports. The superior court granted defendants' motion on the ground that Cal. Penal Code § 930 denied them due process.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, the director and the deputy director of a county planning and building department, brought suit against defendant grand jury members, claiming that they were defamed in grand jury reports. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that granted defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings. The court found that Cal. Penal Code § 930 did not deny defendants substantive or procedural due process, and that plaintiffs' cause of action was sufficient to survive defendants' motion. Pursuant to Cal. Penal Code §914.1, a superior court judge was required to inform defendants that their comments in grand jury reports pertaining to unindicted individuals were not privileged. Having been so informed, there was no violation of substantive due process. There were no procedural due process violations because nothing in § 930 specifically denied defendants the right to defend against allegations of defamation. Although defendants may not have disclosed evidence brought before the grand jury or the content of grand jury deliberations, there were other sources of evidence to prove the truth of defendants' comments and defend against allegations of malice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court granting defendant grand jury members' motion for judgment on the pleadings, finding that the cause of action of plaintiffs, the director and the deputy director of a county planning and building department, was sufficient to survive the motion. Defendants' substantive and procedural due process rights would not have been violated by requiring them to defend a defamation action.

 

758 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



U.D. Registry, Inc. v. Superior Court


No. B092597.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


39 Cal. App. 4th 1241; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 363; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1064; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8491; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14601



October 31, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 31, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 769.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BS032430, Madge S. Watai, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner tenant screening service filed a petition for a writ of mandate seeking reinstatement of a previously revoked blanket exemption from the time restrictions imposed by Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1161.2. The blanket exemption had been revoked as conflicting with Cal. Civ. Code § 1785.13(a). Section 1785.13(a) was later found unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The real party in interest, a municipal court, conferred upon petitioner tenant screening service, a blanket oral exemption from Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1161.2(a). Thereafter, petitioner had immediate access to all of the municipal court's unlawful detainer files. The municipal court later revoked the blanket exemption as having been in conflict with Cal. Civ. Code § 1785.13(a). Petitioner filed a petition for a writ of mandate asking the court to order respondent superior court to issue a writ directing the municipal court to reinstate the blanket exemption. The court denied the petition. The court rejected petitioner's contention that there had never been a challenge to the blanket exemption. The blanket exemption was unpublished, unwritten, and telephonically granted, and petitioner failed to explain how anyone could have known about it or challenged it. The court found that the unconstitutionality of § 1785.13(a)(3) had nothing to do with petitioner's case where the only issue was whether petitioner had a vested and irrevocable right to an oral exemption granted in a non-adversarial context.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner tenant screening service's petition for a writ of mandate. The blanket exemption that petitioner sought to have reinstated was an oral exemption granted in a non-adversarial context. The decision striking down a statute as unconstitutional, upon which the blanket exemption had been revoked, was irrelevant because it did not address the constitutionality of the statute upon which the exemption had been issued.

 

759 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Cartwright


No. C019075.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


39 Cal. App. 4th 1123; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 351; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1054; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8463; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14554



October 30, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of parts III., V. and VII.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review Denied February 15, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 94F02668, Thomas M. Cecil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which convicted him of 19 felonies with numerous weapons enhancements. Defendant was sentenced under the "three strikes" law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b), to an indeterminate term of 375 years to life plus a determinate term of 53 years in prison. Defendant challenged the constitutionality and the application of the "three strikes" law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of 19 felony charges with numerous weapons enhancements and was sentenced under the "three strikes" law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b), to an indeterminate term of 375 years to life plus a determinate term of 53 years in prison. Defendant also had a 30-year criminal history, including convictions for voluntary manslaughter, rape, burglary, and assault with a deadly weapon. The court held that the "three strikes" law was valid urgency legislation because the change in duties of judges and prosecutors was neither new and special nor entirely foreign to their existing duties. The court held that the law did not violate the Cal. Const. art. I, § 17 prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment. The court held that the lower court had the discretion to impose consecutive sentences, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667(b). The court held that, pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 667(e)(2)(A), the alternatives for minimum sentences were calculated separately as to each count. The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of the lower court, which convicted defendant of 19 felonies and sentenced him under the "three strikes" law. The court held that the law was valid urgency legislation and did not violate the constitutional prohibition against "cruel and unusual punishment." The court held that the lower court had the discretion to impose consecutive sentences and to calculate each count separately.

 

760 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



California Gillnetters Assn. v. Department of Fish & Game


No. D021547.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FOURTH APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION ONE


39 Cal. App. 4th 1145; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 338; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1055; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8467; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14548



October 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 24, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 526.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Diego County, No. 662758, Arthur W. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant fishermen challenged a summary judgment from the Superior Court of San Diego County (California) in favor of respondent Department of Fish and Game and intervenors on appellants' challenge to Cal. Const. art. X B, passed as Proposition 132, which banned certain fishing gear along portions of the California coastline. Appellants claimed art. X B deprived them of equal protection and of liberty and property without due process.


OVERVIEW: California voters had recently passed Proposition 132, enacted as Cal. Const. art. X B that banned certain commercial fishing gear along portions of the California coastline. Appellants fishermen challenged art. X B as depriving them of equal protection and depriving them of liberty and property without due process and also claimed that deficient ballot materials were provided. Respondent Department of Fish and Game and intervenors were granted a summary judgment in the trial court, and appellants sought review. The court affirmed summary judgment and finding no fundamental rights at issue, applied the rational basis test and found that the article's classification scheme bore a rational relationship to legitimate state purposes. The court also found a rational basis for the gillnetting ban as a legitimate state interest in regulating business. The court dismissed appellants' challenge under U.S. Const. art. IV, § 4 as a political question for enforcement by the congress. Finally, the court concluded that respondents had provided adequate information on financial impact and existing laws in Proposition 132 ballot materials to reject appellants' claim of deficiency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment for respondent Department of Fish and Game and intervenors and against appellant fishermen who had challenged article X B of the California Constitution that prohibited certain commercial fishing gear. The court found no fundamental rights at issue, used the rational basis test, and found no equal protection or due process violations. The court found the improper ballot materials charge without merit.

 

761 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



International Federation of Prof. & Technical Engineers v. Bunch


No. A068195.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


40 Cal. App. 4th 670; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 813; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1156; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8973; 151 L.R.R.M. 2536; 95 Daily Journal DAR 15668



October 30, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published November 28, 1995. Review Denied January 24, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 514.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 956610, Stuart R. Pollak, Judge.



DISPOSITION: We hold that PERB has exclusive initial jurisdiction to determine this matter, particularly whether the new charter collective bargaining procedures can be applied to the District employees without running afoul of any interests deemed paramount under the EERA. Consequently, the judgment is reversed and remanded with directions to dismiss the action for failure of Local 21 to exhaust its administrative remedies before PERB prior to bringing this action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant labor union sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California), which denied appellant's writ of mandate that sought enforcement of an arbitration award for a wage increase of respondent school district's employees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant labor union received an arbitration award that granted a wage increase for civil service employees. Appellant requested a writ of mandate to the trial court seeking enforcement of the arbitration award. Although the trial court found that the Public Employment Relations Boards (PERB) had jurisdiction of resolving the dispute, the trial court denied appellant's request for a writ of mandate. Appellant sought review, and claimed that notwithstanding the passage of San Francisco (Cal.) Charter, § 8409 et seq., Proposition B, respondent retained its rights of negotiating wages and benefits of civil service employees who worked for respondent school district pursuant to Educational Employment Relations Act (EERA), Cal. Gov't Code § 3540 et seq. The court held that the PERB had exclusive jurisdiction in resolving the matter of the wage dispute of civil service employees because the dispute involved conduct that was protected or prohibited by the EERA. The court reversed the trial court's judgment. The court remanded with directions for dismissing the action because appellant had not exhausted its administrative remedies before the PERB prior to bringing this action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment because the trial court did not have jurisdiction to deny appellant labor union's writ of mandate that sought enforcement of an arbitration award for a wage increase of respondent school district's employees.

 

762 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Andrus v. Estrada


No. A064827.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


39 Cal. App. 4th 1030; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 300; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1030; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8336; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14385



October 25, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 14, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1228. Review Denied January 18, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 375.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Alameda County, No. H163955-9, Mark L. Eaton, Judge.

Original Opinion of July 31, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 720. Rehearing Previously Granted August 29, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 861.



DISPOSITION: The order imposing sanctions is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, plaintiffs' original law firm, challenged on its own behalf an order of sanctions issued by the Superior Court of Alameda County (California) under Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 128.5 for filing a frivolous 13-count lawsuit arising out of respondent landlord's attorney's filing of an unlawful detainer action against appellants' former clients as renters. The trial court ordered $ 4,000 in sanctions payable by both appellants and plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Respondent, landlord's attorney, filed an unlawful detainer action against plaintiff renters for one month's unpaid rent and withdrew the action shortly after payment was made. Appellants, plaintiffs' original law firm, then filed a 13-count complaint against respondent that set off a series of cross filings and motions that resulted in a grant of summary judgment for respondent. After appellants withdrew for conflicts of interest the court ordered a $ 4,000 award of sanctions for respondent and against appellants and plaintiffs. Appellants, without plaintiffs, challenged the sanctions but the court affirmed the award and found that appellants' consistent conduct during the lawsuit supported a sanctions order, especially the filing of a conspiracy action against respondent in his role as an attorney and contrary to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1714.10. In addition, appellants' initially had filed in the wrong division, failed to stipulate to a well-founded change of venue motion, failed to approve the proposed order granting venue change, and advocated unfounded and untenable legal positions throughout the proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a sanctions order of $ 4,000 against appellants, plaintiffs' original law firm and plaintiffs renters for filing a frivolous lawsuit against respondent, landlord's attorney. The court found ample evidence in the 11 reasons given by the trial court to support an award of sanctions including the filing of a conspiracy action against respondent in his role as an attorney and contrary to Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 1714.10.

 

763 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Neecke v. City of Mill Valley


No. A065966.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


39 Cal. App. 4th 946; 46 Cal. Rptr. 2d 266; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1043; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 8339; 95 Daily Journal DAR 14345



October 25, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 4, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 147.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Marin County, No. 147334, Gary W. Thomas, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed in part and affirmed in part. The portions of the judgment awarding Neecke (1) a refund of taxes paid pursuant to Ordinance No. 1086 and interest thereon and (2) attorney fees pursuant to Code of Civil Procedure section 1021.5 are reversed. On remand, the trial court is ordered to reconsider whether Neecke should be awarded attorney fees in light of this decision and, if so, in what amount. In all other respects, the judgment is affirmed and costs on appeal are awarded to defendants and appellants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Marin County (California), which awarded plaintiff property owner a refund of municipal service taxes that he had paid to defendant and which awarded plaintiff attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff property owner asserted that the municipal services tax imposed by defendant city violated Cal. Const. art. XIIIA, § 4. The trial court ruled in favor of plaintiff. On appeal, defendant argued that the municipal services tax was not a special tax. The court agreed, finding that the municipal services tax was not unconstitutional because defendant was a general purpose entity and because the ordinance at issue specifically stated that the tax proceeds were to be placed in defendant's general fund and used for general municipal purposes. The court ruled that special tax funds were those levied by a limited purpose agency, dedicated to a special purpose, or deposited in the fund of a special purpose agency. The court also ruled that the trial court did not err in denying plaintiff's motion for class certification because plaintiff's action was brought under Cal. Rev. & Tax Code § 5097, which did not provide for class claims. Thus, the court reversed that part of the judgment that ordered defendant to refund the taxes plaintiff had paid and reversed an attorney fees award to plaintiff. The court affirmed that part of the judgment that declined to certify the class.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court that found in favor of plaintiff property owner and that awarded him a refund of taxes and that awarded him attorney fees, holding that the municipal services tax was not unconstitutional because the tax was levied by a general purpose entity and the proceeds were deposited into its general purpose fund. The court affirmed the trial court's decision in all other respects.

 

764 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Campos


No. B086077.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN.


47 Cal. App. 4th 1366; 45 Cal. Rptr. 2d 706; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 971; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7863; 95 Daily Journal DAR 13402



October 4, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted December 21, 1995 (S049828), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 7698.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 38 Cal. App. 4th 1669 and 43 Cal. App. 4th 189.)]


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. VA020773, Philip H. Hickok, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The sentence is ordered vacated and the judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state disputed a decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which, in the interest of justice, dismissed three "priors." The state argued that there was no such authority under Cal. Penal Code §§ 667(d), 1385. Defendant's cross-appeal argued that the statutes violated the separation of powers, a felony was not a qualifying "prior" if it were not charged and brought separately, and his sentence was cruel and unusual.


OVERVIEW: As part of a plea bargain, the trial court dismissed three prior felony convictions for purposes of the "three strikes" law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(i). Defendant pleaded guilty and the trial court sentenced him to 25 years to life. The state challenged the dismissal of the "priors." The court held that the trial court had no authority, under Cal. Penal Code §§ 667(d) and 1385, to dismiss a qualifying "prior" on its own motion in the interest of justice. Because the statutes called for both the prosecutor and the trial judge to exercise their discretion in the matter, there was no violation of the separation of powers doctrine. There was nothing in § 667(d) that required that, for defendant's three prior convictions to be considered as qualifying prior felony convictions, they had to have been brought and tried separately. Defendant had not satisfied his burdens under a three-part test established by a case, so his sentence was not cruel and unusual. The court reversed because defendant's guilty plea was based upon the dismissal of the "priors." The court vacated the sentence and directed the trial court to allow him to withdraw his guilty plea and prior allegation admission.


OUTCOME: The court reversed. There was no authority to dismiss the "priors." Both the prosecutor and the trial judge had to exercise statutory discretion, so the separation of powers was not violated. Prior convictions could be treated as separate. Defendant had not met his burdens to show cruel and unusual punishment. The court vacated defendant's sentence and directed the trial court to allow him to withdraw a guilty plea and prior allegation admission.

 

765 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



People v. Whitham


No. F020739.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIFTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


38 Cal. App. 4th 1282; 45 Cal. Rptr. 2d 571; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 968; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7788; 95 Daily Journal DAR 13307



September 29, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] Opinion certified for partial publication. * 


* Pursuant to California Rules of Court, rules 976(b) and 976.1, this opinion is certified for publication with the exception of the Statement of Facts and part I of the Discussion.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified on Denial of Rehearing October 30, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1057. 0Review Denied January 4, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 173.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Kings County, No. 122455, Peter M. Schultz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Kings County (California) convicting her of murder by the administration of poison in violation of Cal. Penal Code §§ 187(a), 190.2(a)(19), of holding victims in involuntary servitude in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 181, and of continuous sexual abuse of a child in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 288.5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder by poisoning, Cal. Penal Code §§ 187(a), 190.2(a)(19), holding victims in involuntary servitude, Cal. Penal Code § 181, and continuous sexual abuse of a child, Cal. Penal Code § 288.5. On appeal, defendant contended that § 288.5 required proof of a specific intent, namely that the acts were committed for sexual gratification. Defendant also claimed that § 288.5 was unconstitutional because, although it required a finding of three specific acts of sexual abuse, it did not require that the jurors unanimously agree on the same three acts. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that a review of the legislative history of § 288.5 made it clear that the legislature intended to proscribe sexual conduct that was done for the purpose of, for instance, punishment or abuse instead of sexual gratification. The court held that § 288.5 was constitutional because it criminalized a continuous course of conduct, not a specific act. As long as there was unanimity as to the continuous course of conduct, the fact that jurors did not agree on which specific acts constituted the course of conduct did not render the section unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder, holding victims in involuntary servitude, and continuous sexual abuse of a child. The statute that criminalized continuous sexual abuse of a child did not require proof of a specific intent that the acts were committed for sexual gratification. The statute was constitutional because, although it did not require unanimity for the specific acts, it did require unanimity that the abuse occurred.

 

766 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Superior Court (Missamore)


No. A067465.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


47 Cal. App. 4th 1292; 45 Cal. Rptr. 2d 392; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 942; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7643; 95 Daily Journal DAR 13130C



September 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted December 21, 1995 (S044037), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 7697.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 38 Cal. App. 4th 1358 and 43 Cal. app. 4th 115.)]
Transferred September 23, 1998 to the Ct. App., 1st Dist. Div. 2 to vacate its previous judgment and review dismissed as moot, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 6218.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sonoma County, No. 21735, Lawrence G. Antolini, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The petition for a writ of mandate is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought a writ of mandamus to the decision of the Superior Court of Sonoma County (California) which imposed a probationary sentence on respondent. Petitioner contended the Three Strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(b)-(i), precluded the trial court from placing defendant on probation when he had already been convicted of a prior violent or serious felony.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was convicted of possessing marijuana in a county jail, which represented his fourth felony conviction. His other three included one for burglary and two for receiving stolen property. Additionally, respondent had a criminal history of minor offenses. The trial court imposed a sentence of probation finding that the sentence urged by petitioner state, would shock the conscience and affect the fundamental notions of human dignity, thereby violating the prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment prohibited by U.S. Const. amend. VIII, and Cal. Const. art. I, § VI. Petitioner filed a writ of mandate to the trial court sentence, which the court granted. The court held that the Three Strikes law, Cal. Penal Code § 667(c)(2) clearly provided that once convicted, felons--assuming their prior felonies met the definitions provided in subdivision (d)--were not upon a subsequent felony conviction, eligible for probation. Cal. Penal Code § 667(f)(2) implicitly limited the trial court's power to dismiss prior convictions, in furtherance of justice to only those occasions when the prosecutor so moved. The court held the trial judge was thus without authority to impose probation.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner state's request for writ of mandamus to the trial court's imposition of a probationary sentence on defendant. The court held that the Three Strikes law precluded the judge from granting probation to a once-convicted felon, notwithstanding any other provision or law.

Las Tunas Beach Geologic Hazard Abatement Dist. v. Superior Court


No. B090779.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


38 Cal. App. 4th 1002; 45 Cal. Rptr. 2d 529; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 939; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7658; 95 Daily Journal DAR 13045



September 28, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 14, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 7527.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. SC029408, Hugh C. Gardner III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The alternative writ having served its purpose is discharged. Let a peremptory writ of mandate issue, directing the respondent court to vacate its order denying the District's motion for summary judgment and to enter a summary judgment declaring the District to be a validly formed political subdivision of the state, and enjoining the City from taking any action to dissolve the District except in compliance with Cortese-Knox. ( Gov. Code, § 56000 et seq., 56100.)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner district sought a writ of mandate directing respondent trial court (California) to vacate its order denying petitioner's motion for summary judgment and to enter instead an order granting the motion.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner district was created as a geologic hazard abatement district (GHAD) after the city adopted a formation resolution pursuant to Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 26500 et seq. The city later attempted to dissolve petitioner under a condition in the formation resolution permitting the city to dissolve petitioner in certain circumstances. Petitioner filed a declaratory relief action seeking a determination that the city lacked authority to order the dissolution and a permanent injunction enjoining the city from attempting to exercise any authority over petitioner. Respondent trial court denied petitioner's motion for summary judgment. The court held that the city could not unilaterally dissolve petitioner by way of a council resolution as the Cortese-Knox Local Government Reorganization Act, Cal. Gov't Code § 56000 et seq. (1985), prescribed the exclusive procedure for dissolution of a GHAD. The court held that the condition reserving to the city the right to order dissolution of petitioner was unenforceable and petitioner was entitled to declaratory and injunctive relief to that effect; however, the city was not foreclosed from later seeking a dissolution pursuant to section 56000.


OUTCOME: The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate and directed respondent trial court to vacate its order denying petitioner district's motion for summary judgment, holding that the city could not unilaterally dissolve petitioner by way of a council resolution as the Cortese-Knox Local Government Reorganization Act prescribed the exclusive procedure for dissolution of a geologic hazard abatement district.

 

768 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Allstate Ins. Co. v. Gonzalez


No. B078387.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


38 Cal. App. 4th 783; 45 Cal. Rptr. 2d 491; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 929; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7533; 95 Daily Journal DAR 12889



September 26, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied January 18, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Cal. LEXIS 387.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. YC010591, William C. Beverly, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment denying Allstate's prayer for declaratory relief is reversed with directions to enter a declaratory judgment in favor of Allstate to the effect that Gonzalez waived arbitration of his uninsured motorist claim by his unreasonable delay in filing the demand, so as to bar the claim.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurance company sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which denied its prayer for declaratory relief from a demand for arbitration of an automobile liability insurance policy claim filed against it by defendant, operator of an insured's automobile that was involved in an accident.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was operating insured's vehicle insured by plaintiff insurance company when they were involved in a car accident with an uninsured motorist. Defendant, who filed a civil action against uninsured motorist, informed plaintiff by letter that there were uninsured motorist claims arising out of the accident. Plaintiff advised defendant to file a demand for arbitration. Defendant failed to file a demand for arbitration for almost five years. Plaintiff then filed a prayer for declaratory relief that was denied by the court below. On appeal, the court found defendant's uninsured motorist claim was not barred by the four-year statute of limitations provided for in Cal. Civ. Proc. Code § 337 because the limitations period did not begin to run until plaintiff refused to arbitrate. However, because the record established unreasonable delay be defendant in filing a demand for arbitration, defendant was deemed to have waived his right to arbitration of his uninsured motorist claim. Therefore, the lower court's judgment was reversed with directions to enter a declaratory judgment in favor of plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court below, which denied plaintiff insurance company's prayer for declaratory relief from a demand for arbitration of an automobile liability insurance policy claim filed against it by defendant, operator of insured's automobile at the time of an accident, was reversed because the record established unreasonable delay in the filing of the demand for arbitration.

 

769 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



Planning & Conservation League, Inc. v. Lungren


No. C016761.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


38 Cal. App. 4th 497; 45 Cal. Rptr. 2d 183; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 918; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7477; 95 Daily Journal DAR 12761



September 22, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. CV373836, James Timothy Ford, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed. Plaintiffs are to recover their costs on appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant government official appealed an order of the Sacramento County Superior Court (California), which compelled him to prepare the title and summary for an initiative submitted by plaintiff environmental groups even though the initiative did not comply with Cal. Elec. Code § 9002.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff environmental groups submitted an initiative to defendant government official. Defendant refused to prepare the title and summary for the initiative because plaintiffs did not comply with Cal. Elec. Code § 9002, which required them to submit an affidavit that no monetary contributions were made to aid in the qualification of the initiative as a quid pro quo for inclusion of appropriations for other projects. The trial court found the statute infringed plaintiffs' U.S. Const. amend. I rights, and compelled defendant to prepare the title and summary. Defendant appealed. The court held that the statute impacted political speech as contributions to support a ballot constituted political expression. As the statute had more than an incidental impact on political speech, which was protected under U.S. Const. amend. I, it was subject to strict scrutiny review. The court determined that the statute was not narrowly tailored to achieve the compelling, legitimate goal of preventing corruption in the electoral process. The statute was therefore unconstitutional, and the court affirmed the trial court's order.


OUTCOME: Order compelling defendant government official to prepare the title and summary for plaintiff environmental groups' initiative was affirmed despite plaintiffs' failure to comply with a statute requiring an affidavit regarding contributions because the statute was unconstitutional; the statute had more than an incidental impact on political speech, and was not narrowly tailored to achieve the goal of preventing corruption.

 

770 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



San Mateo County Coastal Landowners' Assn. v. County of San Mateo


No. A059553.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION TWO


38 Cal. App. 4th 523; 45 Cal. Rptr. 2d 117; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 898; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7369; 95 Daily Journal DAR 12558



September 18, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied December 21, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 7702.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of San Mateo County, Nos. 316851 and 329349, Walter H. Harrington, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nonprofit organizations and landowners sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of San Mateo County (California), which denied their petition for a writ of mandate to command respondent county to cease enforcing "Measure A", a local voter initiative that amended the San Mateo County Local Coastal Program.


OVERVIEW: The voters of respondent county enacted Measure A, which amended respondent county's local coastal program (LCP). Measure A permitted respondent county to submit future amendment proposals to the voters. Appellant nonprofit organizations and appellant coastal landowners filed a petition for mandamus to stop respondent county from enforcing Measure A. Appellants filed a second action against respondent California Coastal Commission. The trial court consolidated the two actions. The trial court entered a judgment that denied appellants' petition for mandamus and refused to grant declaratory relief that found Measure A unconstitutional. On appeal, the court thought that the majority of appellants' challenges on appeal were directed towards their concern that Measure A dealt with a matter of statewide concern and was inconsistent with the Coastal Act of 1976 (Coastal Act), Cal. Pub. Res. Code § 30000 et seq. The court concluded that the local right of initiative was not barred by the fact that the Coastal Act dealt with coastal land use on a statewide basis. Additionally, the court found that Measure A complied with the Coastal Act. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that denied the petition for a writ of mandamus brought by appellant nonprofit organizations and appellant landowners because the court concluded that respondent county's amendment to the local coastal program was permitted despite the fact that coastal land use was a statewide issue.

 

771 of 1449 DOCUMENTS



In re Keisha T.


No. C019041.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


38 Cal. App. 4th 220; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 822; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 871; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7129; 95 Daily Journal DAR 12123; 24 Media L. Rep. 1193



September 7, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified October 10, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, Nos. JD202028, 202882, 203793, 203934, 203972, 204000, 204086, 204087, 204148, and 204172, Talmadge R. Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment (the June 1993 order and the June 1994 order) is reversed and the cause is remanded to the juvenile court for further proceedings in accordance with this opinion. The stay issued by this court on October 13, 1994, shall remain in effect until this opinion is final. The parties shall bear their own costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minors sought review of the order of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which conditionally granted respondent newspaper's petition to inspect court records in juvenile dependency cases pursuant to Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 827(a). Appellants challenged the decision to release information and the procedure established by the juvenile court.


OVERVIEW: Respondent newspaper petitioned the juvenile court for permission to inspect and copy court records of 10 minors. The juvenile court conditionally granted the petition and established a procedure under which a temporary judge would release information. Appellant minors challenged the juvenile court's decision and the procedure established. The court reversed and remanded and held that the juvenile court's procedure for implementing the order was inadequate to effect the proper balancing that must occur and to protect the interests of minors and others. An in camera proceeding was necessary to review the juvenile court record and determined what, if any material should be disclosed to respondent. The court noted that the juvenile court had exclusive authority to determine whether disclosure of juvenile records to persons not specifically named in Cal. Welf. & Inst. § 827, was in the best interests of the minor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order which had conditionally granted respondent newspaper's petition to inspect court records in juvenile dependency cases. The court held that the juvenile court's procedure for implementing the order was inadequate to effect the proper balancing that must occur and to protect the interests of minors and others.

 

772 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Loomis


No. B086628.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


47 Cal. App. 4th 46; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 775; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 864; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7057; 95 Daily Journal DAR 12036



September 5, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted November 16, 1995 (S049374), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 6958.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Superior Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 37 Cal. App. 4th 1781 and 42 Cal. App. 4th 404.)] Opinion filed March 19, 1998 not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. VA021003, John A. Torribio, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is reversed. The matter is remanded to the trial court to permit Loomis to withdraw his plea if he so desires. If Loomis elects to not withdraw his plea, the trial court shall sentence him in accordance with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The people appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant of one count of petty theft with a prior. The people contended the trial court erred when, on its own motion, it struck defendant's prior burglary conviction and determined the prior conviction could not be used both to elevate defendant's petty theft to a felony and for purposes of the three strikes law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stole a calculator worth $ 36.97. He pleaded guilty to petty theft and admitted to two prior felonies. The trial court, on its own motion, struck one of the prior convictions and held that the same prior felony could not be used both to elevate petty theft to a felony and for purposes of the three strikes law. Defendant was sentenced to seven years in lieu of to life as would be required under the three strikes law. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded to permit defendant to withdraw his plea. The court held that it was the intent of the legislature to restrict a court's power to strike prior convictions under the three strikes law. The court held that Cal. Penal Code § 667(f)(2), in granting a prosecutor the right to strike a prior conviction, did not violate the separation of powers doctrine where it did not take any pre-existing power away from the trial court. The court held that where the legislature stated the three strikes law applied in addition to enhancement provisions, the trial court was not barred from using the same prior conviction to elevate petty theft to a felony and for purposes of the three strikes law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of defendant for petty theft and remanded to permit defendant to withdraw his guilty plea. The court held that in light of legislative intent to restrict the power of the court to strike priors in three strikes cases the trial court erred in striking defendant's prior burglary conviction and in disallowing it to be used both to elevate petty theft to a felony and for the three strikes law.

 

773 of 1449 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cartwright


No. C019075.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, THIRD APPELLATE DISTRICT


38 Cal. App. 4th 194; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 755; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 857; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6963; 95 Daily Journal DAR 11870



August 31, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REHEARING


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Opinion of October 30, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 1054. (See 39 Cal. App. 4th 1123)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Sacramento County, No. 94F02668, Thomas M. Cecil, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Sacramento County (California), which convicted him on 19 felony counts and enhanced his sentence under the three strikes law, 1994 Cal. Stat. 12, § 1-2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction on 19 felony counts and challenged the constitutionality and application of the three strikes law that enhanced his sentence. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. It found that an information had been filed when the magistrate deemed the amended complaint as an information and accepted the document on file as an information, and the nunc pro tunc notation was proper to cure a clerical error in failing to file-stamp the document. It held that the three strikes law, 1994 Cal. Stat. 12, § 1-2, was valid urgency legislation because the primary duties of the trial judge and prosecutor were not changed since their discretion in sentencing or prosecuting defendants had never been absolute. The court held that defendant's sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment because it was not grossly disproportionate to his more serious crimes and his prior crimes were numerous and violent. The court also held that using the same prior conviction as both a strike and as enhancement was not double punishment because the prior conviction was not an act under Cal. Penal Code § 654, it only established defendant's status as a recidivist.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence imposed under the three strikes law because the information was properly filed and his sentence was not grossly disproportionate to his more serious crimes.

People v. Williams


No. B086805.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


46 Cal. App. 4th 1522; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 743; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 859; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7021; 95 Daily Journal DAR 11951



August 31, 1995, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified September 12, 1995. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing October 3, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 963. Review Granted November 16, 1995 (S049295), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 6957.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Superior Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 37 Cal. App. 4th 1737 and 42 Cal. App. 4th 384.)]
Transferred January 28, 1998 to Ct. App., 2d Dist., Div. 5, with directions to vacate its decision and reconsider in light of People v. Superior Court (Romero) (1996) 13 Cal. 4th 497, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 630.
Opinion filed March 12, 1998 not for publication.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. VA026660, Norman P. Tarle, Temporary Judge. * 


* Pursuant to California Constitution, article VI, section 21.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant offender appealed a conviction from the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sentenced defendant under the three strikes sentencing law. Defendant asserted the trial court erroneously concluded that it lacked authority under Cal. Penal Code § 1385 to dismiss or strike defendant's prior felony convictions on defendant's or its own motion, so as to impose a lesser sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant offender suffered two prior felony convictions within the meaning of Cal. Penal Code § 667 and was found guilty on one count of attempted first degree burglary. Defendant received enhancements under the three strikes sentencing law and asserted that the trial court erred in concluding the new sentencing laws deprived it of authority under Cal. Penal Code § 1385 to dismiss or strike the prior felony convictions on defendant's or its own motion, so as to impose a lesser sentence. The court affirmed, concluding the trial court correctly determined that it had no authority to strike the prior felony convictions once true findings as to those allegations had been made. The court held that the issue concerned the interplay of two provisions of the Cal. Penal Code: § 1385, authorizing a trial court to dismiss an action in furtherance of justice, and § 667, prescribing longer sentences for persons convicted of certain felonies who have previously been convicted of specified criminal offenses. Once the prior conviction allegations had been pled and proved, the trial court was without authority to suspend execution of sentence on those convictions by way of dismissing them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment holding that the trial court properly determined that it lacked authority to suspend execution or imposition of sentencing of defendant offender's prior convictions by way of striking or dismissing them once they had been pled and proved.

People v. Gore


No. B089331.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN.


46 Cal. App. 4th 1396; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 244; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 788; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6463; 95 Daily Journal DAR 11008



August 15, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted November 22, 1995 (S048866), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 7091.
[Reprinted without Change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 37 Cal. App. 4th 1009 and 42 Cal. App. 4th 1.)]


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. GA020704, Dino J. Fulgoni, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, Los Angeles County (California), which dismissed one serious-violent felony conviction allegation against defendant, who then pled guilty to the remaining serious-violent felony conviction allegations against him.


OVERVIEW: The lower court dismissed one serious-violent felony conviction allegation against defendant. Defendant then pled guilty to the other two serious-violent felony conviction allegations against him. The state argued that the lower court erred in dismissing the serious-violent felony conviction allegation. The court held that where the lower court indicated that it would drop one felony prior of defendant's in exchange for a guilty plea, it engaged in prohibited plea bargaining under Cal. Penal Code § 667(g), which provided that prior felony convictions could not be used in plea bargaining. Furthermore, the court held that in granting defendant's motion to dismiss the subject felony prior, the lower court acted outside the authority of Cal. Penal Code § 1385, which only permitted an action to be dismissed on motion by a prosecutor or court. The court also held that the lower court's order dismissing defendant's prior felony was defective because no reasons for the dismissal were stated as required by section 1385. As such, the court reversed the order dismissing the serious-violent felony conviction allegation against defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order dismissing one serious-violent felony conviction allegation against defendant, holding that the lower court engaged in prohibited plea bargaining where it indicated that it would drop one felony prior in exchange for a guilty plea; furthermore, the lower court erred in granting defendant's motion to dismiss the prior felony because an action could only be dismissed on motion by a prosecutor or court.

People v. Regules


No. H013532.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SIXTH APPELLATE DISTRICT


47 Cal. App. 4th 152; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 688; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 880; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 7178; 95 Daily Journal DAR 12210



August 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published September 8, 1995. Review Granted November 16, 1995 (S048880), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 6953.
[Reprinted without change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cite 38 Cal. App. 4th 100 and 42 Cal.App.4th 1291.)].
Review Dismissed April 24, 1997 in light of intervening amends. to Pen. Code., § 803, subd. (g); Stats. 1996, ch. 130, § 1. Cause remanded to Ct. App. 6th Dist., Reported at: 1997 Cal. LEXIS 2295. Remittitur issued May 1, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Monterey County, No. MS 941488, Richard M. Silver, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The order denying the People's motion to reinstate the complaint is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the State of California, sought review of a decision from the Superior Court of Monterey County (California), dismissing a criminal complaint for committing various lewd acts dating back to 1952 against minors under Cal. Penal Code § 803(g) (1993) as having been filed after the expiration of the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, the State of California, challenged the trial court's dismissal of its criminal complaint against defendant brought under Cal. Penal Code § 803(g) (1993), which provided a limitations period of one year from the date a person of any age reported that he or she was a victim of a lewd act while under the age of 18. Defendant was charged with various sex acts against minors dating back to the year 1952. The trial court sustained defendant's demurrer. On appeal, the court held that the complaint violated the Ex Post Facto Clauses of the United States and California constitutions. The statute punished as crimes certain acts that defendant previously committed for which the then-applicable statute of limitations had expired. Therefore, the subsequent statutory amendment extending the limitations period was unconstitutional. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of defendant's criminal complaint for committing lewd acts against children as long ago as 1952 because the charging statute, which enlarged the statute of limitations to one year from the date that a victim of any age reported the crime, was an illegal ex post facto law under the federal and state constitutions.

In re Sade C.


No. B082230, No. B084043.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION THREE


46 Cal. App. 4th 614; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 509; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 793; 95 Daily Journal DAR 10884; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6393



August 11, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted October 19, 1995 (S048796), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 6397.
[Reprinted without Change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 37 Cal. App. 4th 88 and 41 Cal. App. 4th 1642.)] (See 13 Cal. 4th 952)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, Nos. LK00851 and CK09428, Larry P. Fidler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The appeal from the judgment terminating the parental rights of Gregory C. is dismissed. The appeal from the order declaring Vanessa R. a dependent child of the juvenile court is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two different cases, appellant parents had their parental rights terminated, under Cal. Welf. & Inst. Code § 366.26, by order of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California). Appellants, in each case, requested that the court independently review the record after presenting no issues or arguments. They argued that such review was due process entitlement.


OVERVIEW: In two cases, appellant parents challenged the termination of their parental rights. In each appeal, counsel for the parents raised no issues and presented no arguments, but requested that the court independently review the record. In a challenge to a judgment in civil cases, it was incumbent upon appellant to have presented argument and authority on each point made. In such cases, appellants' failure to articulate a pertinent and intelligible legal argument might have been deemed an abandonment of the appeal that justified dismissal. A narrow and specific exception to the general rule applied in a direct first appeal as of right in a criminal case. Appellants contended that due process entitled them to a similar exception. However, as it was a noncriminal proceeding, the court evaluated the requirements of federal due process by weighing the private interest at stake, the risk of an erroneous deprivation of such interest through the procedures used, and the probable value, if any, of additional or substitute procedural safeguards, and the government's interest. The court concluded that the balance weighed strongly against independent review. The court dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeals were dismissed where counsel for appellant parents filed briefs that raised no issues, the court was not required to conduct its own independent review of the record. The balance of due process factors weighed strongly against such review.

Lafayette Morehouse, Inc. v. Chronicle Publishing Co.


No. A067522.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FIVE


37 Cal. App. 4th 855; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 46; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 762; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6359; 95 Daily Journal DAR 10818; 23 Media L. Rep. 2389



August 9, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Denied November 30, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 7325.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco, No. 952459, William J. Cahill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of judgment striking cause of action, in publishing company respondents' favor in a Strategic Lawsuit Against Public Participation (SLAPP), Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 425.16, suit in the Superior Court of the City and County of San Francisco (California).


OVERVIEW: Appellants sought review of judgment granting a special motion to strike a Strategic Lawsuit Against Public Participation (SLAPP) suit, under Cal. Code Civ. Proc. § 425.16, in favor of respondent publishing companies. The court affirmed, concluding the lower court properly determined the statutory procedure for disposing of a non-meritorious cause of action that chilled the valid constitutional exercise of free speech applied to corporate publishers sued for libel based on an article made in connection with issues under consideration or review by executive, judicial, or legislative bodies. Respondents published a series of articles related to alternative lifestyle university respondents' failure to comply with county enforcement actions and a resulting civil rights lawsuit. The court explained the statute covered such activity which was an activity consistently characterized by courts as fee speech. The court next found the statute did not unconstitutionally interfere with access to the judicial system because its classifications were rationally based and the jury trial right was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed grant of motion striking appellants' SLAPP suit, in favor of publishing company respondents, because the statute was applicable to corporate media entities who were sued for libel in the exercise of free speech in connection with issues under review by executive, judicial, or legislative branches, and right of judicial access was not unconstitutionally interfered with by such summary procedure.

People v. Petty


No. B087484.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN


51 Cal. App. 4th 203; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 34; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 775; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6337



August 8, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review Granted November 2, 1995 (S048702), Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 6757.
[Reprinted without Change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 37 Cal. App. 4th 730 and 41 Cal. App. 4th 1777 and 46 Cal. App. 4th 723.)]
Transferred March 25, 1998 to Ct. App., 2d Dist., Div. 7, with directions to vacate its decision and reconsider in light of People v. Superior Court (Romero) (1996) 13 Cal. 4th 497, Reported at: 1998 Cal. LEXIS 1827. Order filed April 7, 1998 not for publication; remittitur issued July 8, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. BA095110, Bernard J. Kamins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which convicted defendant of felony hit and run, found a serious felony (robbery) conviction allegation true, and sentenced defendant to the low 16-month term, doubled pursuant statute, totaling 32 months in state prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of felony hit and run under Cal. Veh. Code §20001(a), an offense punishable by imprisonment in state prison or county jail, and the trial court found true the serious felony (robbery) conviction allegation under Cal. Penal Code § 667(b-i). Defendant argued that the trial court mistakenly believed the subject offense was not an alternative misdemeanor-felony and that it had to impose a state prison sentence and that the trial court had the power to dismiss a serious felony allegation on its own motion. The court affirmed defendant's conviction, holding that the record failed to demonstrate that the trial court believed it could not impose a county jail sentence. The court determined that nothing in the trial court's remarks suggested that it wanted to impose a county jail sentence or that it believed it could not do so. The court found that the trial court did not have the power to dismiss defendant's felony charge on its own motion because the suggestion that judges had such power based on Cal. Penal Code § 667(f)(2), which mitigated a restriction on prosecutors, was not intended by the legislature and was an absurd consequence of the provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that the record failed to support appellant's contention that the trial court believed it could not impose a county jail sentence.

People v. Bailey


No. B087285.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, SECOND APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION SEVEN.


46 Cal. App. 4th 743; 44 Cal. Rptr. 2d 205; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 789; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6328



August 8, 1995, Decided


NOTICE: NOT CITABLE - SUPERSEDED BY GRANT OF REVIEW


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified August 21, 1995. Second Modification September 7, 1995. Review Granted November 16, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Cal. LEXIS 6951.
[Reprinted without Change to permit tracking pending disposition on review by the Supreme Court. (See Preface to Cumulative Subsequent History Table. Previous cites 37 Cal. App. 4th 871 and 41 Cal. App. 4th 1797.)]


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Los Angeles County, No. NA020760, Arthur H. Jean, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment is reversed and the case is remanded to the trial court for resentencing consistent with the views expressed herein, or for the defendant to withdraw his plea upon proper motion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution appealed from the alleged imposition of an illegal sentence and the dismissal of the prior offense allegations by the Superior Court of Los Angeles County (California), which sentenced defendant to seven years' imprisonment for second-degree commercial burglary in violation of Cal. Penal Code § 459, computed by doubling the high term, under § 667(e)(1), plus an additional year for the remaining prior allegation under § 667.5.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a retail store with the intent to steal. He left the store without paying for numerous items valued at approximately $ 225. Under the "three strikes" law Cal. Penal Code § 667(e)(1), defendant was charged with second-degree commercial burglary. After striking two of three prior convictions pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 1385, the trial court sentenced defendant as if the current case was a "second strike" case. The prosecution appealed. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the striking of each prior was improper because § 667(f)(2), which allowed the prosecution to strike a prior felony conviction allegation in the furtherance of justice, did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. Moreover, the "fair import" of the language of § 1385(b) precluded the trial court from striking or dismissing prior felony conviction allegations pled under the three strikes law. Furthermore, the record did not provide a basis for the trial court to find that sentencing defendant to 25 years to life would constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's "second strike" sentence for second-degree commercial burglary, holding that the trial court erred in failing to sentence defendant under the "three strikes" law because the prosecution's authority to strike a prior felony conviction allegation in the furtherance of justice did not violate the separation of powers doctrine and there was no basis to find that such a sentence would be cruel and unusual punishment.

Homan v. Gomez


No. A067106.


COURT OF APPEAL OF CALIFORNIA, FIRST APPELLATE DISTRICT, DIVISION FOUR


37 Cal. App. 4th 597; 43 Cal. Rptr. 2d 647; 1995 Cal. App. LEXIS 749; 95 Cal. Daily Op. Service 6236; 95 Daily Journal DAR 10581



August 4, 1995, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought a declaration that a provision of the state Budget Act, which made those convicted of certain sex crimes ineligible for family visitation while in prison, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The California legislature added a rider to the state Budget Act. This provision required prisons to deny family visitation to inmates who had been convicted of committing certain sex crimes. Petitioner inmate was incarcerated in a state prison after having pleaded guilty to 11 sex offenses against children. Several counts were violations of Cal. Penal Code § 288, which was one of the code sections that resulted in disqualification for family visitation. Prior to the passage of the challenged budget provision, petitioner was eligible for family visitation. His visit was cancelled as a consequence of the budget provision. Petitioner asked the court to declare the provision unconstitutional on the ground that it violated the California Constitution's single subject rule. The court rejected respondent Director of the California Department of Corrections' contention that family visitation was merely a privilege, not a right conferred by any statute. The court concluded that the budget rider substantively changed the law and violated the single subject rule of Cal. Const. art. IV, § 9. The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate against the provision's enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the provision of the state Budget Act that made those convicted of certain sex crimes ineligible for family visitation while in prison was unconstitutional because it violated the single subject rule. The court issued a peremptory writ of mandate that restrained respondent Director of the California Department of Corrections from enforcing the provision.
